Pledge for Salam Capital and Sarf Price: Hanafi vs. Zufar
Intra-Hanafi dispute on pledge validity for salam/sarf capital

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school validates a pledge for the capital of salam, the price of sarf, and the muslam fihi, and evaluate Imam Zufar's objection based on substitution.

Core Idea
A pledge is valid for salam capital and sarf price because homogeneity is in monetary value, not the specific item.

In salam and sarf contracts, substitution of the specified capital or price is strictly prohibited. Yet the Hanafi school permits pledging different items as collateral for these very obligations. This seems contradictory at first glance. Imam Zufar raised this exact objection, arguing that a pledge necessarily substitutes the original right. In this lesson, we examine the dispute and the Hanafi response that resolves the apparent conflict by focusing on monetary value rather than physical identity.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling from Quduri: it is valid (sahih) to pledge for the capital of salam, the price of sarf, and the muslam fihi. Note that this is the majority Hanafi view.
The ruling applies to three specific items: ras al-mal, thaman, and muslam fihi.
2
Identify Zufar's objection
Zufar argues the pledge is invalid because the purpose of a pledge is istifa' (recovery) of the exact right. Pledging a different item substitutes (istibdal) the original, which is prohibited in salam and sarf due to lack of homogeneity (mujanasah).
The prohibition of substitution in salam/sarf is a key principle: the capital/price cannot be changed after contract.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond that homogeneity (mujanasah) exists in monetary value (maliyyah). The pledge is not a substitution of the specific item but a security based on value. Since value is the basis of liability (as previously explained in rahn), recovery is achieved through value.
The key is separating the physical identity ('ayn) from the monetary value (maliyyah). The pledge is homogeneous with the right in terms of value.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if the pledge is lost, under the Hanafi view the pledgee compensates the creditor from the pledge's value. Under Zufar's view, the pledge is invalid, so no compensation is due from the pledgee.
The dispute directly affects the creditor's security and the pledgee's liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ہے تو مالیت دونوں کے اندر موجود ہے لہذا مجانست متحقق ہے اور تبدیلی کا اعتراض غلط ہے۔
Ashraf al-Bidayah, Urdu commentary of Hidayah, volume 14. FIZ. The ruling of pledge for the capital of salam sale, the price of sarf, and the muslam fihi. Chapter of pledge. He said: And the pledge is valid for the capital of salam, the price of sarf, and the muslam fihi. And Zufar said: It is not permissible because its ruling is recovery, and this is a substitution due to lack of homogeneity, and the door of substitution in these is closed. And for us (Hanafis): Homogeneity is established in monetary value, so recovery is realized in terms of wealth, and that is that which is guaranteed, as passed. Translation: Quduri said: And a pledge for the capital of salam, the price of sarf, and the muslam fihi is valid. And Zufar said: It is not permissible because the ruling of pledge is recovery, and this is changing due to lack of homogeneity, and the door of substitution in these transactions is closed. And our proof is that homogeneity is established in monetary value, so recovery is realized in terms of wealth, and according to previous detail, wealth is what is guaranteed. Explanation: The detailed exposition of salam and sarf has passed in volume 3 of Hidayah. In salam, the price is called ras al-mal, the sold item is called muslam fihi, the seller is called muslam ilayh, and the buyer is called rabb al-salam. In salam, possession of the capital is necessary before separation of parties, and whatever is fixed as capital or muslam fihi, its substitution is not allowed. Similarly, in sarf, possession of both price and sold item is required before separation, and substitution of the price is not allowed. When this detail is understood, now listen: According to us, it is valid to pledge in exchange for the capital, the price of sarf, and the muslam fihi. But an objection arises: This pledge should not be valid because when a pledge is given in exchange for these, substitution of these items becomes necessary. That is, the capital is fixed as something else, and something else is given in its place. So the pledged item does not achieve recovery of the right but rather a change of the right. For this reason, Imam Zufar declared these pledges invalid because there is no homogeneity between the pledged item and the right, so instead of recovery, substitution necessarily occurs. We answered this: It has passed before that the pledged item is a trust and its monetary value is guaranteed. So the mentioned pledge, although different in terms of its specific identity, is not different in terms of its monetary value; rather it is homogeneous with the right. And since in pledge the essence of what is guaranteed is monetary value, and monetary value exists in both, homogeneity is established, and the objection of substitution is incorrect.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage addresses a dispute with Imam Zufar. The ruling from Quduri is that it is valid to pledge for the capital (ras al-mal) in a salam sale, for the price (thaman) in a sarf transaction, and for the muslam fihi (the commodity to be delivered in salam). Zufar argues it is invalid because the purpose of a pledge is to enable recovery of the right (istifa'), but here pledging something else amounts to substitution (istibdal), which is prohibited in salam and sarf. The Hanafi response is that the required similarity (mujanasah) exists in terms of monetary value (maliyyah), so recovery can be realized through value. Liability is based on value, not the specific item. Therefore, the pledge is valid.

Key Terms
رہن (rahn): A pledge or collateral given as security for a debt
بیع سلم (bay' salam): A forward sale where the price is paid in advance for future delivery of a specified commodity
بیع صرف (bay' sarf): Exchange of precious metals (gold/silver) in the same or different forms
مجانست (mujanasah): Similarity or homogeneity in legal attribute
مالیت (maliyyah): Monetary value or property value

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because it leads to substitution (istibdal) which is prohibited
C) Because the pledgee does not have possession
D) Because the debt is not due

Key Takeaway
A pledge for salam capital or sarf price is valid because homogeneity is in monetary value, not the specific item, and value is the basis of liability in rahn.

Pledge for the Sold Item is Invalid
States that a pledge given for the sold item (mabee') in a sale is invalid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a pledge for the sold item (mabee') is batil and explain the reason based on the principle of ghayr madmun.

Core Idea
A pledge for the sold item is invalid because it is not a guaranteed debt.

In this passage, al-Quduri lays down a clear ruling: a pledge (rahn) given for the sold item (mabee') in a sale is invalid. The reasoning rests on a fundamental Hanafi principle: only items that are owed as debts or guarantees (madmun) can be pledged. Since the mabee' is not owed by the seller (the seller owes delivery of the item, but the item itself is not a debt), it cannot be pledged. We will unpack this ruling and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The passage states clearly: 'walrahn bilmabee' batil' – the pledge for the sold item is void. This is the explicit Hanafi position.
Batil means the contract is legally void from its inception.
2
Understand the Rationale
The reason given is that the mabee' is 'ghayr madmun' – not a guaranteed obligation. In Hanafi law, only something that is owed as a debt or guarantee (madmun) can be the subject of a valid pledge.
The mabee' is a specific item, not a debt; therefore it cannot be pledged.
3
Trace the Consequence
If the pledged item is destroyed in the hands of the pledgee (the buyer), no compensation is due. Because the contract is void, the possession is considered 'qabd bi idhn' (possession with permission), which is a trust (amanah).
The loss falls on the pledgor, not the pledgee.
4
Note the Hanafi Principle
The ruling illustrates the broader principle: only items that are madmun (owed) can be pledged. The mabee' is not owed; it is the price that is owed.
Contrast with a pledge for a debt – that is valid.
5
Consider Cross-Madhhab Variation
Other schools may allow a pledge for the sold item, but the Hanafi school strictly prohibits it based on this reasoning.
The disagreement stems from different definitions of what can be pledged.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مبیع کے بدلے رہن کا حکم
قال والرهن بالمبيع باطل لما بينا انه غير مضمون بنفسه فان هلک ذهب بغیر شيئ لانه لا اعتبار للباطل فبقى قبضا باذنه
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور بیع کے بدلہ میں رہن باطل ہے اسی دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں کہ میع غیر مضمون بنفسہ ہے پس اگر مرہون مشتری کے پاس ہلاک ہو جائے تو بغیر کسی ٹی کے ہلاک ہو گا اس لئے کہ عقد باطل کا اعتبار نہیں ہے پس مرہون بائع راہن کی اجازت سے مقبوض باقی رہا۔
The ruling of pledge for the sold item. He said: And the pledge for the sold item is invalid, because we have explained that it is not guaranteed in itself. So if it is destroyed, it is destroyed without anything, because an invalid contract is not considered. So it remains as a possession with permission. Translation: Quduri said: And a pledge for the sold item is invalid due to the same proof that we have explained: that the sold item is not guaranteed in itself. So if the pledged item is destroyed in the buyer's hands, it will be destroyed without any compensation, because the invalid contract is not recognized. So the pledgor's possession remains with permission.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling that a pledge for the sold item (mabee') in a sale is invalid. The reason is that the mabee' is not a guaranteed item (ghayr madmun) in itself; the seller does not owe it as a debt. Therefore, a pledge for it is invalid. If the pledged item is destroyed in the hands of the pledgee (the buyer), no compensation is due because the contract is void; the possession is by permission (qabd bi idhn) and thus a trust.

Key Terms
مبیع (mabee'): The sold item, the subject matter of a sale
غیر مضمون (ghayr madmun): Not guaranteed; not something for which the holder is liable

C) Because the pledgee already owns it
D) Because the seller does not have possession

Key Takeaway
A pledge for the sold item (mabee') is batil because the mabee' is not a guaranteed obligation (ghayr madmun); only debts can be pledged.

Obligations for Which Pledge Is Invalid
Ruling listing non-financial obligations for which pledge is invalid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that a pledge is only valid for financial obligations that are guaranteed (madhmun) and identify which types of obligations cannot be secured by a pledge, giving the rationale for each.

Core Idea
A pledge is only valid to secure a guaranteed financial debt; personal, corporal, and non-financial obligations cannot be pledged.

In the Hanafi school, a pledge (rahn) is a contract that secures a debt. However, not every obligation can be secured by a pledge. The governing principle is that the obligation must be a financial liability that is guaranteed (madhmun) on the debtor. This passage lists several obligations that fail this test, explaining why a pledge is invalid for each. Understanding this principle helps you correctly apply the rules of rahn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the common principle
Determine what all invalid cases share: the obligation is not a financial debt that is guaranteed on the debtor.
The key term is 'madhmun' – something for which the debtor can be held liable in property.
2
Analyze the first exception: kafala bi-nafs
A personal guarantee (e.g., to produce someone in court) is not a financial claim; if the person fails to appear, no monetary loss is recoverable from the guarantor.
3
Analyze qisas and shuf'a
Retaliation (qisas) is a corporal punishment, not a debt; the right of preemption (shuf'a) attaches to property but is not a guaranteed debt until taking possession.
For accidental injury (khata'), the blood money (arsh) is a financial claim, so pledge is valid.
4
Analyze the slave cases and wages
A slave who commits a crime or is indebted is not personally liable for his actions; the master's liability is limited to the slave's value. Similarly, wages for wailing or singing are not considered guaranteed property in Shariah.
The absence of guarantee (damān) renders the pledge ineffective.
5
Synthesize the ruling
Conclude that a pledge is only valid for a debt that is madhmun (guaranteed financial liability). All listed obligations lack this quality.
This is the operative principle for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجوز الرهن بالكفالة بالنفس وكذا بالقصاص فى النفس وما دونها لتعذر الاستيفاء بخلاف ما اذا كانت الجناية خطاء لأن استيفاء الارش من الرهن ممكن ولا يجوز الرهن بالشفعة لان المبيع غير مضمون على المشترى ولا بالعبد الجانى والعبد المديون الماذون لانه غير مضمون على المولى فانه لوهلك لا يجب عليه شيئ ولا باجرة النائحة والمغنية حتى لو ضاع لم يكن مضمونا لانه لا يقابله شيئ مضمون
ترجمہ اور کفالت بالنفس کے بدلے میں رہن جائز نہیں ہے اور ایسے ہی نفس اور مادون النفس کے قصاص کے بدلہ رہن جائز نہیں ہے بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ جنایت خطا ہو اس لئے کہ رہن سے ارش کی وصولیابی ممکن ہے اور شفعہ کے بدلہ میں رہن جائز نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ مشتری پر مبیع غیر مضمون ہے اور عبد مجرم اور عبد مدیون مازون کے بدلہ میں رہن جائز نہیں اس لئے کہ مولیٰ پر غلام مضمون
And it is not permissible to pledge for guarantee of the person (kafala bi-nafs), and similarly for retaliation (qisas) in life or limb, because recovery is impossible; unlike the case where the injury is accidental (khata'), because recovery of the blood money (arsh) from the pledge is possible. And it is not permissible to pledge for the right of preemption (shuf'a), because the sold item is not guaranteed (ghayr madhmun) on the buyer. And not for the slave who commits a crime (al-abd al-jani) or the indebted slave with permission (al-abd al-madyun al-ma'dhun), because he is not guaranteed on the master; for if he perishes, nothing is obligatory. And not for the wages of a wailer (na'iha) or a singer (moghanniya), for if they are lost, they are not guaranteed, because they are not equivalent to something guaranteed. Translation: And pledging for the guarantee of the person is not permissible, and similarly for retaliation for life or limb, due to the difficulty of recovery; unlike the case where the injury is accidental, because recovery of the blood money from the pledge is possible. And pledging for preemption is not permissible, because the sold item is not guaranteed on the buyer. And not for the slave who is a criminal or the indebted slave with permission, because he is not guaranteed on the master; if he perishes, nothing is obligatory. And not for the wages of a wailer or a singer, because if lost, they are not guaranteed, as they are not matched by something guaranteed.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement listing several types of obligations for which a pledge contract is not valid according to the Hanafi school. The underlying principle is that a pledge can only secure a financial obligation (dayn) that is guaranteed (madhmun), meaning the debtor is personally liable for it. If the obligation is not financial or is not guaranteed, a pledge is invalid because there is no effective recourse to the collateral. The list includes: 1) Guarantee of the person (kafala bi-nafs) – guaranteeing that a person will appear, not a debt; 2) Retaliation (qisas) for murder or battery – this is a corporal punishment, not a financial claim; however, if the injury is accidental (khata'), the compensation (arsh) is a financial claim, so a pledge is valid; 3) Right of preemption (shuf'a) – this is a right to purchase property, but the sold item is not guaranteed on the buyer until he takes possession; 4) A slave who commits a crime (al-abd al-jani) or an indebted slave with permission (al-abd al-madyun al-ma'dhun) – these slaves are not personally liable for their acts; the master's liability is limited to the slave's value; 5) Wages of a wailer or singer – these are for services that are not considered valuable property (mal mutaqawwim) in the Shariah. The commentary in Urdu emphasizes that for each, the absence of guarantee (damān) or the impossibility of recovery renders the pledge invalid.

Key Terms
كفالة بالنفس (kafāla bi-nafs): A guarantee that a person will be present at a certain time or place; not a financial liability.
مضمون (madhmūn): Guaranteed; something for which the debtor is personally liable and which can be recovered from his property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because preemption is not a recognized right
B) Because the sold item is not guaranteed on the buyer until he takes possession
C) Because preemption is a personal right, not a financial claim
D) Because the value is unknown

Key Takeaway
A pledge can only secure a financial debt that is guaranteed; personal, corporal, or non-financial obligations cannot be pledged.

6 min
Pledging Free Persons, Mudabbir, Mukatab, and Umm Walad
States the ruling and reason for invalidity of pledging these persons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that these four categories cannot be pledged and explain the legal reason ('illa) based on the impossibility of execution.

Core Idea
A pledge requires the creditor to execute against the property; if execution is impossible, the pledge is invalid.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a fundamental rule in the law of rahn: certain human beings cannot be used as collateral. The author states the ruling and immediately gives the reason. Understanding this 'illa will enable you to reason about other cases where execution is barred.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
List the four types: free person (hurr), mudabbir (slave promised freedom after master's death), mukatab (slave under manumission contract), and umm walad (slave mother of master's child).
Also note that they are distinct in their status of freedom.
2
Understand the purpose of rahn
The essence of a valid rahn is to establish yad al-istifa' — the creditor's right to take possession and execute the debt from the pledged property.
This requires the pledged item to be saleable and transferable.
3
Analyze why execution fails for the free person
A free person has no financial value (mal) because he cannot be owned or sold. Thus execution is impossible.
Even if the free person consents, a pledge is invalid because the property is not saleable.
4
Analyze why execution fails for the other three
The mudabbir, mukatab, and umm walad are wealth but there is a legal barrier (mani') that prevents their sale: the mudabbir is promised freedom, the mukatab's property is protected, and the umm walad becomes free upon the master's death.
The barrier makes execution impossible despite the underlying value.
5
Conclude the ruling
Since execution (istifa') is not achievable in any of these cases, the pledge is invalid (ghayr ja'iz). The contract is void from the start.
This ruling applies regardless of the debtor's consent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تر، مدبر، مکاتب، ام ولد کو بطور رہن رکھنے کا حکم
قال ولا يجوز رهن الحر والمدبر والمكاتب وام الولد لان حكم الرهن ثبوت يد الاستيفاء ولا يتحقق الاستيفاء من هؤلاء لعدم المالية في الحر وقيام المانع في الباقين
ترجمہ مصنف نے فرمایا اور آزاد اور مدبر اور مکاتب اور ام ولد کو رہن رکھنا جائز نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ رہن کا حکم ید استیفاء کا ثبوت ہے اور ان لوگوں سے وصولیابی متفق نہیں ہو سکتی آزاد کے اندر مالیت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اور باقیوں میں مانع کے موجود ہونے کی وجہ سے۔
تشریح آزاد چونکہ مال نہیں ہے اور باقی مال ہیں مگر ان میں من وجہ حریت پیدا ہو جانے کی وجہ سے ان سے قرض کی وصولیابی ناممکن ہے لہذا پھر ان کو رہن رکھنا بھی جائز نہ ہوگا۔
Heading: Ruling on pledging a mudabbir, mukatab, and umm walad. He said: It is not permissible to pledge a free person, a mudabbir, a mukatab, or an umm walad because the ruling of a pledge is the establishment of the hand of execution, and execution cannot be realized from these: due to lack of financial value in the free person, and due to the existence of a barrier in the others. Translation: The author said: It is not permissible to pledge a free person, a mudabbir, a mukatab, and an umm walad because the ruling of a pledge is the establishment of the hand of execution, and recovery from these people is not possible: due to lack of financial value in the free person, and due to the existence of a barrier in the rest. Commentary: The free person is not wealth, and the others are wealth but due to the emergence of freedom in some aspect, recovery of debt from them is impossible; therefore, pledging them is also not permissible.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (talil) from the matn of Al-Hidayah. The author states that a free person (hurr), a mudabbir (slave promised emancipation after master's death), a mukatab (slave under contract of manumission), and an umm walad (slave mother of her master's child) cannot be pledged as collateral. The reason ('illa) is that the purpose of a pledge is to secure a debt by allowing the creditor to execute recovery from the pledged property. For a free person, there is no financial value because a free person cannot be owned or sold. For the other three categories, although they have some financial value, there is a legal barrier (mani') that prevents execution: the mudabbir cannot be sold after the master's death; the mukatab's property is protected during his contract; and the umm walad cannot be sold because she becomes free upon the master's death. Thus, in all cases, the creditor cannot recover the debt from them, so the pledge is invalid. The Urdu commentary clarifies that the free person is not property, while the others are property but due to partial freedom, debt recovery is impossible.

Key Terms
رهن (rahn): A contract where property is given as security for a debt, allowing the creditor to recover the debt from it if necessary.
ید استیفاء (yad al-istifa'): The hand of execution, meaning the creditor's right to take possession of the pledge and recover the debt from it.
مدبر (mudabbir): A slave whom the master has promised to free after the master's death.
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract of manumission with the master to purchase his freedom.
ام ولد (umm walad): A female slave who has borne a child to her master.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because a mudabbir is not considered wealth at all
B) Because there is a legal barrier (mani') that prevents execution
C) Because a mudabbir cannot be owned by anyone
D) Because the debt is not guaranteed

Key Takeaway
A valid pledge requires the pledged item to be saleable and executable upon; persons with barriers to sale or no financial value cannot be pledged.

Rahn — Pledge

When a Pledge is Invalid – Five Cases in Hanafi Fiqh
Lists invalid pledges with ʿilla

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which obligations cannot be secured by a pledge (rahn) and explain the common requirement that the obligation must be a guaranteed financial right (madhmun).

Core Idea
A pledge is only valid for a guaranteed financial debt; pledges for personal guarantees, corporal punishment, unguaranteed sales, or non-binding wages are invalid.

This passage from Al-Hidayah lists five specific obligations for which a pledge is not valid according to the Hanafi school. Each case is accompanied by a clear reason (ʿilla) showing why a pledge cannot be used. Understanding these exceptions reveals the essential condition for a valid pledge: the underlying right must be a guaranteed financial liability (madhmun). This lesson will walk through each case and its reasoning, and demonstrate how the same principle applies across seemingly different situations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the common condition for a valid pledge
Recognize that rahn requires the debt to be a guaranteed financial liability (madhmun). If the underlying right is not a financial obligation or not guaranteed, the pledge is invalid.
The text uses the terms 'مضمون' (guaranteed) and 'تعذر الاستيفاء' (impossibility of execution) as key indicators.
2
Analyze the first case: personal guarantee (kafala bil nafs)
A pledge for guaranteeing a person’s presence in court is invalid because it is a personal guarantee, not a financial debt. The presence of a person cannot be recovered from property.
The 'illa is 'لتعذر الاستيفاء' – execution is impossible.
3
Examine the second case: qisas (retaliation) for intentional injury
Qisas for life or limb is a physical punishment, not a financial claim. Therefore, a pledge cannot secure it. However, if the injury is unintentional (khatta'), compensation (arsh/diyah) is due, which is a financial right, so a pledge is valid.
The text contrasts intentional (ʿamd) with unintentional (khatta') to highlight when a pledge becomes valid.
4
Evaluate the third case: pre-emption (shuf'a)
Pledging for the pre-emption price is invalid because the sold property is not guaranteed against the buyer. If the property is destroyed before transfer, the buyer owes nothing; hence the seller's right to the price is not a guaranteed debt.
The 'illa is 'لان المبيع غير مضمون على المشتري' – the sold property is not guaranteed against the buyer.
5
Scrutinize the remaining cases: offending slave, authorized indebted slave, and wages for wailing/singing
For the offending slave (al-ʿabd al-jānī) and the authorized indebted slave (al-ʿabd al-madhūn al-maʾdhūn), the slave himself is to be handed over; the master is not liable if the slave dies. Thus, the master's obligation is not a guaranteed financial debt. Similarly, wages for wailing or singing are not binding (wājib), and thus not guaranteed.
The common 'illa: the underlying right is not a guaranteed financial liability on the obligor.

Source Text

ولا يجوز الرهن بالكفالة بالنفس وكذا بالقصاص في النفس وما دونها لتعذر الاستيفاء بخلاف ما إذا كانت الجناية خطأ لأن استيفاء الأرش من الرهن ممكن ولا يجوز الرهن بالشفعة لأن المبيع غير مضمون على المشتري ولا بالعبد الجاني والعبد المديون المأذون لأنه غير مضمون على المولى فإنه لو هلك لا يجب عليه شيء ولا بأجرة النائحة والمغنية حتى لو ضاع لم يكن مضمونا لأنه لا يقابله شيء مضمون

تشریح جن چیزوں کے بدلہ میں رہن جائز نہیں ہے کچھ ان چیزوں کا بیان کیا جارہا ہے۔ 1 زید پر عدالت میں مثلاً کوئی مقدمہ ہے جس کی وجہ سے وہ گرفتار ہے خالد نے زید کی ضمانت کی جس کا مقصد یہ ہوتا ہے کہ یہ کہیں بھاگے گا نہیں میں اس کو حاضر کرنے کا کفیل ہوں خالد نے زید کی کفالت بالنفس کے عوض رہن رکھد یا تو یہ رہن جائز نہ ہوگا کیونکہ رہن تو اس لئے ہوتا ہے کہ اس کی وجہ سے حق کی وصولیابی ہو سکے اور یہاں رہن سے زید کی حضوری اور وصولیابی نہیں ہوسکتی۔ - زید نے خالد کو عدا اقتل کر دیا جس کی وجہ سے زید کے اوپر قصاص واجب ہے زید نے قصاص کے بدلے رہن رکھ دیا تو یہ رہن جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ رہن سے قصاص کی وصولیابی نہیں ہوسکتی۔ زید نے عمد اخالد کا ہاتھ کاٹ دیا جس کی وجہ سے قصاصاً زید کا ہاتھ کاٹا جائیگا زید نے اس قصاص کے بدلہ رہن رکھ دیا تو یہ رہن جائز نہ ہوگا کیونکہ مرہون سے قطع ید کی وصولیابی نہیں ہوسکتی۔ - البتہ اگر زید نے خطاء خالد کو قتل کر دیا خطاء اس کا ہاتھ کاٹ دیا جس کی وجہ سے دیت یا ارش واجب ہوا زید نے دیت اور ارش کے بدلہ مثلاً اپنی موٹر بس رہن رکھدی تو یہ جائز ہے کیونکہ یہاں دیت یارش کو وصول کرنا ہے جس کی وصولیابی اس مرہون سے ہو سکتی ہے۔
- زید اور خالد کی زمین باہم متصل ہے مگر زید کی زمین دریا سے ملحق ہے اور خالد کی زمین اوپر ہے پس زید نے اپنی زمین بکر کے ہاتھ فروخت کی اور خالد نے شفعہ طلب کیا تو بکر نے خالد کے پاس شفعہ ( دار شفوعہ) کے عوض رہن رکھا تو یہ رہن جائز نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ اگر دریا کی دھار بدلی اور اس نے زید کی زمین مبیعہ کو کاٹ کر دھارا کر لیا تو بکر پر اس کا ضمان واجب نہیں اور رہن اس چیز کے عوض جائز ہوتا ہے جو مضمون نفسہ ہو۔ ۶۔ زید کے غلام نے خطائہ کسی کا ہاتھ کاٹ ڈالا جس کی وجہ سے یہ واجب ہوا کہ یہ غلام مجرم مقطوع الید کے حوالہ کیا جائے تو مولی اگر اس کے بدلہ میں رہن دے تو جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ اگر یہ غلام ہلاک ہو جائے تو مولیٰ پر کچھ ضمان واجب نہیں اور غیر مضمون کے عوض رہن رکھنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ ے۔ زید نے اپنے غلام کو تجارت کی اجازت دی جس کی وجہ سے وہ مقروض ہو گیا تو یہ غلام قرض خواہوں کے حوالہ کیا جائے گا مولیٰ نے چاہا کہ غلام کے عوض رہن رکھ دوں تو جائز نہیں ہے اسی دلیل مذکور کی وجہ سے۔ -۸- زید کے گھر میں کوئی شخص مر گیا خالد ہ کو اجیر رکھا کہ وہ اس کے اوپر روئے پھر اس کی اجرت کے عوض اس کے پاس کوئی چیز رہن رکھی تو یہ رہن جائز نہیں ہے اسی طرح زید نے اپنے گھر کوئی گانے والی عورت اجرت پر بلائی پھر اس کی اجرت کے عوض اس کے پاس رہن رکھا تو یہ رہن جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ رونے اور گانے والی کی اجرت واجب نہیں ہوئی تو وہ غیر مضمون ہے اور غیر مضمون کے عوض رہن جائز نہیں ہوتا لہذا یہ رہن جائز نہ ہوگا۔
Heading: For which things it is not permissible to pledge. And it is not permissible to pledge for personal guarantee (kafala bil nafs), and likewise for qisas in life and limbs because execution is impossible; unlike when the injury is unintentional (خطأ) because recovery of compensation (arsh) from the pledge is possible. And it is not permissible to pledge for pre-emption (shuf'a) because the sold property is not guaranteed (ghayr madhmun) against the buyer. And not for the offending slave or the authorized indebted slave because the slave is not guaranteed against the master; if the slave dies, nothing is due from the master. And not for the wage of the wailing woman or the singing woman; even if it is lost, it is not guaranteed because there is nothing guaranteed in exchange. Translation: It is not permissible to pledge for personal guarantee, and similarly for qisas in life and what is below it, except when the injury is unintentional (خطأ) because recovery of compensation from the pledge is possible. It is not permissible to pledge for pre-emption because the sold property is not guaranteed against the buyer. It is not permissible to pledge for the offending slave and the authorized indebted slave because the slave is not guaranteed against the master; if the slave dies, nothing is due from the master. And it is not permissible to pledge for the wage of the wailing woman and the singing woman; even if the pledge is lost, it is not guaranteed because there is nothing guaranteed in exchange. Commentary: Some things for which a pledge is not permissible are being explained. 1. If Zaid is detained in court and Khalid guarantees his presence, and Khalid pledges something for that personal guarantee, it is invalid because the pledge is for recovery of a right, but the presence of Zaid cannot be recovered from the pledge. 2. If Zaid intentionally kills Khalid, qisas becomes due; if Zaid pledges for qisas, it is invalid because qisas cannot be exacted from a pledge. Similarly for amputation. But if the killing or amputation is unintentional (خطأ), then blood money or compensation is due, and a pledge for that is valid because it can be recovered. 3. Pre-emption: If Zaid sells his land to Bakr, and Khalid exercises pre-emption, but Bakr pledges something for the pre-emption price, it is invalid because the sold land is not guaranteed against Bakr if it is destroyed (by natural causes). 4. If Zaid's slave unintentionally injures someone, the slave is handed over; if the master pledges for that, it is invalid because if the slave dies, the master owes nothing. 5. If Zaid authorizes his slave to trade and the slave becomes indebted, the slave is handed over to creditors; pledging for him is invalid for the same reason. 6. If someone hires a wailing woman or singing woman, pledging for their wage is invalid because such wages are not obligatory (non-binding) and thus not guaranteed.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage lists several obligations for which a pledge (rahn) is invalid according to the Hanafi school, each with a specific reason. The common thread is that a pledge is only valid for a financial right that is guaranteed (madhmun), meaning the party liable is obligated to pay compensation if the subject matter is lost. 

First, pledging for personal guarantee (kafala bil nafs) is invalid because the purpose of the guarantee is to ensure a person's presence, which cannot be recovered from a pledge.

Second, pledging for qisas (retaliation) for life or limbs is invalid because qisas is a physical punishment that cannot be executed from property. However, if the injury is unintentional (خطأ) and compensation (arsh/diyah) is due, then a pledge is valid because compensation is a financial right.

Third, pledging for pre-emption (shuf'a) is invalid because the sold property is not guaranteed against the buyer if it is destroyed (e.g., by natural disaster); the buyer is not liable for its destruction. Since the right of pre-emption is not secured by a guaranteed obligation, a pledge is not suitable.

Fourth, for an offending slave (who commits a crime) or an authorized indebted slave (who trades with permission), the slave himself is to be handed over to the claimant; if the master pledges something for the slave, it is invalid because the slave is not a guaranteed liability on the master. If the slave dies, the master owes nothing.

Fifth, for the wage of a wailing woman or singing woman, pledging is invalid because such contracts are not enforceable (the wage is not wajib) and therefore not guaranteed.

The Urdu commentary explains each case with examples: Zaid and Khalid scenarios. It emphasizes that the validity of a pledge depends on the underlying right being a guaranteed financial obligation.

Key Terms
كفالة بالنفس (kafala bil nafs): A guarantee to produce a person (e.g., in court) or ensure their presence.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment for murder or injury, equal to the harm caused.
شفعة (shuf'a): Pre-emption: the right of a co-owner or neighbor to purchase property sold to a third party.
مضمون (madhmun): Guaranteed; a liability that must be compensated if lost or destroyed.
ارش (arsh): Compensation for injury below the level of full blood-money (diyah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A pledge is only valid for a guaranteed financial liability; any other obligation cannot be secured by a pledge.

Invalidity of Pledge for Non-Guaranteed Wages
Ruling that a pledge for wages is void because wages are not guaranteed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for a valid pledge (rahn) and explain why a pledge for wages is invalid under Hanafi law.

Core Idea
A pledge is only valid if it secures a guaranteed debt (maddun); wages are not maddun, so the pledge is void.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Hanafi school: a pledge (rahn) given to secure wages (ujrah) is invalid. The reason is that wages are not considered a guaranteed debt (maddun). Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the law of pledges.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is giving a pledge to secure wages. The ruling is that it is invalid (batil) and not a valid pledge at all.
2
Identify the condition for a valid pledge
A valid pledge must correspond to a maddun (guaranteed and enforceable) debt. The author states that nothing maddun corresponds to this pledge because wages are not maddun.
Maddun refers to a debt that is due and certain, such as a loan or price of goods.
3
Understand why wages are not maddun
Wages (ujrah) are not considered maddun in Hanafi law because they are not yet earned or are conditional. They become due only after service is rendered, so they are not a present guaranteed debt at the time of the pledge.
4
Apply the ruling to liability
If the pledged item is destroyed in the hands of the pledgee (the women), they are not liable because the pledge itself is void and the rulings of pledge do not apply.
5
Note the consequence in court
If the pledgee claims wages before the pledge in the qadi's court, the qadi will not order payment because wages are not enforceable as a maddun debt in this context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تو اگر رہن رکھ دیا اور مرہون ان عورتوں کے پاس ہلاک ہو گیا تو ان پر ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا کیونکہ یہ رہن ہی نہیں لہذا اس پر رہن کے احکام بھی جاری نہ ہوں گے۔ اس کو مصنف نے فرمایا لانہ لا یقابلہ شی مضمون اس لئے کہ اس رہن کے مقابلہ میں کوئی مضمون بھی نہیں ہے کیونکہ اجرت مضمون نہیں یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر یہ قاضی کی عدالت میں رہن سے پہلے اجرت کا دعوی کریں تو قاضی یہ حکم نہیں کرے گا کہ ان کو ان کی اجرت دیجائے ۔
So if he gave a pledge and the pledged item was destroyed in the possession of those women, no liability is incumbent upon them because it is not a pledge at all; therefore the rulings of pledge do not apply to it. The author said this: 'because nothing maddun corresponds to it'. This is because in exchange for this pledge there is no maddun item, since wages are not maddun. For this reason, if these women claim wages before the pledge in the qadi's court, the qadi will not order that their wages be paid.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement. It addresses a case where a pledge is given to secure wages (ujrah). The ruling is that such a pledge is invalid and carries no liability if destroyed. The reason is that wages are not considered maddun (a guaranteed debt) in Hanafi law. A valid pledge (rahn) must correspond to a maddun debt; since wages are not guaranteed, the pledge is void. Consequently, the normal rules of pledge do not apply. If the pledgee (here, women) claimed their wages before the pledge was given, a judge would not compel payment because the wages themselves are not legally enforceable as a debt in this context.

Key Terms
مضمون (maddun): A debt or obligation that is legally guaranteed and enforceable; a debt that can be secured by a valid pledge.
اجرت (ujrah): Wages or hire; compensation for services rendered.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a pledge given for wages (ujrah) invalid according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) Because wages are less than the value of the pledge
B) Because wages are not considered maddun (guaranteed debt)
C) Because the pledge is given to women
D) Because the pledge was destroyed

Key Takeaway
A pledge (rahn) is only valid if it secures a maddun (guaranteed) debt; wages are not maddun, so a pledge for wages is void.

Rahn of Wine between Muslims and Dhimmis
Ruling on rahn of wine with liability by qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on pledging wine in three scenarios (Muslim-Dhimmi, Dhimmi-Muslim, Dhimmi-Dhimmi) and explain the liability rules derived from qiyas to ghasb.

Core Idea
Wine is no property for Muslims, so pledging it is haram; but for Dhimmis it is property, so liability follows ghasb.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a nuanced issue: can wine be pledged in a rahn contract? Since wine is not considered property (mal) for Muslims, the general rule is prohibition. However, when one or both parties are Dhimmis, the ruling changes based on their status. The text uses qiyas to ghasb to determine liability when the wine is destroyed. Understanding this case sharpens your application of legal analogy within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general prohibition
The text begins by stating that a Muslim cannot pledge or accept wine as pledge from anyone. Why? Because wine is not considered property (mal) for Muslims, making the transaction impossible to fulfill validly.
Recall the Hanafi principle that only items that are mal (property) can be validly transacted.
2
Analyze the mixed case: Muslim pledgee, Dhimmi pledgor
If a Muslim accepts wine as pledge from a Dhimmi, and the wine is destroyed, the text says it is guaranteed against the Muslim. Why? The proof is qiyas to ghasb: if a Muslim usurps a Dhimmi's wine, he is liable. Here, the pledgee is like a usurper if the wine is lost.
The liability arises because the Dhimmi's wine is property in his right, and the Muslim holds it.
3
Analyze the opposite mixed case: Muslim pledgor, Dhimmi pledgee
Here, the Dhimmi pledgee is not liable to the Muslim if the wine is destroyed. Why? Because if a Dhimmi usurps wine from a Muslim, he is not liable (since wine is not property for the Muslim). The same qiyas applies.
The liability mirrors the ghasb rule in both directions.
4
Analyze the intra-Dhimmi case
When both parties are Dhimmis, the contract is fully valid and normal rahn rules apply, including liability if destroyed. Why? Because wine is property (mal) in their right, so the transaction is lawful for them.
This confirms that property status is relative to the individual's legal capacity.
5
Synthesize the ruling
Summarize: For Muslims, pledging wine is haram and invalid. For Dhimmis, it is valid. In mixed cases, the contract is not entirely void but liability is determined by qiyas to ghasb, protecting the Dhimmi's property rights.
This case illustrates how Hanafi fiqh accommodates Dhimmi legal status within Islamic transactions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجوز للمسلم ان يرهن خمرا اوير تهنه من مسلم او ذمى لتعذر الايفاء والاسيفاء في حق المسلم ثم الراهن اذا كان ذميا فالخمر مضمون عليه للذمى كما اذا غصبه وان كان المرتهن ذميا لم يضمنها للمسلم كمالايضمنهابالغصب منه بخلاف ما اذا جرى ذالك فيما بينهم لانها مال في حقهم

ترجمہ اور مسلمان کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ وہ شراب رہن دے یا اس کو رہن لے مسلمان سے ہو یا ڈمی سے مسلمان کے حق دینے اور لینے کے عذر ہونے کی وجہ سے پھر راہن جبکہ ذمی ہو تو مسلمان پر ذمی کے لئے شراب مضمون ہوگی جیسا کہ جبکہ مسلمان نے ذمی کی شراب غصب کی ہو اور اگر مرتہن ذمی ہو تو مسلمان کے لئے شراب کا ضامن نہ ہوگا جیسا کہ ذمی شراب کا ضامن نہیں جبکہ اس نے مسلمان سے شراب غصب کی ہو بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ یہ عقد آپس میں ذمیوں کے درمیان ہوا ہو اسلئے کہ شراب ان کے حق میں مال ہے۔

تشریح مسلمان کے لئے جائز نہیں کہ وہ شراب رہن دے یا رہن رکھے کیونکہ مسلمان شراب کا نہ مالک ہو سکتا ہے اور نہ بنا سکتا گینی شراب کا لین دین اس کے حق میں ممنوع ہے۔ بہر حال اگر مسلم اور ذمی کے درمیان عقد رہن ہوا تو اب کیا حکم ہے؟ تو فرمایا کہ اگر مسلمان مرتہن ہو اور راہن ذمی ہو اور مسلمان کے پاس یہ شراب ہلاک ہو جائے تو مسلمان پر اس کا ضمان واجب ہوگا کیونکہ اگر مسلمان ذمی کی شراب غصب کرتا تب بھی مسلمان پر اس کا ضمان واجب ہوتا ہے۔ اور اگر مسئلہ برعکس ہو کہ مرتہن ذمی اور راہن مسلمان تو ذمی پر مسلمان کے لئے ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اگر ذمی مسلمان کی شراب غصب کرتا تب بھی ذمی بر ضمان واجب نہ ہوتا اسی طرح یہاں بھی نہ ہوگا، اور اگر یہ عقد رو زمیوں کے درمیان ہو تو اب بہر دو صورت اس پر رہن کے احکام جاری ہوں گے کیونکہ شراب ذمیوں کے حق میں مال ہے۔
And it is not permissible for a Muslim to pledge wine or to take it as a pledge from a Muslim or a Dhimmi, due to the impossibility of giving and taking in the right of the Muslim. Then if the pledgor is a Dhimmi, the wine is guaranteed (maddun) against him for the Dhimmi, just as if he had usurped it. And if the pledgee is a Dhimmi, he is not liable for it to the Muslim, just as he is not liable for it if he usurps it from a Muslim, contrary to the case where this occurs between them (two Dhimmis), because wine is property in their right.

Translation: And it is not permissible for a Muslim to give wine as a pledge or to take it as a pledge, from a Muslim or a Dhimmi, because of the excuse of giving and taking in the right of the Muslim. Then when the pledgor is a Dhimmi, wine is liable upon the Muslim for the Dhimmi, just as when a Muslim usurps a Dhimmi's wine. And if the pledgee is a Dhimmi, he is not liable for the wine to the Muslim, just as a Dhimmi is not liable for wine when he usurps it from a Muslim. Contrary to the case when this contract occurs between Dhimmis, because wine is property in their right.

Explanation: It is not permissible for a Muslim to give wine as a pledge or to take it as a pledge, because a Muslim can neither own wine nor make it; dealing in wine is prohibited for him. Nevertheless, if a contract of pledge occurs between a Muslim and a Dhimmi, what is the ruling? He said: If the Muslim is the pledgee and the pledgor is a Dhimmi, and this wine is destroyed in the possession of the Muslim, then the Muslim is liable for it, because if the Muslim had usurped the Dhimmi's wine, he would also be liable for it. And if the case is opposite, i.e., the pledgee is a Dhimmi and the pledgor is a Muslim, then the Dhimmi is not liable for it to the Muslim, because if the Dhimmi had usurped the Muslim's wine, he would not be liable, similarly here. And if this contract occurs between Dhimmis, then in both cases the rulings of pledge apply, because wine is property in their right.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, explaining the permissibility and liability of pledging wine (khamr). It first states a general prohibition for Muslims: a Muslim cannot pledge wine or accept it as a pledge, because wine is not considered property (mal) for Muslims, and thus it cannot be validly given or taken. Then it details three mixed cases:

1) If the pledgor (rahin) is a Dhimmi and the pledgee (murtahin) is a Muslim, the wine is considered guaranteed (maddun) against the Muslim pledgee. This is by analogy (qiyas) to ghasb (usurpation): if a Muslim usurps a Dhimmi's wine, he must compensate it because wine is property for the Dhimmi. So if the wine is destroyed, the Muslim is liable.

2) If the pledgor is a Muslim and the pledgee is a Dhimmi, the Dhimmi is not liable to the Muslim for the wine if destroyed. This is because if a Dhimmi usurps wine from a Muslim, he is not liable (since wine is not property for the Muslim). So by the same analogy, no liability arises.

3) If both parties are Dhimmis, the contract is fully valid because wine is property in their religion. Both pledging and taking pledge are permissible, and the normal rules of rahn apply, including liability if destroyed.

The proof (dalil) for the prohibition on Muslims is the impossibility of lawful giving and taking (ta'azzur al-ifa' wa al-istifa') since wine is not recognized as property in Islam. The mixed cases are resolved through qiyas on ghasb.

Key Terms
خمر (khamr): Wine; a drink made from grapes that is intoxicating and prohibited for Muslims.
ذمی (dhimmi): A non-Muslim subject living under the protection of an Islamic state, permitted to practice his religion and follow his own laws in private matters, including property rights.
غصب (ghasb): Usurpation; wrongful taking of another's property without right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a rahn contract between a Muslim pledgee and a Dhimmi pledgor involving wine, what happens if the wine is destroyed?
A) The Muslim pledgee is liable because he cannot own wine
B) The Dhimmi pledgor is liable because he owns the wine
C) The Muslim pledgee is liable by analogy to ghasb
D) No one is liable because the contract is invalid

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of rahn depends on whether the item is property (mal) for the parties; wine is not for Muslims but is for Dhimmis, and liability is determined by analogy to ghasb.

Rahn of Carrion is Invalid Even for Dhimmis
Ruling that carrion cannot be pledged, even among Dhimmis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling regarding pledging carrion and explain why it is invalid even among Dhimmis.

Core Idea
Carrion is not property (mal) for anyone, so pledging it is invalid for both Muslims and Dhimmis.

In a previous lesson, you learned that wine is considered property for Dhimmis and thus can be pledged among them. However, this lesson addresses carrion (maytah), which is treated differently. Even though Dhimmis may benefit from carrion in some contexts, Islamic law does not recognize it as property. Therefore, any contract of rahn involving carrion is void, regardless of the parties' faith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and the object
The contract under discussion is rahn (pledge), and the object being pledged is carrion (maytah) — an animal that died without proper Islamic slaughter.
Carrion is najis (impure) and not considered property.
2
State the ruling
The text clearly states that it is not permissible to pledge carrion or to accept it as a pledge. The ruling applies to both Muslims and Dhimmis.
Ruling: batil (void).
3
Identify the reason
Carrion is not considered property (mal) in the view of Islamic law. Since a valid pledge requires the object to be mal, the contract fails.
The root cause is the lack of mal-status.
4
Compare with wine
Wine is recognized as property for Dhimmis, so pledges among them are valid. However, carrion lacks this status universally.
The distinction highlights that property status can vary by party, but carrion is never mal.
5
Consequence of invalidity
Since the contract is void, if the carrion is destroyed in the hands of the pledgee, they bear no liability (daman).
No compensation is owed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اما الميتة فليست بمال عندهم فلا يجوز رهنماوارتها نها فيما بينهم كما لا يجوز فيمابين المسلمين

ترجمہ بہر حال مردار تو وہ ان کے نزدیک مال نہیں ہے تو اسکور بہن دینا اور اس کو رہن لینا ان کے درمیان بھی جائز نہیں ہے جیسا کہ مسلمانوں کے درمیان جائز نہیں ہے۔

تشریح شراب تو ذمیوں کے حق میں مال ہے مگر مردار مال نہیں ہے لہذ امردار کا رہن جیسے مسلمانوں کے درمیان جائز نہیں ایسے ہی
As for carrion, it is not property in their view, so it is not permissible to pledge it or take it as a pledge among them, just as it is not permissible among Muslims.

Translation: As for carrion, it is not considered property in their view, so giving it as a pledge and taking it as a pledge is not permissible among them, just as it is not permissible among Muslims.

Explanation: Wine is property in the right of Dhimmis, but carrion is not property. So the pledge of carrion is not permissible just as it is not permissible among Muslims.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This is a ruling statement establishing that carrion (maytah) cannot be the object of a valid pledge (rahn), even when both parties are Dhimmis. The reason is that carrion is not considered property (mal) in any legal system—neither for Muslims nor for Dhimmis. While wine is recognized as property for Dhimmis (as in the previous lesson), carrion lacks that status. Therefore, any contract of rahn involving carrion is void, and no liability (daman) attaches if it is destroyed. This is consistent with the general principle that only items that are legally considered property can be pledged.

Key Terms
میتہ (maytah): Carrion; an animal that died without being properly slaughtered according to Islamic law.

D) Because the contract would be wasteful

Rahn of Items Later Found Invalid: Liability Despite Defect
Intra-Hanafi dispute on rahn liability for inherently invalid pledged items.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the liability of a pledge when the pledged item is later discovered to be invalid, and distinguish the Zahir al-Riwayah view from the view of Imam Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
A pledge given against an apparently valid debt remains liable even if the pledged item is later found to be inherently invalid.

Imagine you accept a pledge as security for a debt, only to later discover the pledged item is legally defective — a free person, wine, or carrion. Does the pledge still hold? This lesson explores a nuanced Hanafi ruling that protects the creditor's good faith. According to the authoritative Zahir al-Riwayah, the pledge remains liable because the debt was apparently valid at contract time. However, Imam Abu Yusuf dissents. We will unpack the reasoning and practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Zahir al-Riwayah)
Identify that according to Abu Hanifa, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and the Zahir al-Riwayah, the pledge is liable (maddun) in all three scenarios: the pledged slave is free, vinegar is wine, or goat is carrion.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the opposing view
Note that Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees; his qiyas renders the pledge void when the defect is discovered, because the underlying obligation disappears.
Abu Yusuf's qiyas is the same in all similar cases.
3
Analyze the reasoning behind the Zahir al-Riwayah
Understand the key concept: the debt was 'dayn wajib zahiran' (apparently obligatory) at the time of contract. The pledgee acted in good faith, and the debtor cannot escape liability by later claiming ignorance.
The apparent validity is determined at contract formation.
4
Examine the proof
The text argues that if the creditor had sued before the defect was discovered, the judge would have ordered payment. This shows the debt was legally enforceable at that time.
This proof supports the liability despite the defect.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Zahir al-Riwayah, the creditor can claim the value of the pledge up to the debt amount. Under Abu Yusuf, the creditor cannot claim anything because the pledge is void.
The amount of liability is the lesser of the debt or the pledge's value.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو اشترى عبدا ورهن يثمنه عبدا او خلا اوشاة مذبوحة ثم ظهر العبد حرا والخل خمر والشاة ميتة فالرهن مضمون لانه رهنه بدین واجب ظاهرا و كذا اذاقتل عبدا ورهن بقيمته رهنا ثم ظهر انه حرو هذا كله على ظاهر الرواية وكذا اذا صالح على انكار ورهن بما صالح عليه رهنا ثم تصادقا ان لادين فالرهن مضمون وعن ابی یوسف خلافه و كذا قياسه فيما تقدم من جنسه 

ترجمہ اور اگر غلام خریدا اور اس کے ثمن کے بدلہ غلام یا سر کہ مذبوح بکری رہن رکھدی پھر غلام آزاد اور سرکہ شراب اور بکری مردار ظاہری ہوئی رہن مضمون ہے اس لئے کہ مشتری نے ان چیزوں کو ایسے دین کے بدلہ رہن رکھا جو ظاہر واجب ہے اور ایسے ہی جبکہ کسی غلام کو قتل کیا اور اس کی قیمت کے بدلہ رہن رکھا پھر یہ بات ظاہر ہوئی کہ غلام مقتول آزاد ہے اور یہ ساری گفتگو ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق ہے اور ایسے ہی جبکہ انکار پر مصالحت کی اور جس چیز پر صلح کی اس کے بدلہ کوئی رہن رکھ دیا پھر دونوں نے اتفاق کر لیا کہ قرض نہیں تھا تو رہن مضمون ہے اور ابو یوسف سے اس کے خلاف منقول ہے اور اس کے جس کے پہلے مسائل میں ( بھی ) ابو یوسف کا یہی قیاس ہے۔ 

تشریح مصنف نے یہ ساری گفتگو اس وقت فرمائی جبکہ مرہون کا شراب یا مردار یا آزاد ہونا پہلے سے ظاہر ہو اور اگر پہلے سے ظاہر نہ ہو بلکہ بعد میں یہ بات ظاہر ہو تو اس کا حکم اور ہے جس کو یہاں بیان کیا جا رہا ہے۔ ا۔ زید نے خالد سے مثلاً ایک غلام اورشن کے بدلہ بائع کے پاس ایک غلام یا سر کہ باند بوح بکری رہن رکھدی تو رہن صحیح ہے مگر بعد میں معلوم ہوا کہ یہ مرہون غلام نہیں بلکہ آزاد ہے یا مرہون سرکہ نہیں بلکہ شراب ہے یا ند بوح بکری کے بارے میں معلوم ہوا کہ یہ تو مردار ہے تو کیا اب بھی مرہون کا ضمان واجب ہوگا تو فرمایا کہ مرہون مضمون ہے کیونکہ جب رہن رکھا گیا تھا تو ظاہر واجبی قرض کے بدلہ رکھا گیا ہے بہر حال منمان واجب ہو گا رہی یہ بات کہ کتنا ضمان ہوگا تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ثمن مبیع اور مرہون کی قیمت میں سے جو بھی کم ہو اس کے مطابق ضمان ہوگا، اور یہاں دین واجبی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر مذکورہ باتوں کے ظہور سے پہلے بائع ثمن کے بارے میں قاضی کے یہاں نالش کر دے تو قاضی اداء شمن کا حکم کر دیگا۔ ۲ زید نے خالد کا غلام خطاء قتل کر دیا اور اس کی قیمت کے بدلہ زید نے خالد کے پاس رہن رکھد یا جائز ہے پھر معلوم ہوا کہ جس کو قتل کیا گیا ہے وہ آزاد ہے تب بھی رہن مضمون ہوگا بدلیل مذکورہ بالا اور یہ ظاہر الروایہ ہے اور نو اور میں بھی اس کے خلاف منقول نہیں ہے البتہ امام ابو یوسف کے قول کا قیاس کہتا ہے کہ ان کا ان تمام صورتوں میں اختلاف ہے۔ ۳۔ زید نے خالد پر ۱۰ روپے کا دعویٰ کیا خالد نے انکار کیا مگر بات بڑھنے کی وجہ سے خالد نے مصالحت کر لی اور پھر مال صلح کے بدلہ میں اس کے پاس رہن رکھدیا پھر دونوں نے اتفاق کر لیا کہ کوئی قرض نہیں ہے تب بھی رہن مضمون ہوگا۔ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک رہن مضمون نہ ہوگا کیونکہ جب دونوں نے عدم دین پر اتفاق کر لیا تو انہوں نے عدم ضمان پر اتفاق کر لیا اور
And if he bought a slave and pledged a slave or vinegar or a slaughtered goat as the price, then it becomes apparent that the slave is free, the vinegar is wine, and the goat is carrion, the pledge is liable (maddun) because he pledged it against a debt that is apparently obligatory. Likewise, if he killed a slave and pledged something for his blood money, then it becomes apparent that he was free; all this is according to Zahir al-Riwayah. Likewise, if he made a settlement (sulh) upon denial and pledged something for the settlement amount, then they both agree that there is no debt, the pledge is liable. And from Abu Yusuf, there is a contrary opinion, and his qiyas (analogy) is the same in the previous issues of this type.

Translation: And if he bought a slave and pledged a slave or vinegar or a slaughtered goat against its price, then it becomes apparent that the slave is free, the vinegar is wine, and the goat is carrion, the pledge is liable because the buyer pledged it against a debt that is apparently obligatory. And similarly, if he killed a slave and pledged something for his blood money, then it becomes apparent that the killed slave was free; all this is according to Zahir al-Riwayah. And similarly, if he made a settlement upon denial and pledged something for the settlement amount, then they both agree that there was no debt, the pledge is liable. And from Abu Yusuf, there is a contrary opinion, and his qiyas is the same in the previous issues of this type.

Explanation: The author says all this when the fact that the pledged item is wine, carrion, or free was not apparent from the beginning; rather, it becomes known later. The ruling is different. 1. Zaid bought a slave from Khalid and pledged a slave or a slaughtered goat to the seller. The pledge is valid, but later it is discovered that the pledged slave is free, or the vinegar is wine, or the goat is carrion. Is there liability? He said: The pledge is liable because at the time of pledging it was given against a debt that is apparently obligatory. The amount of liability is the lesser of the price of the sold item or the value of the pledge. The evidence that the debt was apparently obligatory is that if the seller had complained to the judge before the discovery, the judge would order payment. 2. Zaid killed Khalid's slave by mistake and pledged something for its blood money. Later it is discovered that the killed person was free. The pledge is still liable, and this is Zahir al-Riwayah; nothing contrary is transmitted in Nawadir, but Abu Yusuf's qiyas indicates his disagreement in all these cases. 3. Zaid claimed 10 rupees from Khalid; Khalid denied, but due to the matter escalating, Khalid made a settlement and pledged something for the settlement amount. Then both agree there was no debt. The pledge is still liable. According to Abu Yusuf, the pledge is not liable because when both agreed on the absence of debt, they agreed on the absence of liability.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) and a ruling with proof. It addresses a scenario where a pledge is given against a debt that appears valid at the time, but later the pledged item is discovered to be inherently invalid for rahn: a free person, wine, or carrion. According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad (the position of Zahir al-Riwayah), the pledge is still liable (maddun) because the debt against which it was given was apparently obligatory (dhan wajib zahiran) at the time of the contract. The pledgee acted in good faith, and the debtor cannot escape liability by claiming ignorance. The liability amount is the lesser of the debt value or the pledge's value. The text provides three examples:

1) Purchase of a slave: The buyer pledges a slave, vinegar, or goat as security for the price. Later it emerges the pledged slave is free, the vinegar is wine, or the goat is carrion. The pledge is liable because the debt (price) was apparently due. If the seller had sued before discovering the defect, the judge would have ordered payment.

2) Accidental killing: A person kills a slave by mistake and pledges security for the blood money (diyah). Later it turns out the slain person was free. The pledge remains liable.

3) Settlement upon denial: A claimant demands money; the defendant denies but settles and pledges property for the settlement amount. Later both agree there was no original debt. The pledge is still liable because the settlement created an apparently valid obligation.

Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees in all these cases. His qiyas (analogy) is that since the underlying debt is ultimately found to be non-existent, the pledge should also be void, and no liability should attach. For example, in the settlement case, both parties agreeing that there was no debt implies they also agree there is no liability; hence the pledge should not be maddun.

Key Terms
ظاہر الروایہ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The well-known and authoritative transmitted rulings from the founding imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) compiled by Imam Muhammad in his six books.
مضمون (maddun): Liable; subject to guarantee or compensation; in this context, the pledge is considered valid and creates a financial obligation on the pledgor.
دین واجب ظاہرا (dayn wajib zahiran): A debt that appears to be legally obligatory at the time of the contract, even if later found to be void.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Zahir al-Riwayah position, if a person buys a slave and pledges a goat as security, but later the goat is found to be carrion, what is the ruling on the pledge?
A) The pledge is void and carries no liability
B) The pledge is valid and the goat is liable (maddun)
C) The contract is nullified because carrion cannot be pledged
D) The buyer must replace the goat with a valid item

Key Takeaway
A pledge remains liable if given against an apparently valid debt, even if the pledged item is later found to be legally invalid — per the mufta bihi Hanafi position.

Liability of Pledge When Pledged Item is Invalid
Ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute on pledge liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on pledge liability when the pledged item is discovered to be invalid, identify the proof (dayn wajib zahiran), and explain the dispute between Zahir al-Riwayah and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
A pledge remains liable if the debt was apparently valid when pledged, even if the item later proves invalid.

Imagine you buy a slave and pledge a bottle of vinegar as security. Later you discover the bottle actually contains wine—an invalid item for pledge. Does your pledge lose all value? The Hanafi ruling is surprising: the pledge remains valid and liable because the debt was apparently obligatory at the time. This lesson explores three such scenarios and the reasoning behind the rule, including a key difference with Imam Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
Read the passage and list the three cases: (1) pledge for a purchased item that turns out to be free/wine/carrion, (2) pledge for blood money where the slain is later found free, (3) settlement pledge where both later agree no debt existed.
All three share a common principle: the debt was wajib zahran at pledge time.
2
Extract the general ruling
The passage states the pledge is madhmun (liable) in all three. Determine the hukm level: valid and binding (sahih/madhmun).
Liability means the creditor can claim compensation if lost.
3
Analyze the proof (dalil)
The proof is rational: if the creditor had sued before the defect appeared, the judge would have ordered payment. Thus the debt was apparently wajib.
This is a qiyas based on the apparent validity of the debt.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
Imam Abu Yusuf differs in the settlement case, and his qiyas extends to all cases. He argues that if both parties later agree there was no debt, their agreement nullifies liability.
The preserved narration from Abu Yusuf is only in the settlement case, but his principle applies broadly.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text explicitly says 'this is all on Zahir al-Riwayah', which is the relied-upon position. Abu Yusuf's view is acknowledged but not operative for fatwa.
Zahir al-Riwayah carries more authority in Hanafi fiqh.

ترجمہ اور اگر غلام خریدا اور اس کے ثمن کے بدلہ غلام یا سر کہ مذبوح بکری رہن رکھدی پھر غلام آزاد اور سرکہ شراب اور بکری مردار ظاہری ہوئی رہن مضمون ہے اس لئے کہ مشتری نے ان چیزوں کو ایسے دین کے بدلہ رہن پر مصالحت کی اور جس چیز پر صلح کی اس کے بدلہ کوئی رہن رکھ دیا پھر دونوں نے اتفاق کر لیا کہ قرض نہیں تھا تو رہن مضمون ہے اور ابو یوسف سے اس کے خلاف منقول ہے اور اس کے جس کے پہلے مسائل میں ( بھی ) ابو یوسف کا یہی قیاس ہے۔ تشریح مصنف نے یہ ساری گفتگو اس وقت فرمائی جبکہ مرہون کا شراب یا مردار یا آزاد ہونا پہلے سے ظاہر ہو اور اگر پہلے سے ظاہر نہ ہو بلکہ بعد میں یہ بات ظاہر ہو تو اس کا حکم اور ہے جس کو یہاں بیان کیا جا رہا ہے۔ ا۔ زید نے خالد سے مثلاً ایک غلام اورشن کے بدلہ بائع کے پاس ایک غلام یا سر کہ باند بوح بکری رہن رکھدی تو رہن صحیح ہے مگر بعد میں معلوم ہوا کہ یہ مرہون غلام نہیں بلکہ آزاد ہے یا مرہون سرکہ نہیں بلکہ شراب ہے یا ند بوح بکری کے بارے میں معلوم ہوا کہ یہ تو مردار ہے تو کیا اب بھی مرہون کا ضمان واجب ہوگا تو فرمایا کہ مرہون مضمون ہے کیونکہ جب رہن رکھا گیا تھا تو ظاہر واجبی قرض کے بدلہ رکھا گیا ہے بہر حال منمان واجب ہو گا رہی یہ بات کہ کتنا ضمان ہوگا تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ثمن مبیع اور مرہون کی قیمت میں سے جو بھی کم ہو اس کے مطابق ضمان ہوگا، اور یہاں دین واجبی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر مذکورہ باتوں کے ظہور سے پہلے بائع ثمن کے بارے میں قاضی کے یہاں نالش کر دے تو قاضی اداء شمن کا حکم کر دیگا۔ ۲ زید نے خالد کا غلام خطاء قتل کر دیا اور اس کی قیمت کے بدلہ زید نے خالد کے پاس رہن رکھد یا جائز ہے پھر معلوم ہوا کہ جس کو قتل کیا گیا ہے وہ آزاد ہے تب بھی رہن مضمون ہوگا بدلیل مذکورہ بالا اور یہ ظاہر الروایہ ہے اور نو اور میں بھی اس کے خلاف منقول نہیں ہے البتہ امام ابو یوسف کے قول کا قیاس کہتا ہے کہ ان کا ان تمام صورتوں میں اختلاف ہے۔ ۳۔ زید نے خالد پر ۱۰ روپے کا دعویٰ کیا خالد نے انکار کیا مگر بات بڑھنے کی وجہ سے خالد نے مصالحت کر لی اور پھر مال صلح کے بدلہ میں اس کے پاس رہن رکھدیا پھر دونوں نے اتفاق کر لیا کہ کوئی قرض نہیں ہے تب بھی رہن مضمون ہوگا۔
امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک رہن مضمون نہ ہوگا کیونکہ جب دونوں نے عدم دین پر اتفاق کر لیا تو انہوں نے عدم ضمان پر اتفاق کر لیا اور ان دونوں کا اتفاق ان کے حق میں حجت ہوگا۔
امام ابو یوسف سے روایت محفوظہ تو صرف اسی مصالحت والے مسئلہ میں ہے مگر ان کے اس قول کا قیاس چاہتا ہے کہ ولوا شتری سے یہاں تک کہ تمام مسائل میں انکا یہ اختلاف جاری ہونا چاہیے۔
If someone buys a slave and pledges as its price a slave or vinegar or a slaughtered sheep, then it appears that the slave is free, the vinegar is wine, and the sheep is carrion, then the pledge is liable (madhmun) because he pledged it against a debt that was apparently wajib. Likewise, if he kills a slave and pledges its value as a pledge, then it appears that [the slain] is free. All this is according to Zahir al-Riwayah. Likewise, if he makes a settlement (sulh) upon denial and pledges something against the settlement, then they both agree that there was no debt, then the pledge is liable. And from Abu Yusuf there is a difference, and likewise his analogy in the preceding similar cases.

Translation: If a slave is purchased and a slave or a slaughtered goat is pledged as its price, then the slave becomes free, the vinegar becomes wine, and the goat becomes carrion, the pledge is liable because the buyer pledged these things against a debt that is apparently wajib. Similarly, when a slave is killed and its value is pledged, then it appears that the slain slave is free. All this discussion is according to Zahir al-Riwayah. Similarly, when a settlement is made upon denial and something is pledged against the settlement, then both agree that there was no debt, then the pledge is liable. And from Abu Yusuf the opposite is narrated, and his analogy in the preceding issues is the same.

Commentary: The author made all this discussion when the pledged item being wine, carrion, or free is apparent beforehand. But if it is not apparent beforehand, but later becomes apparent, then its ruling is different, which is being explained here. For example, Zayd purchased a slave from Khalid for a price and pledged with the seller a slave or a slaughtered goat. The pledge is valid, but later it is known that the pledged slave is actually free, or the pledged vinegar is wine, or the slaughtered goat is carrion. Does the pledge become liable? He said: The pledge is liable because when the pledge was made, it was made against a debt that was apparently wajib. In any case, liability is wajib. As for how much liability, the answer is: the lesser of the price of the sold item and the value of the pledged item will be the liability. The proof that the debt was wajib is that if before the appearance of these facts the seller files a case with the judge regarding the price, the judge would order payment of the price. (2) Zayd kills Khalid's slave by mistake and pledges its value with Khalid, it is permissible. Then it appears that the slain is free, then the pledge is liable by the above proof. This is Zahir al-Riwayah, and in Nawadir nothing is narrated to the contrary. However, the analogy of Abu Yusuf's statement indicates that he differs in all these cases. (3) Zayd claims 10 rupees from Khalid, Khalid denies, but due to escalation Khalid makes a settlement and then pledges something against the settlement. Then both agree that there was no debt. Then the pledge is liable. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, the pledge will not be liable because when both agreed on the absence of debt, they agreed on the absence of liability, and their agreement is a proof for them. The preserved narration from Imam Abu Yusuf is only in this settlement issue, but his analogy requires that his difference runs through all the cases from 'wa law ishtara...' onwards.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and includes an intra-Hanafi dispute. It addresses scenarios where a pledged item is discovered to be invalid (a free person, wine, or carrion), but the debt was apparently valid at the time of pledging. The ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah is that the pledge remains liable (madhmun) because the debt was wajib zahiran (apparently obligatory). The proof is rational: if the creditor had sued before the defect was known, the judge would have ordered payment. The commentary explains three cases: (1) a pledge of trade goods that turn out to be invalid, (2) a pledge for blood money where the slain is later found to be free, and (3) a settlement pledge where both parties later agree there was no debt. In all cases, the pledge is liable. However, Imam Abu Yusuf differs in the settlement case based on a preserved narration, and his qiyas extends the difference to all cases. The text clarifies that the preserved narration is only in the settlement issue, but his reasoning would apply broadly.

Key Terms
رهن مضمون (rahn madhmun): A pledge that is valid and carries liability, meaning the pledged item is held in security and if lost, the creditor may claim compensation.
دین واجب ظاہرا (dayn wajib zahiran): A debt that appears to be obligatory based on external circumstances, even if it later turns out the debt was not actually valid.
ظاہر الروایہ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The manifest narrations from the six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, considered the primary authoritative source in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The pledge is void because the item cannot be owned.
B) The pledge is liable (madhmun) because the debt was apparently wajib.
C) The pledge is valid only if the creditor knew the item was free.
D) The pledge becomes a wadiah (safe custody) instead.

Key Takeaway
A pledge is valid and liable if the debt was apparently wajib at the time of pledging, even if the pledged item later proves to be legally invalid, unless the parties later agree there was no debt (per disputed view).

Father's Pledge of Minor Son's Property: Istihsan vs Qiyas
Intra-Hanafi dispute with istihsan argument

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Imam Muhammad permits a father to pledge his minor son's property, distinguish it from haqiqat al-ada' (direct payment), and evaluate the qiyas objection of Abu Yusuf and Zufar.

Core Idea
Pledging preserves ownership while adding protection; thus istihsan overrides qiyas.

Can a father use his minor son's property to secure his own debt? The Hanafi school has an internal dispute. Imam Muhammad argues it is permissible and even beneficial, while Abu Yusuf and Zufar object based on qiyas with direct payment. This lesson dissects the reasoning behind each view and shows how istihsan resolves the conflict.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify that Imam Muhammad permits pledging, while Abu Yusuf and Zufar prohibit it.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
2
Analyze Imam Muhammad's dalil
He bases his view on istihsan: the father can already deposit the property as wadiah, and pledging offers more diligent custody because the creditor fears liability.
Istihsan overrides qiyas here.
3
Understand the opposing qiyas
Abu Yusuf and Zufar analogize pledging to haqiqat al-ada' (direct payment), which is prohibited because it removes ownership without immediate compensation.
They consider the illa to be using the son's wealth for the father's benefit.
4
Identify the wajh al-farq
The key difference: direct payment transfers ownership, while pledging only appoints a guardian and keeps ownership intact.
This distinction justifies istihsan.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the madhhab is Imam Muhammad's view, as the text presents it as the manifest (zahir) ruling.
Practical fatwa follows the istihsan ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ويجوز للاب ان يرهن بدين عليه عبدا لابنه الصغير لانه يملك الايداع وهذا النظر في حق الصبي منه لان قيام المرتهن بحفظه ابلغ خيفة الغرامة ولو هلک پهلک مضمونا والوديعة تهلك امانة والوصى بمنزلة الاب في هذا الباب لما بينا وعن ابى يوسف وزفر انه لا يجوز ذالك منهما وهو القياس اعتبارا بحقيقة الايفاء

ترجمہ محمد نے فرمایا اور جائز ہے باپ کے لئے کہ وہ رہن رکھدے اپنے قرض کے عوض میں اپنے صغیر بیٹے کے غلام کو اس لئے کہ باپ ودیعت رکھنے کا مالک ہے اور یہ ( رہن رکھ دینا ) بچہ کے حق میں زیادہ شفقت کا باعث ہے ودیعت رکھنے سے اس لئے کہ مرتین کا قیام مرہون کی حفاظت میں زیادہ پینٹنٹ ہے تاوان کے خوف سے اور اگر مرہون ہلاک ہو جائے تو مضمون ہوگا اور ودیعت بطور امانت کے ہلاک ہوتی ہے اور وصی اس باب میں باپ کے درجہ میں ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور ابو یوسف اور زقر سے منقول ہے کہ یہ رہن ان دونوں (اب ووصی ) کی جانب سے جائز نہیں اور یہی قیاس ہے۔ حقیقتہ دینے پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے۔

وجه فرق، اقول فقهاء
ووجه الفرق على الظاهر وهو الاستحسان ان في حقيقة الايفاء ازالة ملك الصغير من غير عوض يقابله في الحال وفي هذا نصب حافظ لما له ناجزا مع بقاء ملكه فوضح الفرق

ترجمہ اور ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق فرق کی وجہ اور یہی استحسان ہے یہ ہے کہ حقیقہ دینے میں صغیر کی ملک کا ازالہ ہے بغیر کسی ایسے عوض کے جو فی الحال اس کی ملک کے مقابل ہو اور رہن میں اس کے مال کے لئے فی الفور نگراں مقرر کرنا ہے صغیر کی ملک کے باقی رہنے کے ساتھ ساتھ تو فرق واضح ہو گیا۔
He (Muhammad) said: It is permissible for the father to pledge a slave belonging to his minor son for a debt owed by the father, because the father has the authority to deposit (wadiah) the son's property, and this (pledging) is more considerate towards the son because the creditor's custody of the pledged item is more diligent for fear of liability. If it perishes, it perishes as a liable (madhmun) item, whereas a wadiah perishes as an amanah. The executor (wasi) has the same status as the father in this matter, as we have explained. And from Abu Yusuf and Zufar it is narrated that this is not permissible from them (father and executor), and that is the qiyas, considering actual payment (haqiqat al-ifa').

Wajh al-Farq (the difference), the fuqaha say: The difference on the manifest (Zahir al-Riwayah), which is istihsan, is that in actual payment (haqiqat al-ifa') there is removal of the minor's ownership without any immediate equivalent compensation, whereas in pledging there is appointment of a guardian for his property immediately while his ownership remains intact. So the difference is clear.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a father can pledge his minor son's property to secure the father's own debt. Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) rules it permissible based on istihsan (juristic preference). He argues that the father already has the authority to deposit the son's property as wadiah (trust), and pledging provides even better protection because the creditor keeps it more carefully to avoid liability. If the pledged item perishes, it is liable (madhmun), unlike a wadiah which is an amanah. The executor (wasi) has the same authority. However, Abu Yusuf and Zufar disagree, saying it is not permissible based on qiyas: comparing it to actually paying the debt with the son's property (haqiqat al-ifa'), which is not allowed because the father would be using the son's wealth without immediate compensation. The text then gives the distinguishing factor (wajh al-farq): actual payment removes the son's ownership without equivalent benefit, while pledging appoints a custodian for the property without removing ownership, so the son benefits from protection. Thus, the istihsan view (Imam Muhammad) is the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas in favor of a more equitable or practical ruling based on a stronger evidence.
حقیقت اداء (haqiqat al-ada'): Actual payment or transfer of ownership from the minor's property to satisfy a debt.
ودیعت (wadiah): A contract of safe custody where the depositary holds the item as an amanah (trust) without liability for loss unless negligent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for Imam Muhammad's ruling that a father may pledge his minor son's property?
A) The father's absolute ownership of the son's property.
B) Qiyas with haqiqat al-ada'.
C) Istihsan because pledging provides better protection than wadiah.
D) The son's consent.

Key Takeaway
A father may pledge his minor son's property for his own debt, based on istihsan, because it provides better protection without transferring ownership.
