Father's Authority to Pledge His Minor Child's Property for His Own Debt
Ruling on father pledging minor's property, with dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf/Zufar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on a father pledging his minor child's property for his own debt and identify the opposing view of Abu Yusuf and Zufar based on qiyas.

Core Idea
Pledging does not transfer ownership, so istihsan permits it, distinguishing it from direct payment.

This passage examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute: may a father use his minor child's property as collateral for his own debt? Imam Muhammad allows it based on istihsan (juristic preference), arguing that pledging provides better protection than a deposit. However, Abu Yusuf and Zufar reject it by qiyas, analogizing to direct payment. The text resolves the dispute by distinguishing between transfer of ownership and mere security.

Guided Path
1
State the relied-upon ruling
Identify that the Hanafi school permits the father to pledge his minor child's property for his own debt.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Examine the istihsan proof
The father already has authority to deposit; pledging provides stronger protection because the pawnbroker is liable.
Deposit is an amanah (trust), while rahn is a daman (guarantee).
3
Identify the opposing qiyas
Abu Yusuf and Zufar analogize pledging to direct payment (haqiqat al-ifa'), which is prohibited because it transfers ownership without compensation.
Qiyas: the father cannot directly pay his debt with the child's property.
4
Analyze the basis of distinction (wajh al-farq)
In direct payment, ownership is removed; in pledging, ownership remains and only a security interest is created.
This distinction justifies the preference for istihsan over qiyas.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The permissive view (istihsan) is the operative fatwa.
Though the Sahibayn disagree, the relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ويجوز للاب ان يرهن بدين عليه عبدا لابنه الصغير لانه يملك الايداع وهذا النظر في حق الصبي منه لان قيام المرتهن بحفظه ابلغ خيفة الغرامة ولو هلك هلك مضمونا والوديعة تهلك امانة والوصى بمنزلة الاب في هذا الباب لما بينا وعن ابى يوسف وزفر انه لا يجوز ذالك منهما وهو القياس اعتبارا بحقيقة الايفاء ووجه الفرق على الظاهر وهو الاستحسان ان في حقيقة الايفاء ازالة ملك الصغير من غير عوض يقابله في الحال وفي هذا نصب حافظ لما له ناجزا مع بقاء ملكه فوضح الفرق
He (Muhammad) said: It is permissible for the father to pledge his minor son's slave for a debt due on him, because he has the authority to deposit. And this (pledging) is a better care for the minor, since the pawnbroker's custody of it is stronger due to fear of liability. And if it perishes, it perishes as a guaranteed obligation, whereas a deposit perishes as a trust. And the executor is in the position of the father in this chapter, for what we have stated. And from Abu Yusuf and Zufar: that it is not permissible from them, and that is the analogy, considering the actual payment. And the basis of distinction according to the manifest (opinion) — and it is istihsan — is that in actual payment, there is removal of the minor's ownership without any equivalent consideration in return immediately, whereas in this (pledging), there is appointment of a custodian for his property promptly while his ownership remains. So the distinction is clear.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the authority of a father to pledge his minor child's property to secure his own debt. Imam Muhammad, states the ruling that it is permissible (ja'iz) based on istihsan. The proof is that the father already has the authority to deposit the child's property for safekeeping, and pledging provides even stronger protection because the pawnbroker is liable if the pawn perishes (making it a guaranteed obligation), whereas a deposit is merely a trust with no liability. Moreover, this is more beneficial for the minor. The executor (wasi) has the same authority. In contrast, Abu Yusuf and Zufar hold that it is not permissible based on strict qiyas: they analogize it to the father paying his debt directly with the child's property (haqiqat al-ifa'), which is not allowed because it extinguishes the minor's property without immediate compensation. The text then provides the basis of distinction (wajh al-farq) according to the manifest opinion (istihsan): in direct payment, ownership is transferred without consideration, whereas in pledging, ownership remains with the minor and only a security interest is created with a custodian appointed. Hence, the ruling of permissibility is preferred. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the istihsan view, making this a valid transaction in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
رهن (rahn): A contract where property is given as security for a debt, with the pawnbroker holding possession.
صغير (saghir): A minor child who has not reached puberty and is under guardianship.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides strict qiyas in favor of a more suitable ruling.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning used to derive rulings for new cases based on existing ones.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the basis for permitting a father to pledge his minor child's property for his own debt?
A) Qiyas to deposit
B) Istihsan because it provides better protection
C) The father's right to sell the child's property
D) Necessity

Key Takeaway
A father may pledge his minor child's property for his own debt under Hanafi istihsan, because it does not transfer ownership and benefits the minor.

Effects of a Valid Pledge of Minor's Property and the Analogy with Sale
Consequences of a valid pledge and analogy with sale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the legal effects of a valid pledge of a minor's property by the father, and apply the qiyas between rahn and bay' to determine set-off (muqassah).

Core Idea
A valid pledge of a minor's property discharges the father's debt, and the father is liable; the analogy with sale governs set-off according to the majority.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies the consequences when a father validly pledges his minor child's property. It establishes that the pawnbroker recovers his debt if the pawn perishes, and the father becomes liable to the child. The text then draws an analogy (qiyas) with sale to determine whether set-off (muqassah) occurs when the father sells the child's property directly to his creditor. This reveals a key intra-Hanafi difference between the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling
What happens if the pledged property perishes? State the effect on the pawnbroker's debt and the father's liability.
See the phrase 'يصير المرتهن مستوفيا دينه... ويضمنه للصبى'.
2
Identify the secondary ruling
What is the ruling if the father authorizes the pawnbroker to sell the pledged property?
It is valid as an agency (tawkil).
3
Understand the qiyas
The text states that the basis for this issue is sale (bay'). Identify the asl (sale of minor's property to father's creditor) and the far' (pledge of minor's property).
The 'illa is the end-result regarding liability.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Compare the positions of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and Abu Yusuf regarding set-off in the sale analogy.
The two say set-off occurs; Abu Yusuf says it does not.
5
Extract the 'illa
What is the common effective cause that makes the analogy valid?
It is the end-result (a'qibah) concerning liability (wujub al-daman).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا جاز الرهن يصير المرتهن مستوفيا دينه لو هلك في يده ويصير الاب او الوصى موفيا له ويضمنه للصبى لانه قضى دينه بماله وكذا لوسلطا المرتهن على بيعه لانه توكيل بالبيع وهما يملكانه قالو اصل لهذه المسألة البيع فان الاب او الوصى اذا باع مال الصبى من غريم نفسه جاز وتقع ويضمنه للصبى عندهما وعند ابنى يوسف لا تقع المقاصة وكذا وكيل البائع بالبيع والرهن نظير البيع نظراً الى عاقبته من حيث وجوب الضمان
And when the pledge is permissible, the pawnbroker becomes a recipient of his debt if it perishes in his hand, and the father or executor becomes a payer of it, and they are liable to the child because they paid his debt with his property. Similarly, if they authorize the pawnbroker to sell it, because that is an appointment of agency for sale, and they have the authority to do that. They said: The basis for this issue is sale. For if the father or executor sells the child's property to his own creditor, it is permissible and the set-off occurs, and they are liable to the child according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), whereas according to Ibn Abi Yusuf, the set-off does not occur. Similarly, the agent of the seller in sale and the pledge are analogous to sale, considering their end-result in terms of liability.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage explains the legal effects that follow once a father's pledge of his minor child's property is valid. First, if the pawned property perishes while in the pawnbroker's possession, the pawnbroker is considered to have recovered his debt (i.e., the debt is discharged), and the father (or executor) becomes liable to the child for the value of the property, because he used the child's property to pay off his own debt. Second, the father or executor may also authorize the pawnbroker to sell the pawned property, as this is a valid agency (tawkil) for sale since they have authority over the child's property. The text then draws an analogy with sale (bay'): if the father or executor sells the child's property directly to his own creditor, the sale is valid and set-off (muqassah) occurs between the father's debt and the sale price, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. However, Abu Yusuf disagrees and holds that set-off does not occur in this case. The analogy emphasizes that the pledge (rahn) is similar to sale in its end-result regarding liability (wujub al-daman). The relied-upon position is that set-off occurs (the view of the two, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad).

Key Terms
مقاصة (muqassah): Set-off; the mutual discharge of debts where each party's debt cancels the other's to the extent of the smaller amount.
ضمان (daman): Liability or guarantee; here, the father's obligation to compensate the child for using his property.
توكيل (tawkil): Agency; authorizing another to act on one's behalf, here the guardian authorizing the pawnbroker to sell.
نظير (nazir): Analogue; the text states rahn is nazir al-bay' (analogous to sale).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The pawnbroker loses the debt.
B) The pawnbroker recovers the debt from the father, and the father is liable to the child.
C) The debt is extinguished and no one is liable.
D) The child must repay the debt.

Key Takeaway
A valid pledge of a minor's property discharges the father's debt and makes him liable; the analogy with sale determines set-off according to the majority.

Pawning Minor's Property: Istihsan vs Qiyas
Intra-Hanafi dispute on father pawning minor's property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on pawning a minor's property and distinguish between istihsan and qiyas in this context.

Core Idea
Pawning a minor's property is permitted by istihsan because it appoints a guardian, unlike direct debt repayment which eliminates ownership without compensation.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a father or guardian may pawn a minor's property to secure his own debt. The ruling hinges on whether pawn is equivalent to sale (impermissible) or distinct due to its protective nature. Understanding this difference clarifies the Hanafi methodology of preferring istihsan over strict qiyas in certain cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
What is the specific legal question? The permissibility of a father pawning his minor child's property to secure his own debt.
Note that the father is the guardian (wali) and the debt is personal, not for the minor's benefit.
2
State the two positions
The Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) say it is permissible via istihsan. Abu Yusuf and Zufar say it is not permissible via qiyas.
3
Understand the proofs
The Sahibayn argue that pawn includes appointing a guardian for the minor's property, so it is not an outright elimination. Abu Yusuf and Zufar analogize pawn to sale, which is impermissible for the father's debt.
The key distinction is that pawn does not transfer ownership immediately; it only encumbers the property.
4
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if pawn is executed and the property perishes, the creditor recovers his debt, but the father becomes guarantor for the minor. If not allowed, the pawn is void.
This shows how the ruling affects real transactions.
5
Note the mufta bihi
The text gives preference to the Sahibayn, so the relied-upon position is permissibility by istihsan.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح ظاہر الروایہ میں بچہ کے مال سے قرض ادا کرنا جائز نہیں ، بہر حال قول طرفین استحسان ہے اور قولِ ابو یوسف و زفر قیاس ہے وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ اگر حقیقہ بچہ کے مال سے قرض ادا کیا جائے تو فی الحال بچہ کی ملک کا کوئی عوض نہیں تو یہ مفت میں بچہ کی ملک کا ازالہ ہے جو جائز نہیں اور اگر رہن رکھا جائے تو اس میں فی الحال بچہ کے مال کے لئے اس کی ملکیت کے ساتھ ساتھ نگراں اور محافظ کا مقرر کرنا ہے اس لئے یہ جائز ہے۔ بچے کے مال کو رہن رکھنا درست ہے تو رہن کے احکام جاری ہونگے
Commentary: In Zahir al-Riwayah, it is not permissible to repay debt from a minor's property. Nevertheless, the position of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is istihsan, and the position of Abu Yusuf and Zufar is qiyas. The reason for the difference is that if the minor's property were actually used to repay the debt, there would be no immediate compensation for the minor's ownership, so it would be an elimination of the minor's property without compensation, which is not permissible. But if it is pawned, then initially there is also the appointment of a guardian and protector along with the minor's ownership, so it is permissible. To pawn the minor's property is valid, so the rulings of pawn will apply.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about the permissibility of a father or guardian pawning a minor's property to secure his own debt. The dispute is between the Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) on one side, and Abu Yusuf and Zufar on the other. The Sahibayn rely on istihsan (juristic preference), while Abu Yusuf and Zufar rely on qiyas (analogy to sale). The key distinction is that repayment of debt without compensation eliminates the minor's property outright, which is not allowed. However, pawning provides ongoing security and a guardian, so it is permissible. The passage concludes that pawning the minor's property is valid, thus the rulings of pawn apply.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Equity-based departure from analogical reasoning due to a stronger opposing consideration.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical deduction using the 'illa (effective cause) from a primary case.
طرفین (taraffein): The two: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two authors of the matn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because pawn transfers ownership to the creditor, which is beneficial for the child.
B) Because pawn includes the appointment of a guardian and protector for the minor's property, unlike outright repayment.
C) Because the father needs the money and the child is obligated to help.
D) Because pawn is a stronger contract than sale.

Key Takeaway
Pawning a minor's property is valid per istihsan because it provides ongoing guardianship, unlike outright repayment which eliminates ownership without compensation.

Guarantee of Father/Guardian Upon Perishing of Pawned Minor's Property
Rulings on consequences when pawn of minor's property is valid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the legal consequences when a valid pawn of a minor's property perishes, and explain why the father/guardian becomes a guarantor for the minor's property value.

Core Idea
A father who uses his minor child's property to secure a debt must guarantee its value if lost.

This lesson examines the effects that follow once a pawn (rahn) of a minor's property is validly executed. The Hanafi school rules that if the pawned property perishes in the creditor's possession, the creditor is considered to have recovered his debt, and the father or guardian becomes liable to compensate the minor. This liability is based on the rational principle that one who uses another's property for his own benefit must make good any loss.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
Read the passage carefully and note the situation: a father or guardian pawns the minor's property for his own debt. The pawn is valid. If the pawned property perishes in the mortgagee's hand, what are the consequences?
The text gives two interrelated effects: the mortgagee recovers his debt, and the father/guardian becomes a guarantor (damin) for the minor.
2
Analyze the basis of the guarantee
The text states that the guarantee arises because the father paid his debt with the minor's property. This is a rational reason (ta'lil). Understand that the father's act of using the minor's property to satisfy his own obligation creates a daman obligation.
The guarantee is not based on negligence but on the benefit the father derived from the minor's property.
3
Distinguish the scope of the guarantee
The commentary clarifies that the father must pay the full value of the pawned property, whether it equals, exceeds, or is less than the debt. However, for any excess value, the father is considered a trustee (amin) and is not liable for that portion if it perishes without his fault.
This distinction highlights the Hanafi principle: the father is a guarantor for the principal value but a trustee for any surplus.
4
Understand the authorization to sell
The passage also covers that the father/guardian may authorize the mortgagee to sell the pawned property. Since they have the right to sell the minor's property, they can delegate this power.
This authorization is an agency (wakalah) for sale, which is valid because the father/guardian owns the right to sell.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا جاز الرهن يصير المرتهن مستوفيا دينه لو هلك في يده ويصير الاب او الوصى موفيا له ويضمنه للصبى لانه قضى دينه بماله وكذا لوسلطا المرتهن على بيعه لانه توكيل بالبيع وهما يملكانه ترجمہ اور جب رہن جائز ہوا تو مرتہن اپنے قرض کو وصول کرنے والا ہو جائیگا اگر مرہون اس کے قبضہ میں ہلاک ہو جائے اور باپ یا وصی اس کو ادا کرنے والے ہوں گے اور باپ اور وصی بچہ کے لئے اس کے ضامن ہوں گے اس لئے کہ انہوں نے بچہ کے مال سے اپنا قرض ادا کیا اور ایسے ہی اگر ان دونوں نے مرہون کی بیچ پر مرتین کو مسلط کر دیا ہو اس لئے کہ تسلیط بیچ کی تو کیل ہے اور یہ دونوں تو کیل کے مالک ہیں۔ تشریح جب بچہ کے مال کو رہن رکھنا باپ وہی کے لئے جائز ہے تو اب اس پر رہن کے احکام جاری ہوں گے اور اگر مرتہن کے پاس مرہون ہلاک ہو جائے تو مرتہن اپنے قرض کو وصول پانے والا اور باپ وصی کو ادا کرنے والا شمار کیا جائیگا اور چونکہ انہوں نے بچہ کے مال سے اپنا قرض ادا کیا ہے اس لئے ان پر ضمان واجب ہوگا جس کی تفصیل یہ ہے کہ مرہون کی قیمت دین کے برابر ہو یا زیادہ ہو یا کم ہو بہر صورت مرہون کی قیمت دینی ہوگی برابر اور کمی کی صورت تو ظاہر ہے اور زیادتی کی صورت میں اس لئے کہ باپ اور وصی زیادتی کے اندر مودع اور امین ہیں جس کا ضمان واجب نہیں ہوا کرتا۔ باپ اور وصی کو یہ بھی اختیار ہوتا ہے کہ بچہ کا مال فروخت کر دیں تو فروخت کا وکیل بھٹی بنانے کا حق ہوگالہذا اگر ان دونوں نے مرتہن سے کہ دیا ہو کہ تو رہن کو فروخت کر دے تو یہ بھی جائز ہے۔
And when the pawn is valid, the mortgagee becomes a recoverer of his debt if the pawn perishes in his hand, and the father or executor becomes a payer to him, and he (father/executor) becomes a guarantor for the minor because he [the father/executor] paid his debt with the minor's property. Similarly, if both of them [father and executor] authorize the mortgagee to sell it, it is permissible because the authorization is an agency for sale, and both of them own [the right] to appoint an agent. Translation: And when the pawn is valid, the mortgagee will become a recoverer of his debt if the pawned property perishes in his possession, and the father or executor will be considered as paying him, and the father and executor will be guarantors for the minor because they repaid their debt with the minor's property. And similarly, if both of them authorized the mortgagee to sell the pawn, it is permissible because authorization is agency for sale, and both of them own the right to appoint an agent. Commentary: When pawning the minor's property is permissible for the father or executor, the rulings of pawn will apply. If the pawned property perishes with the mortgagee, the mortgagee recovers his debt, and the father/executor is considered as paying him. And since they paid their debt with the minor's property, they are liable for compensation. The detail: whether the pawn's value equals, exceeds, or is less than the debt, in all cases the value of the pawn must be given. In case of deficiency, it is obvious; in case of excess, because the father and executor are trustees and custodians regarding the excess, so they are not liable. The father and executor also have the authority to sell the minor's property, so they have the right to authorize sale. Therefore, if they told the mortgagee to sell the pawn, it is permissible.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage states the legal consequences once the pawn of a minor's property is validly executed. The Arabic matn (from the Hidayah) provides the ruling: if the pawned property perishes in the mortgagee's possession, the mortgagee is considered to have recovered his debt, and the father or guardian becomes a guarantor for the minor. The Urdu commentary elaborates that the father/guardian must pay the value of the pawned property to the minor, regardless of whether it equals, exceeds, or is less than the debt. For the excess, they are trustees, so no guarantee. Additionally, the father/guardian may authorize the mortgagee to sell the pawn, as they have the right to sell the minor's property.

Key Terms
مرتہن (murtahin): The creditor who receives the pawn as collateral.
ضمان (daman): Liability/guarantee; here the father/guardian becomes liable for the value of the pawn to the minor.
مودع (mudi' / amin): A trustee; here the father is a trustee for the excess value of the pawn beyond the debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The mortgagee loses his debt and the father owes the minor nothing.
B) The mortgagee recovers his debt, and the father owes the minor the value of the pawn.
C) The mortgagee recovers his debt, but only if the pawn's value exactly equals the debt.
D) The father must pay the minor only the amount of the debt, not the pawn's full value.

Key Takeaway
A father who pawns his minor's property must compensate the minor for the full value if the property perishes, regardless of the debt amount.

Set-off in Pawn of Minor's Property: Dispute between Sahibayn and Abu Yusuf
Dispute on set-off in pawn of minor's property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of the Sahibayn and Abu Yusuf regarding set-off in pawn of a minor's property and explain the qiyas basis for extending the sale ruling to pawn.

Core Idea
Set-off in pawn follows the rule of sale: the Sahibayn allow it; Abu Yusuf requires explicit agreement.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether muqassa (automatic set-off) occurs when a guardian sells or pawns a minor's property to his own creditor. The Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) hold that set-off occurs automatically, while Abu Yusuf disagrees. The dispute is extended from sale to pawn because of the shared consequence of guarantee. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to trace how ikhtilaf is applied across analogous transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original case
The base case is a father or executor selling the minor's property to his own creditor. This establishes the ruling for set-off in sale.
The sale itself is valid by consensus.
2
State the positions on set-off
The Sahibayn hold that set-off (muqassa) occurs automatically: the price cancels the debt, and the father guarantees the minor. Abu Yusuf holds that set-off does not occur; the debt remains and the price belongs to the minor.
This is the core ikhtilaf in sale.
3
Identify the shared cause (ʿilla)
The consequence of the transaction is the obligation of guarantee (al-daman) on the father/executor for the minor's property. This ʿilla is present in both sale and pawn.
Guarantee arises because the guardian disposed of the minor's property for his own benefit.
4
Apply qiyas from sale to pawn
Since pawn has the same outcome (obligation of guarantee), the ruling on set-off in sale is extended to pawn by analogy. The author states: 'الرهن نظير البيع' (pawn is analogous to sale).
This is an example of qiyas jaliy (clear analogy).
5
Conclude the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, if the Sahibayn's view is followed, the creditor's debt is cleared immediately and the father owes the minor the price. If Abu Yusuf's view is followed, the creditor must still be paid and the price is held for the minor separately.
Both positions are valid within the Hanafi school; the relied-upon (mufta bihi) is the Sahibayn's view.

المقاصة قالو اصل لهذه المسألة البيع فان الاب او الوصى اذا باع مال الصبى من غريم نفسه جازو تقع ويضمنه للصبى عندهما وعند ابنى يوسف لا تقع المقاصة وكذا وكيل البائع بالبيع والرهن نظير البيع نظراً الى عاقبته من حيث وجوب الضمان ترجمہ مشائخ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اس مسئلہ کی اصل صبیح ہے اس لئے کہ باپ یا وصی جبکہ بچہ کے مال کو اپنے قرضخواہ کے ہاتھ بیچد میں تو جائز ہے اور مقاصہ واقع ہو جائیگا اور یہ دونوں بچہ کے لئے اس کا ضامن ہونگے طرفین کے نزدیک اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک مقاصہ نہیں واقع ہوگا اور ایسے ہی بیچ کے سلسلہ میں بائع کا وکیل اور رہن بیچ کی نظیر ہے اپنے انجام کے اعتبار سے ضمان کے واجب ہونے کی حیثیت سے۔ تشریح مشائخ کرام نے فرمایا کہ امام ابو یوسف اور طرفین کا اصل اختلاف بیع میں ہے اسی اختلاف کو رہن میں فٹ کیا گیا ہے مثلاً باپ یا وصی نے صغیر کا مال اپنے قرض خواہ کے ہاتھ فروخت کر دیا تو بیع جائز ہے اور مقاصہ ہو جائے گا یعنی دین کا بدل ہو جائیگا اور باپ یا وصی کے بچہ کیلئے اس کے مال کا ضامن ہو گا یہ طرفین کا مذہب ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ بیع جائز ہے مگر مقاصہ نہیں ہوگا بلکہ قرضخواہ کا قرض بدستور ہیگا اور شمن بچہ کے لئے ہوگا۔ اس طرح زید ے بکر کو اپنا گھوڑا بیچنے کا وکیل بنایا اتفاق سے اس نے وہ گھوڑا خالد کے ہاتھ فروخت کیا اور خالد کے ایک ہزار روپے زید پر قرض ہیں تو بیع جائز ہے اور مقاصہ ہو جائیگا یعنی زید پر جو قرض ہے یہ ثمن اس کا بدل ہو جائیگا طرفین کے نزدیک اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک مقاصہ نہ ہو گا۔ بہر حال اصل اختلاف یہاں ہے مگر جب دیکھا کہ جیسے بیج کی صورت میں باپ یا وصی پر ضمان واجب ہوتا ہے ایسے ہی رہن کے اندر بھی ضمان واجب ہوتا ہے تو اس اختلاف کو رہن کے اندر بھی جاری کر دیا گیا اس کو مصنف نے فرمایا کہ انجام یعنی وجوب ضمان کے اعتبار سے رہن بیع کی نظیر ہے۔
Al-Muqassa. They said: The basis of this issue is [the case of] sale: if the father or executor sells the minor's property to his own creditor, it is permissible, and the set-off (muqassa) occurs, and he (father) guarantees it for the minor according to both (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). But according to Ibn Yusuf (Abu Yusuf), the set-off does not occur. Similarly, the agent of the seller in sale, and pawn is analogous to sale considering its outcome in terms of the obligation of guarantee. Translation: The mashayikh said: The basis of this issue is sale. When the father or executor sells the minor's property to his own creditor, the sale is valid and set-off occurs, and both (father/executor) are guarantors for the minor – this is the position of the two (taraffein). According to Abu Yusuf, set-off does not occur. And similarly, the agent of the seller [in selling] and pawn is analogous to sale looking at its consequence regarding the obligation of guarantee. Commentary: The mashayikh said that the original dispute between Imam Abu Yusuf and the two (taraffein) is in sale; the same dispute is applied to pawn. For example, if the father or executor sold the minor's property to his own creditor, the sale is valid and set-off occurs, meaning the price becomes a substitute for the debt, and the father or executor is guarantor for the minor for that property – this is the madhhab of the two. Imam Abu Yusuf said: The sale is valid but set-off does not occur; rather, the debt of the creditor remains as before, and the price belongs to the minor. Similarly, if Zayd appointed Bakr as his agent to sell his horse, and Bakr sold it to Khalid, and Khalid owed Zayd a thousand rupees, the sale is valid and set-off occurs – that is, the price becomes a substitute for the debt – according to the two, but according to Imam Abu Yusuf, set-off does not occur. In any case, the original dispute is here. But when it was observed that just as in the case of sale the father or executor is liable for guarantee, similarly in pawn also guarantee is obligatory, so this dispute was also applied to pawn. The author said that in terms of outcome (i.e., the obligation of guarantee), pawn is analogous to sale.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage discusses the issue of muqassa (set-off) in the context of pawn of a minor's property. The principle is analogous to the case of sale: when a father or executor sells the minor's property to his own creditor, there is a dispute between the Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and Abu Yusuf. The Sahibayn hold that the sale is valid and the price automatically sets off the debt (muqassa), making the father guarantor to the minor. Abu Yusuf holds that the sale is valid but no automatic set-off occurs; the debt remains and the price belongs to the minor. The same dispute is extended to pawn because the consequence (obligation of guarantee) is the same. This shows the Hanafi method of extending rulings from one case to another based on shared 'illa (effective cause).

Key Terms
مقاصہ (muqassa): Automatic set-off of a debt by a payment or by the purchase price in a sale.
نظیر (nazir): Analogous; used to extend a ruling from one case to another based on shared cause.
ضمان (daman): Guarantee; liability to compensate for loss or value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, if a father sells his minor child's property to his own creditor, what happens to the debt?
A) The debt remains and the price is held for the minor.
B) The sale is invalid.
C) Set-off occurs and the debt is cleared.
D) The father must repay the debt separately.

Key Takeaway
The set-off dispute in pawn is a direct extension of the sale dispute via qiyas based on the obligation of guarantee.

Father Pawning Minor's Property to Himself: The Legal Fiction of Two Persons
Ruling with proof: talil based on shafaqah and qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a father pawning a minor's property to himself and explain the legal reasoning (talil) based on shafaqah and qiyas.

Core Idea
A father’s compassion makes him two persons — so his single statement suffices for both offer and acceptance in pawning a minor’s property.

Normally, a pawn contract requires two distinct parties for offer and acceptance. But what if a father pawns his minor child’s property to himself? The Hanafi school, based on the father’s unique compassion (shafaqah), treats him as two persons, allowing the contract to be valid. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the analogy to the father buying the minor’s property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is the father doing? He is pawning his minor child's property to himself or to his other minor son or trading slave. The ruling is 'jaez' (permissible).
This is an exception to the general rule that a pawn contract needs two parties.
2
Recognize the apparent problem
A pawn requires offer (ijab) and acceptance (qabul) from two different persons. If the father does both, it seems impossible. The Urdu commentary raises this very objection.
This is the central tension the passage resolves.
3
Trace the legal reasoning (talil)
The solution: the father’s complete compassion (shafaqah) places him in the position of two persons. His single statement counts as both offer and acceptance.
This is an istihsan (juristic preference) based on the exceptional nature of paternal care.
4
Analyze the supporting analogy (qiyas)
The same principle applies when a father buys the minor’s property for himself: he undertakes both sides of the contract. The analogy strengthens the ruling.
Qiyas is used here to extend the existing exception from sale to pawn.
5
Note the scope and limits
This exception applies only to the father (not the mother or other guardians) and only to specific recipients: himself, another minor son, or a trading slave with no debt.
The slave must be a trading slave (tajir) and free of debt; otherwise, the ruling may differ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا رهن الاب من نفسه او من ابن له صغيرا وعبد له تاجر لا دين عليه جاز لان الاب لو فور شفقته انزل منزلة شخصين واقيمت عبارته مقام عبارتين في هذا العقد كما في بيعه مال الصغير من نفسه فتولي طرفي العقد ترجمہ اور جبکہ باپ نے اپنے ہی پاس رہن رکھ لیا یا اپنے دوسرے چھوٹے بچہ کے پاس یا اپنے اس تاجر غلام کے پاس جس پر قرض نہیں ہے تو یہ جائز ہے اس لئے کہ باپ اپنی شفقت کے کمال کی وجہ سے دو شخصوں کے درجہ میں اتار لیا جائے گا اور اس کی عبارت اس عقد میں دو عبارتوں کے قائم مقام کر لی جائے گی جیسا کہ باپ کے بیچنے میں صغیر کے مال کو اپنے ہی ہاتھ تو باپ متولی ہو گا عقد کی دونوں طرفوں کا ( ایجاب قبول کا ) ۔ تشریح اگر باپ نے بچہ کے مال کو اپنے پاس رہن رکھا یا ایسے افراد کے پاس جو اسی کے نفس کے درجہ میں ہیں مثالاً اپنے دوسرے چھوٹے بچہ کے پاس یا اپنے ایسے غلام تاجر کے پاس جس کے اوپر قرض نہ ہو تو یہ جائز ہے۔ سوال اس پر سوال پیدا ہوا کہ رہن کے لئے تو ایجاب و قبول چاہئیں اگر اس کے قول کو ایجاب مانیں تو قبول ندار داور اگر قبول ما نہیں تو ایجاب ندار دالہذا یہ رہن صیح نہ ہونا چاہیے؟ جواب بات تو یونہی ہے مگر ہم نے دیکھا کہ باپ میں کامل شفقت ہے اس لئے اس کو دو آدمیوں کے درجہ میں اتارلیا گیا ہے اور اس کے قول کو دو عبارتوں کے درجہ میں اتار لیا گیا ہے جیسے اگر باپ بچہ کے مال کو خود خریدے تو جائز ہے یہاں بھی وہ تنہا ایجاب قبول کا متولی ہو جاتا ہے تو رہن میں بھی ایسے ہی ہوگا۔
And if the father pawns to himself, or to his other young son, or to his trading slave who has no debt, it is permissible, because the father, due to the perfection of his compassion, is placed in the position of two persons, and his statement is considered as two statements in this contract, just as in his sale of the minor's property to himself, he undertakes both sides of the contract. Translation: And when the father pawns to himself, or to his other young son, or to his trading slave who has no debt, then this is permissible. Because the father, due to the perfection of his compassion, is placed in the rank of two persons, and his statement stands in place of two statements in this contract, just as in the sale of the minor's property to himself, the father undertakes both sides of the contract (offer and acceptance). Commentary: If the father pawns the minor's property to himself, or to persons who are in the station of his own self—such as his other young son or his trading slave who has no debt—then it is permissible. An objection arose: For a pawn, offer and acceptance are required. If we consider his statement as offer, there is no acceptance; if as acceptance, there is no offer. Therefore, it should not be valid. The answer: Indeed, but we see that the father has complete compassion, so he is placed in the position of two persons, and his statement is placed in the position of two statements. Just as if the father buys the minor's property himself, it is permissible; here too, he alone undertakes both offer and acceptance, so in pawn it will be the same.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage discusses a special ruling: a father may pawn his minor child's property to himself, to another minor son, or to his trading slave who is not indebted. Although normally a pawn contract requires two parties for offer and acceptance, the father is deemed two persons due to his complete compassion (shafaqah). This is analogous to the case where the father buys the minor's property for himself. The Urdu commentary raises a potential objection: how can one person perform both offer and acceptance? The answer is that the father's compassion elevates him to the status of two persons, so his single statement serves as both statements. This is an exception based on istihsan.

Key Terms
شفقت (shafaqah): Compassion and care; here it is the basis for treating the father as two persons legally.
ایجاب و قبول (ijab wa qabul): Offer and acceptance; the two essential components of a contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because pawn does not require offer and acceptance.
B) Because the father's compassion places him in the position of two persons.
C) Because the child's property belongs to the father.
D) Because the father can appoint an agent for acceptance.

Key Takeaway
The father's shafaqah creates a legal fiction of two persons, permitting him to contract with himself for the benefit of his minor child.

Father's Right to Pawn a Minor's Property from Himself: Ruling and Rationale
Ruling with proof on father's capacity to pawn minor's property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a father pawning his minor child's property from himself and explain the rationale based on the father's compassion (shafaqa).

Core Idea
A father's compassion allows him to act as both parties in a pawn contract, making it valid.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a unique case: a father pawning his minor child's property from himself. Normally, a contract requires two distinct parties for offer and acceptance. However, due to the father's complete compassion (shafaqa), Islamic law treats him as two persons in this context. This lesson explores the ruling, its proof, and an intra-Hanafi disagreement on a related matter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act? Pawning minor's property from himself or from certain others. The ruling: it is valid (jā'iz).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the father's shafaqa (compassion), which places him in the position of two persons.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does shafaqa prove validity? It allows the father to perform both ijab and qabul, which are normally needed from two separate parties.
4
Note the analogy
The ruling is analogous to the father selling the minor's property to himself, which is also valid.
5
Identify the ikhtilaf
There is a dispute between Imam Abu Yusuf and the two companions (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) regarding muqassa (offsetting) in sale, which extends to pawning.

کتاب الرهن
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۴ ہوگا اور ایسے ہی بیچ کے سلسلہ میں بائع کا وکیل اور رہن بیچ کی نظیر ہے اپنے انجام کے اعتبار سے ضمان کے واجب ہونے کی حیثیت سے۔ تشریح مشائخ کرام نے فرمایا کہ امام ابو یوسف اور طرفین کا اصل اختلاف بیع میں ہے اسی اختلاف کو رہن میں فٹ کیا گیا ہے مثلاً باپ یا وصی نے صغیر کا مال اپنے قرض خواہ کے ہاتھ فروخت کر دیا تو بیع جائز ہے اور مقاصہ ہو جائے گا یعنی دین کا بدل ہو جائیگا اور باپ یا وصی کے بچہ کیلئے اس کے مال کا ضامن ہو گا یہ طرفین کا مذہب ہے۔
امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ بیع جائز ہے مگر مقاصہ نہیں ہوگا بلکہ قرضخواہ کا قرض بدستور ہیگا اور شمن بچہ کے لئے ہوگا۔ اس طرح زید ے بکر کو اپنا گھوڑا بیچنے کا وکیل بنایا اتفاق سے اس نے وہ گھوڑا خالد کے ہاتھ فروخت کیا اور خالد کے ایک ہزار روپے زید پر قرض ہیں تو بیع جائز ہے اور مقاصہ ہو جائیگا یعنی زید پر جو قرض ہے یہ ثمن اس کا بدل ہو جائیگا طرفین کے نزدیک اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک
مقاصہ نہ ہو گا۔
بہر حال اصل اختلاف یہاں ہے مگر جب دیکھا کہ جیسے بیج کی صورت میں باپ یا وصی پر ضمان واجب ہوتا ہے ایسے ہی رہن کے اندر بھی ضمان واجب ہوتا ہے تو اس اختلاف کو رہن کے اندر بھی جاری کر دیا گیا اس کو مصنف نے فرمایا کہ انجام یعنی وجوب ضمان کے اعتبار سے رہن بیع کی نظیر ہے۔
باپ بچے کے مال کو اپنے پاس اور کسی دوسرے کے پاس رہن رکھ سکتا ہے
واذا رهن الاب من نفسه او من ابن له صغيرا وعبد له تاجر لا دين عليه جاز لان الاب لو فور شفقته انزل منزلة شخصين واقيمت عبارته مقام عبارتين في هذا العقد كما في بيعه مال الصغير من نفسه فتولي طرفي العقد
ترجمہ اور جبکہ باپ نے اپنے ہی پاس رہن رکھ لیا یا اپنے دوسرے چھوٹے بچہ کے پاس یا اپنے اس تاجر غلام کے پاس جس پر قرض نہیں ہے تو یہ جائز ہے اس لئے کہ باپ اپنی شفقت کے کمال کی وجہ سے دو شخصوں کے درجہ میں اتار لیا جائے گا اور اس کی عبارت اس عقد میں دو عبارتوں کے قائم مقام کر لی جائے گی جیسا کہ باپ کے بیچنے میں صغیر کے مال کو اپنے ہی ہاتھ تو باپ متولی ہو گا عقد کی دونوں طرفوں کا ( ایجاب قبول کا ) ۔
تشریح اگر باپ نے بچہ کے مال کو اپنے پاس رہن رکھا یا ایسے افراد کے پاس جو اسی کے نفس کے درجہ میں ہیں مثالاً اپنے دوسرے چھوٹے بچہ کے پاس یا اپنے ایسے غلام تاجر کے پاس جس کے اوپر قرض نہ ہو تو یہ جائز ہے۔ سوال اس پر سوال پیدا ہوا کہ رہن کے لئے تو ایجاب و قبول چاہئیں اگر اس کے قول کو ایجاب مانیں تو قبول ندار داور اگر قبول ما نہیں تو ایجاب ندار دالہذا یہ رہن صیح نہ ہونا چاہیے؟ جواب بات تو یونہی ہے مگر ہم نے دیکھا کہ باپ میں کامل شفقت ہے اس لئے اس کو دو آدمیوں کے درجہ میں اتارلیا گیا ہے اور اس کے قول کو دو عبارتوں کے درجہ میں اتار لیا گیا ہے جیسے اگر باپ بچہ کے مال کو خود خریدے تو جائز ہے یہاں بھی وہ تنہا ایجاب قبول کا متولی ہو جاتا ہے تو رہن میں بھی ایسے ہی ہوگا۔
Book of Pawning. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume 14 - And similarly, in the series of sale, the seller's agent and pawning are analogous to sale in terms of the consequence, i.e., the obligation of guarantee. Explanation: The senior scholars said that the original difference between Imam Abu Yusuf and the two parties (the two companions) is in sale; this difference has been applied to pawning. For example, if a father or guardian sold the property of a minor to his own creditor, the sale is valid and muqassa (offset) will occur, meaning it will become a substitute for the debt, and the father or guardian will be guarantor for the child's property. This is the school of the two parties. Imam Abu Yusuf said: The sale is valid but muqassa will not occur; rather, the creditor's debt remains as is, and the price is for the child. Similarly, if Zaid made Bakr his agent to sell his horse, and he sold that horse to Khalid, and Khalid owes one thousand rupees to Zaid, then the sale is valid and muqassa will occur according to the two parties, but Imam Abu Yusuf says muqassa will not occur. In any case, the original difference is here. But when it was seen that just as in the case of sale, guarantee is obligatory upon the father or guardian, similarly in pawning, guarantee becomes obligatory, so this difference was also applied in pawning. The author said: In terms of the consequence, i.e., the obligation of guarantee, pawning is analogous to sale. A father can pawn the child's property from himself and from another. And when the father pawns from himself, or from his minor son, or from his trading slave who has no debt upon him, it is permissible, because the father, due to the perfection of his compassion, is placed in the position of two persons, and his statement is made to stand in place of two statements in this contract, just as in his sale of the minor's property to himself, he undertakes both sides of the contract. Translation: And when the father pawns from himself, or from his other minor child, or from his trading slave who has no debt upon him, then it is permissible. Because the father, due to the perfection of his compassion, is placed in the position of two persons, and his statement is made to stand in place of two statements in this contract, just as in the father's selling of the minor's property to himself, he undertakes both sides of the contract (ijab and qabul). Explanation: If the father pawned the child's property from himself, or from those who are in the same position as himself, for example, from his other minor child, or from his trading slave who has no debt upon him, then it is permissible. A question arose: For pawning, ijab and qabul are required. If we consider his statement as ijab, then there is no qabul; and if we consider it as qabul, then there is no ijab. Therefore, this pawn should not be valid? The answer is that it is so, but we see that the father has complete compassion, so he is placed in the position of two men, and his statement is placed in the position of two statements. Just as if the father purchases the child's property himself, it is valid; here too, he alone undertakes ijab and qabul, so it will be the same in pawning.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding a father's capacity to pawn his minor child's property. The ruling is that it is valid (jā'iz) for a father to pawn the property of his minor child from himself, from another minor child, or from his trading slave who has no debt. The proof lies in the father's complete compassion (shafaqa), which allows him to be treated as two persons in the contract, both as the pledger and the pledgee. This is analogous to the case where a father sells the minor's property to himself, which is also valid. The commentary addresses a potential objection: how can a single person perform both ijab and qabul? The answer is that due to the father's shafaqa, his single utterance is considered as two, eliminating the need for two separate parties. The passage also discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Yusuf differs from the two companions (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding muqassa (offsetting) in sale, and this difference is applied to pawning as well. According to the 'tarafain', when a father sells the minor's property to a creditor, the price offsets the debt, and the father becomes guarantor. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that the sale is valid but no offset occurs; the debt remains and the price belongs to the minor. This difference is extended to pawning based on the similarity in the obligation of daman (guarantee).

Key Terms
رہن (rahn): A contract whereby property is given as security for a debt, with the property remaining in the possession of the creditor or a trustee.
شفقت (shafaqa): Complete compassion and affection, specifically the natural love a father has for his child, which justifies treating him as two persons in certain contracts.
ایجاب و قبول (ijab wa qabul): Offer and acceptance, the two essential components of a contract. Normally required from two separate parties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the father owns the property and can do as he wishes.
B) Because the father's complete compassion allows him to be treated as two persons, fulfilling both offer and acceptance.
C) Because the minor child has given explicit permission.
D) Because pawning does not require offer and acceptance.

Key Takeaway
A father can pawn his minor child's property from himself because his complete compassion (shafaqa) allows him to act as both parties in the contract.

A Wasi Cannot Pawn the Orphan's Property from Himself
Ruling and reasoning for why a wasi cannot pawn from himself

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a wasi cannot pawn from himself or certain related parties, and explain the two reasons: (1) one person cannot undertake both sides of the pawn contract, and (2) the wasi lacks the full compassion that would allow an exception like the father.

Core Idea
A wasi cannot pawn from himself because he is a mere agent with deficient compassion—he cannot act as two parties.

The pawn contract (rahn) requires two distinct parties: a pledgor and a pledgee. For a father pawning from himself, Hanafi law makes a special exception due to his complete compassion. But what about a wasi (guardian) who manages an orphan's property? This lesson examines why the wasi cannot benefit from that exception, and explores the boundaries of the wasi's authority in pawn transactions.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its scope
Identify the four specific scenarios that are impermissible for the wasi: (1) pawning from himself, (2) pawning from his minor son, (3) pawning from his trading slave without debt, and (4) pawning his own property with the orphan in exchange for a right due from him. The core principle: a wasi cannot do what a father can because the wasi is a mere agent (wakīl muḍ).
2
Analyze the first reason: one person cannot handle both sides
The text argues that just as in sale, a single person cannot perform both ijāb (offer) and qabūl (acceptance) in a pawn contract. The wasi, acting on behalf of the orphan, would be both the pledgor and the pledgee if he pawns from himself. This is invalid because a contract requires two distinct parties.
This is a general contractual principle; the father is an exception due to special compassion.
3
Examine the second reason: deficient compassion
The father's exception is specific to him because of his complete shafaqa (compassion). The wasi's compassion is deficient (qāṣir al-shafaqa), so he cannot be equated to the father. Therefore, the exceptional ruling that allows the father to pawn from himself does not extend to the wasi.
The wasi's authority is limited; he is merely an agent, not a full guardian like the father.
4
Distinguish cases where pawning is allowed
The wasi may pawn from an adult son, his own father, or a trading slave with debt because he has no wilayah (authority) over them. These are independent third parties, so the contract has two distinct parties. This contrasts with the minor child or slave without debt, over whom the wasi has authority.
The key is whether the wasi has authority over the other party. If yes, it is like pawning from himself; if no, it is permissible.
5
Contrast with an agent in sale
In sale, an agent is suspected (tuhmah) of favoritism when selling to close relatives, so such sales are restricted. In pawn, there is no such suspicion because pawn does not transfer ownership; it merely secures a debt. Therefore, the wasi's limited authority in pawn is not lifted by tuhmah concerns.
This explains why the agent for sale is treated more strictly in related-party transactions than the wasi in pawn.

ہاں آدمی کو اپنے بالغ لڑکے پر اور اپنے باپ پر اور اس غلام تاجر پر جس پر قرض ہو ولایت نہیں ہے لہذا ان کے پاس رہن رکھنا وصی کیلئے بھی جائز ہوگا ،صرف رہن رکھنا ہی ان کے پاس جائز ہوگا اگر زید نے بکر کو اپنا سامان بیچنے کا وکیل بنادیا اور اس نے وہ سامان اپنے بالغ بیٹے یا اپنے باپ یا اپنے اس غلام کے ہاتھ جس پر قرض ہے فروخت کیا تو جائز نہیں کیونکہ یہاں اس بیج میں تہمت ہے كمالا يخفى اور رہن میں کوئی تہمت نہیں کیونکہ رہن کا تو ایک ہی حکم ہے خواہ مرتہن کوئی بھی ہو ید استیفاء کا ثبوت اور مرہون کا مضمون ہونا اس لئے کہ تہمت نہیں ہے۔
Can the wasi pawn from himself or not? And if the wasi pawns from himself, or from these two (his minor child or trading slave), or pawns his own property with the orphan in exchange for a right that the orphan has upon him, it is not permissible, because the wasi is a mere agent, and one person cannot undertake both sides of the contract in pawn, just as he cannot undertake both in sale. And he is deficient in compassion, so one does not deviate from the reality in his case by attaching him to the father. And pawning from his minor son and his trading slave who has no debt upon him is like pawning from himself, unlike his adult son, his father, and his slave who has debt, because he has no authority over them. Unlike an agent for sale when he sells to these, because he is suspect therein, but there is no suspicion in pawn because it has a single ruling. Translation: And if the wasi pawned the property of the minor from himself, or from these two (his other child or the mentioned slave), or the wasi pawned his own property with the orphan in exchange for a right that the orphan has upon him, then it is not permissible, because the wasi is a mere agent, and one person cannot undertake both sides of the contract in pawn, just as one person cannot undertake both in sale. And the wasi is deficient in compassion, so one does not deviate from the reality in his case by attaching him to the father. And pawning from his minor son and his trading slave who has no debt is like pawning from himself, unlike his adult son, his father, and his slave who has debt, because he has no authority over them. Unlike an agent for sale when he sells to these, because he is suspect therein, but there is no suspicion in pawn because it has a single ruling. Explanation: This pawning from himself is permissible for the father and not permissible for the wasi. Similarly, if the wasi pawns with the orphan in exchange for a right that the orphan has upon him, that too is not permissible. In summary, these four forms are impermissible for the wasi, because the principle has been established that a single person cannot undertake both ijab and qabul neither in sale nor in pawn. And the father's ruling, due to the abundance of compassion, is contrary to analogy and is specific to him. The wasi cannot be analogized to him because the wasi is deficient in compassion, so deviation from reality to attach him to the father is not permissible. And a minor child and a trading slave without debt, since the wasi has authority over them, they are considered to be in the same position as himself. Yes, a person has no authority over his adult son, his father, and his trading slave with debt. Therefore, pawning from these is permissible for the wasi as well. However, only pawning from them is permissible. If Zaid made Bakr his agent to sell his goods, and he sold those goods to his adult son, or his father, or his slave with debt, then it is not permissible because there is suspicion in this sale, as is clear. And in pawn, there is no suspicion because pawn has only one ruling, whether the pledgee is anyone, due to the establishment of the right of recovery and the property being held as security, because there is no suspicion.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling that a wasi (guardian/executor) cannot pawn the property of an orphan from himself or from certain parties, unlike a father. The reason is that the wasi is a mere agent (wakīl muḍ) with limited compassion (qasir al-shafaqa), so he cannot be treated as two persons in a contract. The the father's exceptional capacity is specific to him due to his complete shafaqa. The passage lists four impermissible scenarios: (1) pawning from himself, (2) pawning from his minor son (the orphan's sibling), (3) pawning from his trading slave without debt, and (4) pawning his own property with the orphan in exchange for a right. All are invalid because the wasi alone cannot perform both ijab and qabul. However, pawning from an adult son, the wasi's own father, or a slave with debt is permissible because the wasi has no authority over them, so they are independent third parties. The passage also distinguishes between an agent for sale and a wasi in pawn: in sale, the agent is suspected of favoritism, so selling to close relatives is restricted; but in pawn, there is no such suspicion because pawn has a single ruling (the property is merely security, not transferred).

Key Terms
وصی (wasi): A guardian or executor appointed to manage the affairs of an orphan, with limited authority compared to a father.
تہمت (tuhmah): Suspicion of partiality or favoritism, especially in transactions where an agent might favor his own relatives.
ولایت (wilayah): Legal authority or guardianship over another person, enabling one to act on their behalf in contracts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because pawning from oneself is always invalid regardless of the person.
D) Because the orphan has not given permission.

Key Takeaway
A wasi cannot pawn from himself or from those under his authority because he is a mere agent with deficient compassion, and only a father's complete compassion justifies an exceptional ruling.

Father Pledging Child's Property: The Child's Right of Recourse
Ruling with analogical reasoning on father's pledge of child's property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a father pledges his child's property for his own debt and explain the qiyas (analogical reasoning) that supports the child's right of recourse.

Core Idea
A child compelled to pay his father's debt to save his own property can recover from the father.

This passage addresses a subtle issue in rahn (pledge) where a father uses his minor child's property as collateral for his own debt. The Hanafi school, using istihsan and qiyas, grants the child the right to recover the amount paid to redeem the property, based on necessity and analogy to the mu'ir al-rahn (lender of a pledge). Understanding this ruling clarifies the limits of parental authority over a child's property and the principle of preventing loss.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the ruling
Identify the act: father pledges child's property for his own debt; child pays off the debt to redeem the property. The ruling is that the child can recover the amount paid from the father's property.
The father's action is not automatically invalid; the child's recourse is established by qiyas.
2
Identify the illa (effective cause)
The child is compelled (mudtar) to pay in order to preserve his own property (ihya' milkih). This compulsion is the key reason justifying recourse.
Without this compulsion, the payment might be considered voluntary and non-recoverable.
3
Trace the qiyas
The asl (original case) is the mu'ir al-rahn: a person who lends his property to another to be pledged, and then the borrower pays the debt to retrieve it. In that case, the borrower can recover from the lender. The far' (new case) is the child paying off the father's debt. The illa is compulsion to preserve property. The hukm (ruling) is transferred: the child can recover.
This is qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) based on istihsan (juristic preference) to avoid loss.
4
Consider the objection and response
Objection: The father did not command the child to pay. Response: The child's compulsion overrides the lack of command – necessity justifies recourse.
This rebuttal is crucial to distinguish from a gift or voluntary payment.
5
Apply the same rule if the pledge perishes
Even if the pledge is destroyed before the child redeems it, the father's debt is discharged, and the child still has recourse because the father effectively used the child's property to pay his debt.
This extends the ruling to a situation where the child did not actively pay but suffered loss.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو كان الاب رهنه لنفسه فقضاه الابن رجع به فى مال الاب لانه مضطر فيه لحاجته الى احياء ملکه فاشبه معير الرهن وکذا اذا هلک قبل ان يفتكه لان الاب يصير قاضيا دينه بماله فله ان يرجع عليه

ترجمہ: اور اگر باپ نے اس کو اپنے لئے رہن رکھا ہو پس بیٹے نے اس کو (باپ کے قرض کو) ادا کر دیا تو وہ اس کے سلسلہ میں باپ کے مال میں رجوع کریگا اس لئے کہ بیٹا اس ادا میں مجبور ہے اس کے محتاج ہونے کی وجہ سے اپنی ملک کے احیاء کی جانب تو یہ معیر رہن کے مشابہ ہو گیا اور ایسے ہی جبکہ رہن ہلاک ہو جائے اس کو چھڑانے سے پہلے ہی اس لئے کہ باپ نے اپنے قرض کو اس کے مال سے ادا کیا ہے تو اس کو باپ پر رجوع کا حق ہے۔

تشریح: باپ نے بچہ کے سامان کو اپنے قرض میں رہن رکھا تھا بیٹے نے مرتبہن کا وہ قرض دے کر اپنا سامان لے لیا تو اس نے جتنا قرض ادا کیا ہے اتنا مال باپ کے مال میں سے لینے کا حق ہے۔

سوال: اس کو باپ نے کب حکم دیا ہے کہ تو میرا قرض ادا کر لہٰذا جائز نہ ہونا چاہیے؟
جواب: باپ نے تو حکم نہیں کیا لیکن یہ اپنے سامان کی حفاظت پر مجبور تھا اس لئے اس کو رجوع کا حق ہوگا۔

سوال: کیا اس کی کوئی نظیر پیش کی جاسکتی ہے؟
جواب: زید نے بکر سے قرض مانگا بکر کے پاس روپے نہیں تھے اس نے اپنی قیمتی گھڑی اس کو دیدی کہ اس کو رہن رکھ کر قرض لے کر اپنا کام چلاؤ پھر بکر نے اپنی گھڑی مرتہن کو رقم دے کر چھڑا لی تو بکر نے جو رقم مرتہن کے حوالہ کی ہے اس کو زید سے وصول کرے گا اسی طرح یہ بھی ہوگا اور اگر اس سے پہلے بیٹا مرہون کو چھڑانے نہیں پایا تھا کہ مرہون مرتہن کے پاس ہلاک ہو گیا جس سے باپ کا قرض ساقط ہو گیا تو بیٹے کو حق ہو گا کہ وہ قرض کی مقدار کے مطابق باپ کے مال سے وصول کرے۔
And if the father pledged it for his own debt, then the son paid it off, he (the son) will have recourse to the father's property, because he is compelled in this (payment) due to his need to revive his property, so it resembles the lender of a pledge (mu'ir al-rahn). Likewise if it perishes before he redeems it, because the father has paid off his debt with his (the son's) property, so he has the right to recourse against him. Translation: And if the father pledged it for himself, then the son paid it (the father's debt), he will have recourse to the father's property because the son is compelled in this payment due to his need to revive his ownership, so it resembles the lender of a pledge. And likewise if the pledge perishes before he redeems it, because the father paid off his debt with his (the son's) property, so he has the right to recourse against the father. Commentary: The father had pledged the child's goods for his own debt; the son paid off the creditor's debt and took back his goods; he has the right to take from the father's property the amount he paid. Question: The father did not command him to pay his debt, so it should not be permissible? Answer: The father did not command, but he was compelled to protect his property, so he has the right of recourse. Question: Can an analogy be presented? Answer: Zayd borrowed from Bakr; Bakr had no money, so he gave his valuable watch to Zayd to pledge it and borrow for his need; then Bakr paid the creditor and redeemed his watch; Bakr can recover the amount from Zayd. Similarly here. And if before the son could redeem it the pledge perished with the creditor, thereby discharging the father's debt, then the son has the right to recover the amount of the debt from the father's property.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof by analogy (qiyas). It states the Hanafi position: if a father pledges his minor child's property as collateral for his own debt, and the child (or his guardian) later pays off the debt to redeem the property, the child has the right to recover the amount paid from the father's property. The reasoning is that the child is compelled to pay to preserve his own property (since the collateral belongs to him), so it is analogous to the case of a person who lends a pledge to someone (mu'ir al-rahn) — the lender can recover from the borrower if he pays the debt to retrieve his property. The same rule applies if the pledge perishes before redemption: the father's debt is discharged, but the child still has recourse against the father because the father effectively used the child's property to pay his debt. The text then addresses a potential objection: the father did not command the child to pay, so it might seem irregular. The answer is that the child's compulsion to save his property justifies recourse. A further analogy is provided: if someone borrows money from another and gives him a valuable item to pledge for the loan, and the borrower later pays off the loan to retrieve his item, he can recover the amount from the lender. This clarifies the underlying principle with a practical example.

Key Terms
رہن (rahn): A contract where property is held as security for a debt
معیر الرہن (mu'ir al-rahn): One who lends his own property to another to be used as a pledge
اضطرار (idhtirar): Compulsion or necessity that overrides normal rules

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this lesson, what justifies the child's right to recover from the father after paying off the father's debt to redeem his own property?
A) The father's explicit command to the child to pay the debt.
B) The child's compulsion to preserve his property (idhtirar).
C) The child's kindness in helping his father.
D) The pledge being worth more than the debt.

Key Takeaway
When a father pledges his child's property for his own debt, the child can recover the amount paid to redeem it from the father, based on the analogy to mu'ir al-rahn and the principle of compulsion to prevent loss.

Father Pledging Child's Property for Both Debts
Ruling on father pledging child's property for both debts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a father pledging his child's property for both his own and the child's debt, and explain the father's liability if the pledge perishes.

Core Idea
A pledge for both debts is valid; liability is proportional to the father's own debt.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in Hanafi fiqh where a father, who has lawful authority over his minor child's property, uses that property as collateral for both his own debt and the child's debt. The ruling clarifies not only the permissibility of such a combined pledge but also the important consequence if the pledged property perishes: the father must compensate the child only for the portion used to pay his own debt. We will also see how this ruling extends to the executor and grandfather.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its permissibility
Recognize that the father is pledging the child's property for two distinct debts: his own and the child's. Note that each individual pledge is permissible, and combining them does not change the ruling.
The Hanafi position is that combining two permissible acts does not render the combined act impermissible.
2
Analyze the liability condition
If the pledged property perishes, the father is liable for his portion only. Understand why: he used the child's property to pay off his own debt, so he must compensate the child for that amount.
The father is not liable for the child's portion of the debt because that portion was already a debt on the child.
3
Extend the ruling to executor and grandfather
The same rule applies to the father's executor (wasi) and to the paternal grandfather (jadd) when the father is absent or has no executor. This shows consistency in Hanafi rulings on guardianship of property.
The grandfather's authority is secondary: he steps in only when the father or his executor is absent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو رهنه بدين على نفسه وبدين على الصغير جاز لاشتماله على امرين جائزين فان هلک ضمن الاب حصته من ذالك للولد لا يفائه دينه من ماله بهذا المقدار و کذالک الوصى وکذالک الجداب الاب اذالم يكن الاب او وصى الاب

ترجمہ: اور اگر باپ نے صغیر کے مال کو رہن رکھا اپنے اوپر قرض کے بدلہ اور صغیر کے اوپر قرض کے بدلہ تو جائز ہے اس کے مشتمل ہونے کی وجہ سے دو جائز چیزوں پر پس اگر مرہون کی ہلاکت ہو جائے تو باپ اس رہن میں سے اپنے حصہ کے بقدر بچہ کے لئے ضامن ہو گا باپ کے ادا کرنے کی وجہ سے اپنے قرض کو بچہ کے مال سے اس مقدار کے مطابق اور ایسے ہی وصی ہے اور دادا جبکہ باپ یا باپ کا وصی نہ ہو۔

تشریح: اگر باپ پر سو روپے اور بچہ پر سو روپے قرض تھا باپ نے ان دونوں کے بدلہ بچہ کا سامان رہن رکھ دیا تو جائز ہے کیونکہ اگر ان دونوں میں سے کوئی ایک انفراداً ہوتا تو جائز تھا تو اب بھی جائز ہوگا لیکن اگر مرہون ہلاک ہو جائے تو باپ پر اپنے حصہ کے بقدر ضمان واجب ہوگا نہ کہ کل کا کیونکہ اس نے اس قدر بچہ کے مال سے اپنا قرض ادا کیا ہے، پھر ان مسائل مذکورہ میں باپ کا وصی یا دادا مثل باپ کے ہے جبکہ باپ نہ ہو اور دادا جبکہ باپ یا اس کا وصی نہ ہو۔
And if he pledged it for a debt upon himself and a debt upon the minor, it is permissible because it includes two permissible matters. Then if it perishes, the father guarantees his portion from that to the child, because he paid off his debt from the child's property by this amount. And likewise the executor, and likewise the grandfather when there is no father or executor of the father. Translation: And if the father pledged the minor's property for a debt on himself and a debt on the minor, it is permissible because it includes two permissible matters. So if the pledge perishes, the father is liable for his share to the child, because he paid off his debt from the child's property in that amount. And similarly the executor, and similarly the grandfather when there is no father or father's executor. Commentary: If the father owed 100 rupees and the child owed 100 rupees, and the father pledged the child's goods for both debts, it is permissible because each individually is permissible. But if the pledge perishes, the father is liable only for his portion, not the whole, because he used the child's property to pay off his own debt to that extent. Then in these mentioned issues, the father's executor or grandfather is like the father when the father is absent, and the grandfather when the father or his executor is absent.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage states a ruling: a father may pledge his child's property as collateral for both his own debt and the child's debt. This is valid because each component (pledging for a valid debt) is individually permissible. However, if the collateral perishes while in the creditor's possession, the father becomes liable to compensate the child only for his own portion of the debt (the amount that was for his own debt). This is because the father effectively used the child's property to pay off his own debt. The same rule applies to the executor (wasi) of the father and to the paternal grandfather (jadd) when the father is absent or has no executor. The grandfather's authority is secondary. The ruling is straightforward: the pledge is valid, and liability is proportional.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for loss or damage
وصی (wasi): Executor appointed by father to manage child's affairs

Key Takeaway
A father may pledge his child's property for both debts, but if the pledge perishes, he must compensate the child only for his own debt portion.

Executor Borrowing Pledged Item: Liability Depends on Purpose
Ruling on executor borrowing pledged item and liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the executor's liability when borrowing a pledged item for the orphan's need versus his own need, applying the Hanafi principle of qiyas to the orphan's own act.

Core Idea
Executor borrowing for orphan's need = no liability; for own need = liability.

This lesson examines a nuanced scenario in the law of pledge (rahn): an executor (wasi) who has pledged the orphan's goods for a debt later borrows the pledged item back. If the item perishes in his hands, who bears the loss? The Hanafi ruling hinges on the purpose of the borrowing, illustrating the scope of the executor's authority and the use of qiyas. We will walk through the text of Al-Hidayah, identify the two scenarios, and understand the legal reasoning behind the different outcomes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and sequence
Understand the initial transaction: executor takes a debt for the orphan, pledges the orphan's goods, creditor takes possession. Then executor borrows back the pledged item (isti'arah) for the orphan's need.
The borrowing is not a new contract but a return of possession for temporary use.
2
Separate the two scenarios
The passage distinguishes two situations: (1) borrowing for the orphan's need, (2) borrowing for the executor's own need. The ruling differs.
The second scenario is introduced later in the text as a contrast.
3
Apply the analogy (qiyas)
The text says 'the executor's act is like the orphan's own act after puberty'. Treat the executor's borrowing for the orphan's need as if the orphan himself did it. If the orphan had done it, the loss would be on the orphan and the debt remains. So here, the loss is on the orphan and the executor is not liable.
The asl (original case) is the orphan acting for himself; the far' is the executor acting for the orphan.
4
Determine liability in the second scenario
If the executor borrows for his own need, he exceeds his authority (wilayah). He is liable (daman) to the orphan for the value of the item, because he had no right to use it for himself.
The cause (illa) is the purpose of the borrowing: benefit of orphan vs. benefit of executor.
5
Note the practical outcome
In the first scenario, the debt is demanded from the executor (as he is the borrower) but he can recover the amount from the orphan because the orphan benefited. The pledge is void since the item perished.
This ensures the creditor is paid while the orphan bears ultimate loss, consistent with the benefit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو رهن الوصى متاعاً لليتيم في دين استدائه عليه وقبض المرتهن ثم استعاره الوصى لحاجة اليتيم فضاع في يد الوصي فانه خرج من الرهن وهلك من مال اليتيم لان فعل الوصى كفعله بنفسه بعد البلوغ لانه استعاره لحاجة الصبي والحكم فيه هذا على ما نبينه ان شاء الله تعالى

ترجمہ: اور اگر وصی نے یتیم کے سامان کو رہن رکھا اس قرض کے بدلہ میں جو اس نے یتیم کے لئے قرض لیا تھا اور مرتہن نے (مرہون پر) قبضہ کر لیا پھر وصی نے مرہون کو یتیم کی ضرورت کے لئے مستعار لے لیا پس مرہون وصی کے قبضہ میں ضائع ہو گیا تو مرہون رہن سے خارج ہو گیا اور یتیم کا مال ہلاک ہوا اس لئے کہ وصی کا فعل بلوغ کے بعد یتیم کے فعل کے مثل ہے اس لئے کہ وصی کا فعل بچہ کی ضرورت کے لئے عاریت لینا ہے اور اس میں یہی حکم ہے اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو ہم انشاء اللہ بیان کریں گے۔

تشریح: وصی نے بچہ کے لئے قرض لے کر بچہ کا سامان رہن رکھا اور پھر بچہ کی ضرورت کیلئے مرہون کو مستعار لے لیا اتفاقاً مرہون وصی کے پاس ہلاک ہو گیا تو اب یہ رہن نہیں رہا اور وصی پر کوئی ضمان نہ ہوگا بلکہ یہ بچہ کا مال ہلاک ہوا کیونکہ وصی کا فعل بچہ کے فعل کے مثل ہے اور اگر بچہ بڑا ہوکر یہ کام کرتا تو وہاں بھی یہی حکم ہوگا کہ قرض خواہ کا قرض اس کے اوپر بدستور برقرار ہے لہذا یہ بھی ایسا ہی ہوگا۔

صورت مذکورہ میں مرتہن کا قرض کس پر ہے
والمال دين على الوصى معناه هو المطالب به ثم يرجع بذلک علی الصبى لانه غير متعد في هذه الاستعارة اذ هى لحاجة الصبى ولو استعاره لحاجة نفسه ضمنه للصبى لانه متعد اذ ليس له ولاية الاستعمال في حاجة نفسه

ترجمہ: اور مال وصی کے اوپر قرض ہوگا اس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ وصی ہی سے اس کا مطالبہ کیا جائے گا پھر وہی اس کے سلسلہ میں بچہ پر رجوع کریگا اس لئے کہ وہ اسے مستعار لینے میں زیادتی کرنے والا نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ یہ استعارہ بچہ کی ضرورت کے لئے ہے اور اگر وصی نے اس کو اپنی ضرورت کے لئے مستعار لیا بچہ کے لئے اس کا ضامن ہو گا اس لئے کہ وصی زیادتی کرنے والا ہے اس لئے کہ اس کو اپنی ضرورت میں استعمال کی ولایت نہیں ہے۔
And if the executor pledges the orphan's goods for a debt he took on behalf of the orphan, and the creditor takes possession, then the executor borrows the pledged item for the orphan's need, and it is lost in the executor's hand, then it exits from the pledge and perishes from the orphan's property, because the executor's act is like his own act after puberty, since he borrowed for the child's need. The ruling in this is as we will explain, God willing. Translation: And if the executor pledges the orphan's goods for the debt which he took for the orphan, and the creditor takes possession, then the executor borrows the pledged item for the orphan's need, and it is lost in the executor's hand, then the pledge is void and the loss is from the orphan's property, because the executor's act is like the child's act after attaining majority, since he borrowed for the child's need. The ruling is as we will explain. Commentary: The executor borrowed for the child and pledged the child's goods, then borrowed the pledged item back for the child's need; it was accidentally lost in the executor's hands. Thus it is no longer a pledge, and the executor is not liable; rather, the child's property is lost, because the executor's act is like the child's act. If the child had done this after becoming major, the same ruling would apply: the creditor's debt remains on him. So here too the same. 

In the mentioned case, on whom is the creditor's debt? 
And the debt is upon the executor; meaning he is demanded for it, then he recovers it from the child, because he has not transgressed in this borrowing, since it was for the child's need. And if he borrowed for his own need, he would be liable to the child, because he transgressed, since he has no authority to use it for his own need.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling and its underlying reasoning. The scenario: an executor (wasi) takes a loan for the orphan, pledging the orphan's goods as collateral. The creditor takes possession. Later, the executor borrows back the pledged item (istihara) for the orphan's need. If the item is lost in the executor's possession, the ruling is: the item exits from the pledge (i.e., the pledge is terminated), and the loss is borne by the orphan's property (i.e., the orphan loses the item, and the debt remains). The executor is not liable. The reason given is that the executor's act is analogous to the act of the orphan himself after he reaches puberty. Since the borrowing was for the orphan's benefit, it is as if the orphan did it. Consequently, the debt is owed by the executor (as the borrower) but he can recover the amount from the orphan (since the orphan benefited). However, if the executor had borrowed the pledged item for his own personal need, he would be liable (daman) to the orphan because he exceeded his authority; he has no authority to use the orphan's property for his own benefit. This highlights the distinction based on the purpose of borrowing: for the orphan's need → no liability; for executor's own need → liability.

Key Terms
استعارہ (isti'arah): Borrowing for use without compensation
ولایت (wilayah): Legal authority to act on behalf of another

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where an executor borrows a pledged item for the orphan's need and it perishes, the executor:
A) Is liable to the orphan for the value.
B) Is not liable, and the loss is on the orphan.
C) Is liable only if he was negligent.
D) Must return the item to the creditor.

Key Takeaway
An executor borrowing a pledged item for the orphan's need results in no personal liability; borrowing for his own need makes him liable, highlighting the importance of purpose and authority in Hanafi fiqh.
