تشریح یہ صاحبین کی دلیل ہے کہ خلاف جنس کے ساتھ ضمان واجب کر کے اس کو مر ہون کی جگہ کیوں رکھا جائیگا اور پھر یوں کیوں رکھا جائیگا اور پھر یوں کیوں حکم ہوگا کہ جب راہن قرض ادا کر دیگا تو اس کا قائم مقام مرہون کا مالک بھے گا۔
تو انہوں نے کہا کہ اس میں مختلف احتمالات تھے مگر سب باطل نکلے اس لئے ہم نے یہی صورت اختیار کی کیونکہ وزن کا اعتبار کرنے سے مرتہن کا نقصان ہے کیسے؟ اس لئے کہ لوٹا اگر چہ دس درہم وزن کا ہے مگر قیمت تو اس کی آٹھ روپے ہے تو ظاہر ہے کہ اس میں مرتہن کا نقصان ہے اس لئے یہ صورت تو باطل ہوئی۔ اور اگر قیمت کا اعتبار کرتے ہیں کہ مثلاً آٹھ روپے مرتبہن نے وصول پائے لوٹے کی قیمت سے اور راہن دو روپے اور دیدے تو یہ ربوا اور سود ہے دونوں صورتیں باطل ہوئیں تو ضمان مذکور کا قول اختیار کیا۔
سوال خیر چلو مگر یہ تو بتا ہے کہ ضمان مذکور خلاف جنس سے کیوں واجب ہے؟ جواب ... چونکہ دوسری اگر دس درہم ہی رکھی جائیں تو اس میں یہ احتمال تھا کہ شاید مرتہن نے بس اپنا حق وصول کر لیا ہے اس لئے مرہون پر قبضہ کو مضبوط کرنے کے لئے خلاف جنس کو رکھا گیا تو سابق احتمال ہی ختم ہو گیا ۔ یہ صاحبین کی دلیل تھی ۔ آگے امام صاحب کی دلیل آ رہی ہے۔
امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل
وله ان الجودة ساقطة العبرة فى الاموال الربوية عند المقابلة بجنسها واستيفاء الجيد بالردى جائز كما اذاتجوز به وقد حصل الاستيفاء بالاجماع ولهذا يحتاج الى نقضه ولا يمكن نقضه بايجاب الضمان لانه لا بدله من مطالب ومطالب وكذا الانسان لا يضمن ملك نفسه وبتعذر التضمين يتعذر النقض
ترجمہ اور ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جودت اموال ربویہ میں اپنے جنس کے ساتھ مقابلہ کے وقت ساقط الاعتبار ہے اور عمدہ کو وصول کر لینا ردی کے بدلہ جائز ہے جیسا کہ جبکہ اس کے ساتھ چشم پوشی کی ہو اور بالا جماع استیفاء حاصل ہو گیا اسی وجہ سے اس کو توڑنے کی حاجت پیش آئی ہے اور ضمان واجب کر کے اس کو توڑنا ممکن نہیں اس لئے کہ ضمان کے لئے مطالب اور مطالب کا ہونا ضروری ہے اور ایسے ہی
كتاب الرهن
۲۳۸
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۴
انسان اپنی ملک کا ضامن نہیں ہوتا اور تضمین کے متعذر ہونے کی وجہ سے استیفاء کوتوڑ نامتعذ رہو گیا۔ تشریح یہ امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل ہے کہ جن اموال میں ربوا حق ہو سکتا ہے ان میں جنس کے ساتھ مقابلہ کے وقت جودت ساقط الا عتبار ہے ورنہ ر ہوا پیدا ہو جائیگا۔
اور اگر بالفرض کوٹے کی قیمت کم مان لیں مگر وزن تو اس کا پورا دس درہم ہے بس اتنی بات ہوئی کہ قرض ( درہم ) عمدہ ہیں اور مرہون (ابریق ) ردی ہے اور مرتبین نے عمدہ کے عوض ردی کو وصول کیا ہے تو یہ جائز ہے جیسا کہ بدل صرف یا بیع سلم میں اگر عمدہ دراہم کئے بجائے چشم پوشی کے طور پر کھوٹے لئے تو جائز ہے اور حق ادا ہو گیا۔ بس اب تو یہاں یہ دیکھنے کی ضرورت باقی رہ گئی کہ مرتبہن نے اپنا حق پایا ہے یا نہیں تو ہم نے جب غور کیا تو معلوم ہوا کہ مرتہن کے پاس جب مرہون ہلاک ہو جاتا ہے تو اس کو وصول پانے والا شمار کیا جاتا ہے لہذا معلوم ہوا کہ مرتبہن نے اپنا حق وصول پایا۔ بلکہ یہاں وصولیابی حق بالا جماع حاصل ہو چکی ہے۔
سوال صاحبین کے نزدیک وصولیابی نہیں ہوئی تو آپ نے بالا جماع کیسے کہدیا؟ جواب . بالا جماع وصولیابی حاصل ہو چکی ہے اسی وجہ سے تو صاحبین کو قبضہ توڑنے کی حاجت پیش آتی ہے کیونکہ قبضہ مرہون قبضہ استیفاء ہے لہذا مر تہن کا وصول و استیفاء پایا گیا۔ بہر حال صاحبین کا یہ فرمان کہ وصول کو توڑ دیا جائیگا یہ اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ وصول حاصل ہو چکا ہے اب رہی یہ بات کہ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ وصول تو ڑ دیا جائیگا تو یہ غور طلب ہے کیونکہ اس وصول کو توڑنا مرتہن پر ضمان واجب کرنے کے لئے ایک مطالب چاہیے اور یہاں کوئی مطالب نہیں ہے لہذا نہ ضمان واجب ہوگا اور نہ وصول ٹو میگا نہ رہے بانس اور نہ بجے بانسری۔ رہی یہ بات کہ مطالب نہیں ہے تو اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ مطالب آپ راہن کو مانیں گے یا مرتہن کو اور دونوں باطل ہیں، راہن تو اس لئے مطالب نہیں ہو سکتا کہ اس میں راہن کا ضرر ہے اور نفع کچھ نہیں جیسا کہ ظاہر ہے اور مرتہن بھی مطالب نہیں رہ سکتا۔ کیونکہ جب آپ نے اس معاملہ میں مرتہن کو مدعی علیہ قرار دیا ہے تو وہی مدعی کیونکر ہو سکتا ہے، اور اسی طرح مرتہن کو خلاف جنس کا ضامن بنانا بھی غلط ہے کیونکہ جب مرہون ہلاک ہو جانے کی وجہ سے مرتہن کو وصول کرنے والا شمار کر لیا گیا اور اسی کو مرہون کا مالک شمار کیا گیا تو وہ اپنی ملک کے لئے ضامن کیونکر ہو سکتا " ہے لہذا معلوم ہوا کہ عمان کی کوئی صورت نہیں ہے اور جب ضمان واجب کرنا محال ہو گیا تو وصول کو توڑنا بھی محال ومستعد رہو گیا یہ امام صاحب کی دلیل ہے۔
امام صاحب اور صاحبین کے اختلاف کی بنیاد ایک اور مسئلہ پر ہے اس مسئلہ کی وضاحت وقيل هذه فريعة ما اذا استوفى الزيوف مكان الجياد فهلكت ثم علم بالزيافة وهو معروف غير ان البناء لا يصح على ما هو المشهور لان محمدا فيها مع ابي حنيفة وفى هذا مع ابي يوسف والفرق لمحمد انه قبض الزيوف ليستوفى من عينها والزيافة لا تمنع الاستيفاء وقد تم بالهلاك وقبض الرهن ليستوفي من محل
آخر فلابد من نقض القبض وقد أمكن عنده بالتضمين
Book of Pledge. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah Volume 14. But if the jug's value is eight rupees, now there is disagreement: according to Imam [Abu Hanifa], Khalid has received his debt because the jug's weight is ten dirhams. And according to the Sahibayn, he will be guarantor for its value with a different genus, and that value will be placed in lieu of the pledge. The Sahibayn's proof: They said: There is no way to receive by weight due to harm to the creditor, nor to consider value because it leads to usury. So we resorted to guaranteeing with a different genus so that the possession is broken and it is placed in its place, then the pledgor (after paying the debt) becomes its owner. Commentary: This is the Sahibayn's proof: why is guarantee with a different genus made obligatory and placed in place of the pledge, and then the ruling is that when the pledgor pays the debt, he becomes the owner of the substitute? So they said: There were various possibilities but all turned out invalid, so we chose this form. Because considering weight causes loss to the creditor. How? Because the jug though weighing ten dirhams, its value is eight rupees, so clearly the creditor suffers loss. So that form became invalid. And if we consider value, e.g., the creditor receives eight rupees from the jug's value and the pledgor pays two more, that is usury. Both forms are invalid, so they chose the said guarantee. Question: Very well, but tell me why is the said guarantee with a different genus obligatory? Answer: Because if we kept ten dirhams, there was the possibility that the creditor might have simply received his right. So to strengthen the possession of the pledge, a different genus is placed, eliminating that possibility. That was the Sahibayn's proof. Next comes Imam [Abu Hanifa]'s proof. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof: He said: Quality is disregarded in ribawi goods when compared with their genus, and receiving good in exchange for bad is permissible, as when one overlooks it. And receipt has been accomplished by consensus, and therefore it needs to be broken. It cannot be broken by imposing a guarantee because it requires a claimant and a respondent, and likewise a person does not guarantee his own property. Since guarantee is impossible, breaking is impossible. Translation: And Abu Hanifa's proof is that quality is disregarded in ribawi goods when compared with their genus, and receiving good in exchange for bad is permissible, as when one overlooks it. And by consensus receipt has been achieved. For this reason, there is need to break it. But it cannot be broken by imposing guarantee because guarantee requires a claimant and a respondent, and similarly a person does not guarantee his own property. Since guarantee is impossible, breaking receipt becomes impossible. Commentary: This is Imam Abu Hanifa's proof: In goods where usury can occur, when compared with their genus, quality is disregarded, otherwise usury would arise. And if we assume the jug's value is low, but its weight is a full ten dirhams, then the debt (dirhams) are good and the pledge (jug) is bad, and the creditor has received bad in exchange for good. This is permissible, just as in currency exchange or salam sale, if one takes bad dirhams instead of good by way of overlooking, it is valid and the right is fulfilled. So now the only remaining need is to see whether the creditor has received his right. When we reflect, we find that when the pledge perishes with the creditor, he is considered to have received. Hence the creditor has received his right. Rather, here receipt is achieved by consensus. Question: According to the Sahibayn, receipt has not occurred; how did you say 'by consensus'? Answer: Receipt has been achieved by consensus; that is why the Sahibayn need to break the possession, because possession of the pledge is possession for receipt. So the creditor's receipt is established. In any case, the Sahibayn's statement that the receipt will be broken is evidence that receipt has already occurred. Now, as for the Sahibayn saying that the receipt will be broken, this requires reflection. Because to break this receipt, imposing guarantee on the creditor requires a claimant. And there is no claimant here. So neither guarantee will be obligatory nor will receipt be broken. The matter remains unresolved. The reason there is no claimant is because if you consider the pledgor as claimant, that is invalid because it brings loss to him with no benefit. If you consider the creditor as claimant, that is also invalid because when you have made the creditor the defendant in this matter, how can he be the plaintiff? Similarly, making the creditor the guarantor for a different genus is wrong because when due to the destruction of the pledge the creditor is considered to have received and is considered owner of the pledge, how can he be a guarantor for his own property? So it becomes clear that there is no form of guarantee. And when imposing guarantee is impossible, breaking receipt also becomes impossible. This is Imam [Abu Hanifa]'s proof. The basis of the disagreement between Imam and the Sahibayn is on another issue. Explanation of that issue: It is said that this is a branch of the case where one receives counterfeit coins in place of good ones, then they perish, and then the counterfeit is discovered. This is well-known, but the building [of the analogy] is not correct according to what is famous because Muhammad [al-Shaybani] is with Abu Hanifa in that issue, but here he is with Abu Yusuf. The distinction for Muhammad is that he received the counterfeit coins to receive from their very substance, and counterfeit does not prevent receipt, and it is completed by destruction. As for receiving the pledge, it is to receive from a different source, so it is necessary to break the possession, and that is possible for him through guarantee.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the fate of a pledge when it is destroyed after the pledgor has offered repayment but before the pledge is released. The scenario: A person pledges a brass jug (different genus from the silver dirhams of the debt). The jug weighs 10 dirhams but its market value is 8 rupees (a slightly different currency). The debtor offers the debt, but the jug is destroyed. How is the creditor compensated? Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the creditor has already received his due by weight, because the jug's weight equals the debt weight, and quality is disregarded in ribawi goods of the same genus — here the genus is weight-based. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that since the jug is of a different genus (brass vs. silver), weight cannot be the basis because it harms the creditor (he gets less value), and considering value would lead to riba (since the debt is of a different genus and value is less). So they impose a guarantee with a different genus: the creditor must guarantee the value (8 rupees), and that value stands in place of the pledge. The pledgor can then redeem it by paying the debt. The author then presents each side's proofs. The Sahibayn argue that neither weight nor value works: weight harms the creditor, value leads to riba. So they adopt a middle path: the creditor is made a guarantor for the value in a different form (e.g., currency) so that the possession of the pledge is effectively broken, and the pledgor can later get back the substitute. Imam Abu Hanifa counters that quality is irrelevant in ribawi goods of the same genus; receiving good in exchange for bad is permissible. Since the jug is of the same weight, the creditor has already received his right by consensus. To break that receipt would require a claimant, but neither the pledgor nor the creditor can be a claimant. Also, one cannot be a guarantor for one's own property. Therefore, receipt stands and no guarantee is needed. The dispute boils down to a foundational issue: in the case of receiving counterfeit coins (bad) in place of good ones, Muhammad al-Shaybani agrees with Abu Hanifa that receipt is valid (counterfeit does not prevent), but here he sides with Abu Yusuf because the pledge is a different species — receipt from the substance vs. receipt from another source. This shows the depth of Hanafi legal reasoning.

Key Terms
مرتہن (murtahin): The person who receives the pledge as security for a debt (creditor).
راہن (rahin): The person who gives the pledge as security for a debt (debtor/pledgor).
استیفاء (istifa'): Receipt/collection of the debt; here, when the pledge is destroyed in the creditor's possession, he is deemed to have received his due.
تضمین (tadmin): Imposing a guarantee/liability; here, the creditor becomes guarantor for the value of the destroyed pledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Imam Abu Hanifa consider the receipt (istifa') to be complete when a pledge of a different genus is destroyed?
A) Because the debtor has offered repayment, so the debt is automatically discharged.
B) Because quality is disregarded in ribawi goods of the same weight genus, and the weight of the pledge equals the weight of the debt.
C) Because the Sahibayn's view is weaker in evidence.
D) Because the pledge was not in the creditor's possession at the time of destruction.

Key Takeaway
The Sahibayn's view (guarantee with different genus) is the mufta bihi to prevent riba and harm, even though Abu Hanifa's reasoning is also methodologically valid.

Rahn — Pledge
intermediate
6 min
Satisfaction of Debt Upon Destruction of the Mortgaged Item: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explaining the intra-Hanafi dispute on satisfaction of debt upon destruction of the mortgaged item.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on satisfaction of debt upon destruction of the mortgaged item and explain the reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The debt is satisfied by destruction because possession is for collection — one cannot be liable for one's own property.

When a mortgaged item (marhun) is destroyed in the creditor's possession, does the debt automatically become satisfied? This question sparks a key intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). The answer hinges on the nature of the creditor's possession: is it a possession for collection (qabd al-isti'fa') or for security (qabd al-istithmar)? This lesson unpacks the arguments of both sides and clarifies the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa regarding the debt when the marhun is destroyed. What is the consequence for the creditor?
Abu Hanifa: debt satisfied, creditor not liable.
2
Identify the opposing view
Identify the position of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). What do they require the creditor to do?
Sahibayn: debt not satisfied; creditor must guarantee the value.
3
Follow the proof of each side
Examine the key proofs: for Abu Hanifa, the nature of possession as collection and the principle that one cannot guarantee one's own property. For the Sahibayn, the analogy to collecting bad coins and the idea of possession as security.
Note the qabd distinction and the bad coins analogy.
4
Analyse the Hanafi rebuttal
Understand how Abu Hanifa responds to the Sahibayn, particularly the argument that an impossible demand (mutalib) arises and that imposing liability contradicts property ownership.
Abu Hanifa argues no demand exists, so no breaking of collection.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
What is the practical difference between the two views in a real case? Which view is mufta bihi (operative for fatwa) and why?
Under Abu Hanifa: debt cancelled. Under Sahibayn: creditor pays value then claims debt. Mufta bihi: Abu Hanifa.

کی حاجت پیش آتی ہے کیونکہ قبضہ مرہون قبضہ استیفاء ہے لہذا مر تہن کا وصول و استیفاء پایا گیا۔ بہر حال صاحبین کا یہ فرمان کہ وصول کو توڑ دیا جائیگا یہ اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ وصول حاصل ہو چکا ہے اب رہی یہ بات کہ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ وصول تو ڑ دیا جائیگا تو یہ غور طلب ہے کیونکہ اس وصول کو توڑنا مرتہن پر ضمان واجب کرنے کے لئے ایک مطالب چاہیے اور یہاں کوئی مطالب نہیں ہے لہذا نہ ضمان واجب ہوگا اور نہ وصول ٹو میگا نہ رہے بانس اور نہ بجے بانسری۔ رہی یہ بات کہ مطالب نہیں ہے تو اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ مطالب آپ راہن کو مانیں گے یا مرتہن کو اور دونوں باطل ہیں، راہن تو اس لئے مطالب نہیں ہو سکتا کہ اس میں راہن کا ضرر ہے اور نفع کچھ نہیں جیسا کہ ظاہر ہے اور مرتہن بھی مطالب نہیں رہ سکتا۔ کیونکہ جب آپ نے اس معاملہ میں مرتہن کو مدعی علیہ قرار دیا ہے تو وہی مدعی کیونکر ہو سکتا ہے، اور اسی طرح مرتہن کو خلاف جنس کا ضامن بنانا بھی غلط ہے کیونکہ جب مرہون ہلاک ہو جانے کی وجہ سے مرتہن کو وصول کرنے والا شمار کر لیا گیا اور اسی کو مرہون کا مالک شمار کیا گیا تو وہ اپنی ملک کے لئے ضامن کیونکر ہو سکتا " ہے لہذا معلوم ہوا کہ عمان کی کوئی صورت نہیں ہے اور جب ضمان واجب کرنا محال ہو گیا تو وصول کو توڑنا بھی محال ومستعد رہو گیا یہ امام صاحب کی دلیل ہے۔ امام صاحب اور صاحبین کے اختلاف کی بنیاد ایک اور مسئلہ پر ہے اس مسئلہ کی وضاحت وقيل هذه فريعة ما اذا استوفى الزيوف مكان الجياد فهلكت ثم علم بالزيافة وهو معروف غير ان البناء لا يصح على ما هو المشهور لان محمدا فيها مع ابي حنيفة وفى هذا مع ابي يوسف والفرق لمحمد انه قبض الزيوف ليستوفى من عينها والزيافة لا تمنع الاستيفاء وقد تم بالهلاك وقبض الرهن ليستوفي من محل آخر فلابد من نقض القبض وقد أمكن عنده بالتضمين ترجمہ اور کہا گیا ہے کہ یہ مسئلہ فرع ہے اس مسئلہ کی جبکہ اس نے گھروں کی جگہ کھوئے وصول کر لئے ہوں پس وہ اس کے پاس ہلاک ہو گئے پھر اس نے کھوٹے ہونے کو جانا اور یہ (اسی مسئلہ کا حکم ) معروف و مشہور ہے علاوہ اس بات کے کہ بناء ( رہن کے مسئلہ کو اس پر بناء کرنا ) صحیح نہیں ہے مشہور قول کے مطابق اس لئے کہ محمد اس میں (اصل والے مسئلہ میں) ابوحنیفہ کے ساتھ ہیں اور اس میں ( رہن والے مسئلہ میں ) ابو یوسف کے ساتھ ہیں۔ اور محمد کے لئے وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ اس نے کھوٹوں پر قبضہ کیا ہے تا کہ ان کے مین سے وصول کر سکے اور کھوٹا ہونا وصولیابی سے نہیں روکتا اور ہلاکت کی وجہ سے وصولیابی تام ہوگئی اور رہن پر قبضہ اس لئے ہے تا کہ وہ دوسرے محل سے وصول کر سکے تو قبضہ کو توڑنا ضروری ہے اور محمد کے نزدیک مرتہن کو ضامن بنا کر قبضہ کو توڑ ناممکن ہے۔ تشریح مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ بعض حضرات کا کہنا ہے کہ رہن بی امام ابو حنیفہ اور صاحبین کا اختلاف مذکور ایک دوسرے مسئلہ کی فرع ہے مصنف کہناہے ان بی ابیضیفہ اور اور وہ یہ ہے کہ زید کے بکر پر سو درہم قرض میں بکر نے ادا کئے لیکن جو اداء کئے وہ کھوئے ہیں اور نید کے کھرے تھے جب زید نے ان کو صرف کر کے ہلاک کر دیا تب معلوم ہوا کہ یہ تو کھوٹے تھے تو اب کیا حکم ہے؟ امام ابو حنیفہ فرماتے ہیں کہ بس زید کا حق ادا ہوگیا اور بکر کچھ کرنے کا مجاز نہیں ہے۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ زید بکر کو ایسے ہی کھوٹے دراہم دے گا اور بکر سے عمدہ در اہم لیگا یہ ہے اصل مسئلہ جس پر یہ اختلافی مسئلہ متفرع ہے لیکن مصنف نے اس کو قیل سے تعبیر کیا ہے، جو اس کے ضعف کی طرف اشارہ ہے اس لئے بعض حضرات کا کہنا ہے کہ یہ مستقل مسئلہ ہے۔ سوال مگر حضور یہ بنا تو درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ اصل میں امام محمد امام ابوحنیفہ کے ساتھ ہیں اور فرع میں امام ابو یوسف کے ساتھ پھر بنا ، کیسی؟ جواب ... جی ہاں مانا۔ مگر اس کے باوجود بھی بناء صحیح ہے اور امام محمد نے جو ان دونوں میں فرق کیا ہے اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اصل مسئلہ میں قبضہ کا مقصود حق کا عین در اہم سے استیفاء ہے اور یہ استیفاء دوصولیابی کھوٹے دراہم سے بھی ہو جاتی ہے اور ہلاکت نے مزید وصولیابی کو پختہ بنا دیا ہے، اور فرع والے مسئلہ میں مرہون پر قبضہ کا اصل مقصد مضبوطی ہے تا کہ مرہون کی بنیاد پر دوسرے محل سے اپنا حق وصول کر سکے اور مرتہن کو ضامن بنا کر دوسرے محل سے وصولیابی ہو جائیگی لہذ اقبضہ کو توڑنے کیلئے خلاف جنس سے اس کی قیمت رہن ہوگی۔ تنبیہ - اصح یہ ہے کہ مسئلہ رہن خود مستقل ہے لہذا ان تاویلات کی حاجت نہ ہوگی۔ دوسرا جواب لوگوں نے یہ بھی دیا ہے کہ معروف مسئلہ میں بھی امام محمد کا آخری قول امام ابو یوسف کے ساتھ ہے۔
A person is not a guarantor for his own property, and due to the impossibility of imposing liability, breaking the collection becomes impossible. Explanation: This is the proof of Imam Abu Hanifa: in goods where riba can occur, when comparing by type, quality is disregarded, otherwise riba would occur. And if we assume the value of the jug is less, but its weight is exactly ten dirhams, then the situation is that the loan (dirhams) are of good quality and the mortgaged item (jug) is of inferior quality, and the creditor has received inferior in exchange for good. This is permissible, just as in a contract of money exchange or salam, if one takes bad dirhams instead of good ones out of leniency, it is permissible and the right is fulfilled. Now the only remaining question is whether the creditor has received his right. When we consider, it becomes clear that when the mortgaged item is destroyed in the possession of the creditor, he is considered to have collected it. Therefore, it is clear that the creditor has collected his right. Rather, here the satisfaction of the right has been achieved by consensus. Question: According to the Sahibayn, satisfaction has not occurred, so how did you say 'by consensus'? Answer: Satisfaction of the right has occurred by consensus; that is why the Sahibayn need to break the possession. Because the possession of the mortgaged item is a possession for collection, so the creditor's collection has been attained. In any case, the Sahibayn's statement that the collection will be broken is proof that the collection has occurred. Now the remaining point is that the Sahibayn say the collection will be broken. This requires scrutiny, because breaking the collection requires a demand (mutalib) for imposing liability on the creditor, and there is no demand here. Therefore, neither will liability be imposed nor will the collection break. The matter is settled. The reason there is no demand is that if you consider the demand coming from the mortgagor or the creditor, both are invalid. The mortgagor cannot demand because that would harm him and bring no benefit, as is apparent. The creditor also cannot remain a demander because when you have made the creditor the defendant in this matter, how can he be the plaintiff? Similarly, making the creditor liable for something different in kind is also wrong, because when the creditor is considered a collector due to the destruction of the mortgaged item and is considered the owner of the mortgaged item, how can he be a guarantor for his own property? Thus, it is clear that there is no possibility of liability, and since imposing liability is impossible, breaking the collection is also impossible. This is the proof of Imam Abu Hanifa. The basis of the dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn lies in another issue. The clarification of that issue: 'It is said that this is a branch of the issue when one collects bad coins instead of good coins, then they are destroyed, and then he learns of their badness. This is well-known, except that building upon it (the rahn issue on this) is not correct according to the famous view, because Muhammad is with Abu Hanifa in that (the coins issue) and with Abu Yusuf in this (the rahn issue). The distinguishing factor for Muhammad is that he took possession of the bad coins to collect from those very coins, and badness does not prevent collection, and collection was completed by destruction. But possession of the mortgaged item is to collect from another source, so breaking the possession is necessary, and in his view, it is possible by making the creditor liable.' Translation: And it is said that this issue is a branch of that issue when he collected bad coins in place of good coins, then they were destroyed, then he learned of their badness. This is well-known, except that building (the rahn issue upon it) is not correct according to the famous view, because Muhammad is with Abu Hanifa in that (original issue) and with Abu Yusuf in this (rahn issue). For Muhammad, the reason for the distinction is that he took possession of the bad coins to collect from those very coins, and badness does not prevent collection, and collection was completed by destruction. And possession of the rahn is to collect from another source, so breaking the possession is necessary, and in his view, it is possible by making the creditor liable. Commentary: The author (Musannif) says that some people say that the mentioned dispute of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on rahn is a branch of another issue. The author says: ... and that is that Zaid owes Bakr one hundred dirhams as a loan. Bakr paid them, but what he paid were bad dirhams, while Zaid's dirhams were good. When Zaid spent them and they were destroyed, then he learned that they were bad. Now what is the ruling? Imam Abu Hanifa says that Zaid's right has been fulfilled and Bakr cannot do anything. The Sahibayn say that Zaid will give Bakr similar bad dirhams and take good dirhams from Bakr. This is the original issue upon which this disputed issue is branched. But the author expressed it with 'qil' (it is said), which indicates its weakness. Therefore, some people say that this is an independent issue. Question: But Sir, this building is not valid because in the original issue, Imam Muhammad is with Imam Abu Hanifa, and in the branch, he is with Imam Abu Yusuf. So how can building be? Answer: Yes, granted. But despite this, the building is correct, and the distinction that Imam Muhammad made between them is that in the original issue, the purpose of possession is to collect the right from the actual dirhams, and this satisfaction can also occur with bad dirhams, and destruction further solidified the satisfaction. In the branch issue, the purpose of possession of the mortgaged item is to secure, so that based on the mortgaged item, he can collect his right from another source. By making the creditor liable, collection from another source will occur. Therefore, to break the possession, the value of the item in different kind becomes the mortgage. Notice: The correct view is that the rahn issue is itself independent, so there is no need for these interpretations. A second answer: Some people have also given that even in the well-known issue, Imam Muhammad's final saying is with Imam Abu Yusuf.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the destruction of a mortgaged item (marhun) in the creditor's (murtahin) possession. The core question: does the debt become satisfied upon destruction? 

Imam Abu Hanifa argues that the debt is satisfied because the creditor's possession of the marhun is a 'possession for collection' (qabd al-isti'fa'). Upon destruction, the creditor is deemed to have collected his right. He supports this by noting that in transactions where riba is possible, quality is disregarded when the type and weight match. Therefore, if the marhun's weight equals the debt's weight, the debt is considered paid. He also argues that imposing liability would make the creditor a guarantor for his own property, which is impossible. 

The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disagree: the creditor's possession is for security (qabd al-istithmar), so destruction does not complete collection. They analogize to a case where a debtor repays with bad coins instead of good: if the bad coins are destroyed, the creditor must return similar bad coins and take good ones. Thus, here the creditor must guarantee the value of the marhun. 

The passage then explores the basis of this dispute, suggesting that the rahn issue is a branch of the bad coins issue. However, the author notes that this analogy is weak because Imam Muhammad aligns with Abu Hanifa on the coins issue but with Abu Yusuf on the rahn issue. The distinguishing factor is that in the coins case, possession is for collection from the specific coins, while in the rahn case, possession is for collection from another source. Hence, breaking the possession is necessary, achievable by making the creditor liable. 

The commentary concludes that the rahn issue is independent, and the reliance on the coins analogy is not required. The second answer suggests that even in the coins issue, Imam Muhammad's final position aligns with Abu Yusuf, further weakening the analogy. 

Thus, the passage provides the reasoning of each side and clarifies that the rahn dispute stands on its own, with the relied-upon position being that of Imam Abu Hanifa (debt satisfied).

Key Terms
مرہون (marhun): The mortgaged item given as security for a debt.
مرتہن (murtahin): The creditor who receives the mortgage.
استیفاء (istifa'): The collection or satisfaction of a debt, considered complete upon destruction of the marhun in Abu Hanifa's view.
ضمان (daman): Liability or guarantee, which the Sahibayn argue the creditor must bear for the value of the marhun.
قبض (qabd): Possession of the mortgaged item by the creditor.
بناء (bina'): Building one legal ruling upon another through analogy (qiyas).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a mortgaged item (marhun) is destroyed in the creditor's possession, what is the status of the debt?
A) The debt remains unpaid, and the creditor must guarantee the value.
B) The debt is considered satisfied, and the creditor is not liable.
C) The creditor must return the item's value and can claim the debt.
D) The debt is cancelled only if the item's value equals the debt.

Key Takeaway
The debt is satisfied when the mortgaged item is destroyed in the creditor's possession under Abu Hanifa's view, which is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

Rahn — Pledge
intermediate
8 min
Is the Pledge Ruling a Branch of the Counterfeit Coins Issue?
Intra-Hanafi dispute over branching of rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the pledge issue is considered independent from the counterfeit coins issue and identify the methodological significance of Muhammad's shifting alignment.

Core Idea
A ruling is not automatically a branch of another if the companion Imam's alignment changes.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi debate: is the ruling on a pledge destroyed by the pledgee a branch of an earlier dispute about counterfeit coins? Some scholars claim branching due to similarities in possession and destruction. However, the author of al-Hidayah argues that the pledge issue is independent, pointing to a shift in Imam Muhammad's alignment across the two cases. Understanding this dispute reveals how Hanafi jurists evaluate whether one ruling can be derived from another.

Guided Path
1
State the claim of branching
Identify the claim that the pledge issue (destruction of marhun by murtahin) is a branch (far') of another issue (counterfeit coins destroyed by creditor).
This claim is presented as 'qila' (it is said), indicating weakness.
2
Identify the original issue and its ruling
Describe the original case: Zaid pays Bakr with counterfeit coins; Bakr destroys them unknowingly. Abu Hanifa says debt is discharged; the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say Bakr must return the counterfeit and take good coins.
In the original, Muhammad agrees with Abu Hanifa, not with Abu Yusuf.
3
Analyse the opponent's proof
The opponent argues that both cases involve a creditor taking possession and then destroying the item, so the same reasoning should apply.
4
Examine the Hanafi response: Muhammad's alignment shift
The author notes that in the original, Muhammad is with Abu Hanifa, but in the pledge issue, he is with Abu Yusuf. This shift breaks the claimed branching.
If the issues were truly the same, Muhammad's alignment would not change.
5
Understand the distinguishing rationale
In the original, possession aimed to collect the debt from those very coins; counterfeit does not prevent collection, and destruction completes it. In the pledge, possession aims to secure collection from another source; thus, destroying the pledge requires substitution or liability.
This difference in purpose makes the rulings independent.

ترجمہ اور کہا گیا ہے کہ یہ مسئلہ فرع ہے اس مسئلہ کی جبکہ اس نے گھروں کی جگہ کھوئے وصول کر لئے ہوں پس وہ اس کے پاس ہلاک ہو گئے پھر اس نے کھوٹے ہونے کو جانا اور یہ (اسی مسئلہ کا حکم ) معروف و مشہور ہے علاوہ اس بات کے کہ بناء ( رہن کے مسئلہ کو اس پر بناء کرنا ) صحیح نہیں ہے مشہور قول کے مطابق اس لئے کہ محمد اس میں (اصل والے مسئلہ میں) ابوحنیفہ کے ساتھ ہیں اور اس میں ( رہن والے مسئلہ میں ) ابو یوسف کے ساتھ ہیں۔ اور محمد کے لئے وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ اس نے کھوٹوں پر قبضہ کیا ہے تا کہ ان کے مین سے وصول کر سکے اور کھوٹا ہونا وصولیابی سے نہیں روکتا اور ہلاکت کی وجہ سے وصولیابی تام ہوگئی اور رہن پر قبضہ اس لئے ہے تا کہ وہ دوسرے محل سے وصول کر سکے تو قبضہ کو توڑنا ضروری ہے اور محمد کے نزدیک مرتہن کو ضامن بنا کر قبضہ کو توڑ ناممکن ہے۔
تشریح مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ بعض حضرات کا کہنا ہے کہ رہن بی امام ابو حنیفہ اور صاحبین کا اختلاف مذکور ایک دوسرے مسئلہ کی فرع ہے مصنف کہناہے ان بی ابیضیفہ اور اور وہ یہ ہے کہ زید کے بکر پر سو درہم قرض میں بکر نے ادا کئے لیکن جو اداء کئے وہ کھوئے ہیں اور نید کے کھرے تھے جب زید نے ان کو صرف کر کے ہلاک کر دیا تب معلوم ہوا کہ یہ تو کھوٹے تھے تو اب کیا حکم ہے؟
امام ابو حنیفہ فرماتے ہیں کہ بس زید کا حق ادا ہوگیا اور بکر کچھ کرنے کا مجاز نہیں ہے۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ زید بکر کو ایسے ہی کھوٹے دراہم دے گا اور بکر سے عمدہ در اہم لیگا یہ ہے اصل مسئلہ جس پر یہ اختلافی مسئلہ متفرع ہے لیکن مصنف نے اس کو قیل سے تعبیر کیا ہے، جو اس کے ضعف کی طرف اشارہ ہے اس لئے بعض حضرات کا کہنا ہے کہ یہ مستقل مسئلہ ہے۔
سوال مگر حضور یہ بنا تو درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ اصل میں امام محمد امام ابوحنیفہ کے ساتھ ہیں اور فرع میں امام ابو یوسف کے ساتھ پھر بنا ، کیسی؟ جواب ... جی ہاں مانا۔ مگر اس کے باوجود بھی بناء صحیح ہے اور امام محمد نے جو ان دونوں میں فرق کیا ہے اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اصل مسئلہ میں قبضہ کا مقصود حق کا عین در اہم سے استیفاء ہے اور یہ استیفاء دوصولیابی کھوٹے دراہم سے بھی ہو جاتی ہے اور ہلاکت نے مزید وصولیابی کو پختہ بنا دیا ہے، اور فرع والے مسئلہ میں مرہون پر قبضہ کا اصل مقصد مضبوطی ہے تا کہ مرہون کی بنیاد پر دوسرے محل سے اپنا حق وصول کر سکے اور مرتہن کو ضامن بنا کر دوسرے محل سے وصولیابی ہو جائیگی لہذ اقبضہ کو توڑنے کیلئے خلاف جنس سے اس کی قیمت رہن ہوگی۔ تنبیہ - اصح یہ ہے کہ مسئلہ رہن خود مستقل ہے لہذا ان تاویلات کی حاجت نہ ہوگی۔
Translation: And it has been said that this issue is a branch of that issue where he took counterfeit coins instead of genuine ones, then they perished with him, then he came to know they were counterfeit. And this ruling is well-known. However, the basis (of making the pledge issue a branch of it) is not correct according to the well-known saying, because Muhammad agrees with Abu Hanifa in the original issue but agrees with Abu Yusuf in this (pledge) issue. And for Muhammad, the differentiating reason is that he took possession of the counterfeit coins to collect (the debt) from them, and being counterfeit does not prevent collection, and due to destruction collection became complete. But possession of the pledge is to enable collection from another source, so breaking the possession is necessary, and according to Muhammad, making the pledgee a guarantor makes breaking possession impossible.
Explanation: The author says that some say the mentioned difference of opinion between Abu Hanifa and the two companions is a branch of another issue. That issue is: Zaid owes Bakr one hundred dirhams; Bakr paid but with counterfeit coins while Zaid's were genuine; after Zaid spent them and they perished, he learned they were counterfeit. What is the ruling? Abu Hanifa says Zaid's debt is discharged and Bakr cannot do anything. The two companions say Zaid will give such counterfeit dirhams to Bakr and take good dirhams from him. This is the original issue on which this disputed issue is branching. But the author has expressed it as 'it is said', indicating its weakness, so some say this is an independent issue.
Question: But sir, this branching is not correct because in the original, Imam Muhammad is with Abu Hanifa while in the branch he is with Abu Yusuf. How can it be branching? Answer: Yes, we admit that, but despite that, the branching is correct. And Imam Muhammad's distinction between the two is: in the original issue, the purpose of possession is to receive the debt from the coins themselves, and this collection can also be achieved with counterfeit coins, and destruction made the collection complete. But in the branch issue, the purpose of possession of the pledged item is security, so that based on it, he can collect his right from another source, and by making the pledgee a guarantor, collection from another source will occur. Therefore, to break the possession, its value – from a different type – will be a pledge. Caution: The correct view is that the issue of pledge is independent, so these interpretations are not needed.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether the ruling on a pledged item destroyed by the pledgee is a branch of another issue about counterfeit coins. The author first presents the claim that it is a branch, then refutes it. The original issue: if a debtor pays with counterfeit coins that the creditor destroys, Abu Hanifa says the debt is discharged; the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say the creditor must pay back the counterfeit and take good ones. In the pledge issue, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold one view, while Muhammad differs. The author explains why the branching is not straightforward: Muhammad agrees with Abu Hanifa in the original but with Abu Yusuf in the branch. However, the author defends the branching by providing a distinction: in the original, possession is for collection of the debt from the same coins, which can be done even if counterfeit; in the pledge, possession is for security, so breaking it requires substitution. Ultimately, the author notes that the correct view is that the pledge issue is independent.

Key Terms
فرع (far'): A subsidiary issue derived from a root (asl) issue
بناء (bina'): Basing a ruling on another ruling; making one issue a branch of another

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do some scholars say that the pledge issue is a branch of the counterfeit coins issue?
A) Because both involve destruction of property
B) Because both involve possession and collection of debt
C) Because Imam Muhammad aligns with Abu Hanifa in both
D) Because the rulings are identical

Key Takeaway
The pledge issue is independent from the counterfeit coins issue because the purpose of possession differs, as evidenced by Imam Muhammad's shifting alignment.

Ruling on a Pledged Pitcher That Breaks
Intra-Hanafi dispute on pledged item breakage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions (the two shaykhs vs. Imam Muhammad) when a pledged item is broken and apply the ruling to similar cases.

Core Idea
When a pledged item breaks, the rahin is not forced to redeem; he may either bear the loss or transfer liability to the pledgee.

In this lesson, we examine a nuanced case in Hanafi rahn law: what happens when a pledged item is broken but not completely destroyed? The great Imams differ on the rahin's options. We will follow the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, then contrast Imam Muhammad's view, and understand the practical consequences of their difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the factual scenario
The case: a pledged pitcher (value equals its weight) breaks (e.g., spout broken, still weighing the same). The rahin could redeem by paying the debt in full, but the item is now defective.
Value equals weight - no dispute on that condition.
2
State the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
The two shaykhs hold that the rahin is not forced to redeem. He has a choice: either redeem with the full debt (accepting the defect) or make the pledgee liable for the pitcher's value (which becomes a new pledge). The broken pitcher becomes the pledgee's property.
Their reasoning avoids two invalid outcomes: deducting for quality (invalid) or forced redemption with harm.
3
Identify the reasoning behind the two shaykhs' position
They argue that if the rahin were forced to redeem, only two possibilities exist: (1) deduct part of the debt for the defect - this would mean paying by quality alone, which is invalid; (2) redeem with full debt despite defect - this causes harm to the rahin. Since both are invalid, the rahin is given a choice.
This is an expansion of the base text's 'because of harm'.
4
State Imam Muhammad's position and its basis
Imam Muhammad holds a different choice: either redeem with the defect (paying full debt) or treat the breakage as destruction, meaning the broken item itself secures the debt (as if destroyed). His basis: qiyas to destruction - since free redemption is impossible, it is like total destruction, and in destruction the item is liable for the debt by consensus.
Imam Muhammad's view is more rigid: the rahin cannot transfer liability; the broken item remains as security.
5
Compare the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under the two shaykhs: rahin may choose to make the pledgee liable for the value, which becomes a new pledge; under Muhammad: the broken item itself continues to secure the debt (like destroyed item). The rahin's options differ in how the security is maintained.
No explicit tarjih in the text, but later Hanafi practice often follows the two shaykhs.

Source Text

ترجمہ اور اگر لوٹا ٹوٹ گیا تو پہلی صورت میں اور وہ وہ ہے جبکہ لوٹے کی قیمت اس کے وزن کے برابر ہو تو ابوحنیفہ اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک را ہن کو رہن چھڑانے پر مجبور نہیں کیا جائیگا اس لئے کہ اس کی تو کوئی وجہ نہیں کہ کچھ قرض ساقط ہو جائے اس لئے کہ راہن تنہا جودت و ساخت سے اپنے قرض کو ادا کرنے والا ہو جائیگا ( اور یہ باطل ہے ) اور نہ اس کی کوئی وجہ ہے کہ راہن نقصان کے باوجود اس کو چھڑالے کیونکہ اس میں راہن کا ضرر ہے تو ہم نے اس کو اختیار دیا کہ اگر چاہے اس کو اس کے قرض کے عوض چھڑالے ( یعنی خسارہ برداشت کر کے مرتبہن کا پورا قرض ادا کر کے ) اور اگر چاہے تو مرتہن اس کی قیمت کا ضامن بنا دے اس کی جنس سے ہو یا خلاف جنس سے اور قیمت مرتہن کے پاس رہن رہے گی اور ٹوٹا ہوا لو ٹا ضمان ادا کرنے کی وجہ سے مرتہن کی ملک ہو گا۔
تشریح جولو ٹا مرہون تھا وہ مرتین کے پاس ہلاک ہونے کے بجائے ٹوٹ گیا مثلاً اس کی ٹونٹی ٹوٹ گئی اور وہ مختون ہو گیا تو اب کیا حکم ہے؟
-1
و فرمایا کہ اگرلوٹے کا وزن اور قیمت برابر ہو تواس میں شیخین اور امام کا اختلاف ہے۔ شیخین فرماتے ہیں کہ را ہن کو واختیار ہیں۔ خساره برداشت کرے اور مرتین کا پورا قرض دیکر اپنا لوٹا جس حال میں ہے واپس لے لے ۔ مرتہن کو مکلف کرے کہ لوٹے کا تو مالک بن گیا اور تو اس کی قیمت جو دس درہم ہے ادا کر ۔ اور قیمت کو مرہون کی جگہ پر رکھ پھر راہن جب قرض ادا کر دے تو مرہون کے قائم مقام یعنی قیمت مذکورہ کو مرتہن سے واپس لے گا پھر قیمت کا ضمان خواہ دراہم سے ادا کیا جائے یا دینار سے دونوں جائز ہیں یہ ہے اس صورت میں حضرات شیخین کا مذہب لہزار اہن پر شیخین کے نزدیک یہ جبر نہیں کیا جاسکتا کہ رہن چھڑائے کیونکہ اس کی دو ہی صورتیں ہو سکتی ہیں اور دونوں باطل ہیں جب یہ دونوں صورتیں باطل ہو ئیں تو ہم نے راہن کو یہ اختیار دیا اور دو باطل صور میں یہ تھیں۔ راہن ٹوٹا ہوا لوٹا لے لے اور مرتہن کے دس دراہم میں سے ٹوٹنے کی وجہ سے تین درہم کم کر دئیے جائیں کیونکہ لوٹے کا وزن تو پورا باقی ہے تو تین درہم کو کم کر نا خالص لوٹے کی ساخت کی وجہ سے ہوگا جس کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ را بہن نے لوٹے کی ساخت کی وجہ سے تین در هم قرض کے ادا کر دیئے اور یہ باطل ہے۔ - یارا ہن نقصان برداشت کرے اور پورا قرض دیگر مختون لوٹا واپس لے تو ظاہر ہے کہ اس میں راہن کا کھلا ہوا ضر ر ہے کہ اس نے رکھا تھا عمدہ لوٹا اور مل رہا ہے ٹوٹا ہوا۔
لہذا جب یہ دونوں صورتیں باطل ٹھہریں تو ہم نے اختیار کو منتخب کیا۔
امام محمد کا نقطہ نظر
وعند محمد ان شاء افتكه ناقصا وان شاء جعله بالدين اعتبارا لحالة الانكسار بحالة الهلاك وهذا لانه لما تعذر الفكاك مجانا صار بمنزلة الهلاك وفى الهلاك الحقيقى مضمون بالدين بالاجماع فكذا فيما هو في معناه
And if the pitcher breaks, then in the first case, which is when its value equals its weight, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, (the rahin) is not forced to redeem because there is no way for any part of the debt to fall away, for he would be paying his debt by the quality alone, nor is there a way for him to redeem it with a defect, because of harm. So we gave him a choice: if he wishes, he redeems it with the debt (i.e., accepts the defect and pays full debt), and if he wishes, he makes (the pledgee) liable for its value, whether from its type or from another type, and it remains a pledge with the pledgee, and the broken pitcher belongs to the pledgee by virtue of liability.

Translation: And if the pitcher broke, then in the first case, when the value of the pitcher equals its weight, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the rahin is not forced to redeem it, because there is no reason for any part of the debt to be waived, for the rahin would be paying his debt by virtue of the quality alone (and that is invalid), nor is there a reason for him to redeem it with the defect because of harm to him. So we gave him a choice: if he wishes, he redeems it with the debt (i.e., bears the loss and pays the full debt), and if he wishes, he makes the pledgee liable for its value, whether from its type or from a different type, and the value remains a pledge with the pledgee, and the broken pitcher becomes the property of the pledgee due to liability.

Explanation: The pitcher that was pledged broke, e.g., its spout broke and it became defective, so what is the ruling?

It was said: If the weight and value of the pitcher are equal, then there is a difference between the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad. The two shaykhs say the rahin has a choice: either bear the loss and pay the full debt to take back his pitcher in its current state, or demand the pledgee to become liable for its value (e.g., ten dirhams) and place that value as a pledge; then when the rahin pays the debt, he takes back the substitute value from the pledgee. This liability can be paid with dirhams or dinars, both are permissible. That is the madhhab of the two shaykhs. They do not force the rahin to redeem because there are only two possible scenarios and both are invalid. The two invalid scenarios: (1) The rahin takes the broken pitcher and deducts three dirhams from the ten dirhams due to the breakage, but since the weight is still full, the reduction is due to the quality, meaning the rahin paid three dirhams for the quality, which is invalid. (2) The rahin bears the loss and pays the full debt to take back a defective pitcher, which is clearly a loss for him. Since both are invalid, we have chosen the option of choice. 

Imam Muhammad's view: According to Muhammad, if he wishes, he redeems it with the defect, and if he wishes, he makes it (the value) against the debt, considering the state of breakage like the state of destruction. This is because when free redemption is impossible, it becomes like destruction, and in true destruction, it is liable for the debt by consensus, so the same holds for what is in its meaning.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling when a pledged item is broken (not completely destroyed). The text first states the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: when the value equals weight, the rahin is not forced to redeem. Instead, he has a choice: either redeem with the full debt despite the defect, or make the pledgee liable for the item's value, which becomes a new pledge. The broken item then becomes the pledgee's property. The explanation clarifies the reason: forcing redemption would lead to one of two invalid outcomes. Then Imam Muhammad's view is given: he equates breakage with destruction, giving the rahin a choice to redeem with defect or have the broken item secure the debt as if destroyed. This is based on the principle that when free redemption is impossible, it is treated as destruction.

Key Terms
فكاك (fakak): Redemption of a pledge by paying the debt
ضمان (daman): Liability; here, the pledgee becomes liable for the value of the broken item
جودة (jooda): Quality; here, the better quality of the pitcher (its craftsmanship) is considered separate from weight

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, what is the rahin's option when a pledged pitcher of equal value and weight breaks?
A) He must redeem it with the full debt
B) He may deduct the defect from the debt
C) He may either redeem with full debt or make the pledgee liable for its value
D) He must give the broken pitcher to the pledgee as compensation

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when a pledged item breaks (value equals weight), the rahin is not forced to redeem; he may choose between bearing the loss or transferring liability to the pledgee, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Partial Breakage of a Mortgaged Item: The Rahin's Choice
Intra-Hanafi dispute over treatment of broken jug in mortgage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on partial breakage (inkisar) of a mortgaged item, distinguish the positions of the shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad, and evaluate the tarjih (preference) in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A broken mortgaged item is not automatically forfeited; the rahin chooses between redeeming at full debt or claiming the item's value.

When a mortgaged item is partially broken, does the debt automatically drop? The Hanafi school has an internal dispute between the shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad. This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah clarifies the ruling and the reasoning behind the preferred view. You will learn the legal options available to the pledgor and why the school rejects the analogy to total destruction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A jug (lota) is pawned. Its spout breaks, so it is partially damaged but still intact. The weight and original value are equal.
This is the specific case: value = weight.
2
State the shaykhayn's position (Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf)
The rahin cannot be forced to redeem the broken item. He has two choices: either redeem by paying the full debt (bearing the loss) or demand the murtahin pay the item's value, which becomes the new pledge.
The murtahin then owns the broken piece as compensation.
3
Understand the two invalid possibilities
(1) Reducing the debt because of lost craftsmanship is invalid. (2) Forcing the rahin to redeem at a loss harms him. Therefore, the choice is the only valid option.
These two possibilities are rejected.
4
Explain Imam Muhammad's analogy
Muhammad analogizes breakage to total destruction. Since free redemption is impossible, breakage reaches the level of destruction. In total destruction, the pledge becomes substitute for the debt. So here, the broken item can discharge the debt.
Muhammad gives the rahin the option to either redeem or let the broken item cancel the debt.
5
Analyse the Hanafi response
The commentator rebuts that even in destruction, recovery is through value, not forfeiture of the specific item. Making the item a substitute for the debt is ighlaq al-rahn (forfeiting the pledge), which is a pre-Islamic practice (jahili) and disapproved.
Thus, making the murtahin liable for value is more appropriate (awla).
6
Determine the mufta bihi
The view of the shaykhayn is adopted: the rahin has a choice; the debt does not automatically drop. The murtahin must compensate the value if the rahin chooses that option.
This is the operative position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الرهن ان يفتكه مع النقصان لما فيه من الضرر فخيرناه ان شاء افتكه بمافيه وان شاء ضمنه قيمته من جنسه او خلاف جنسه وتكون رهنا عند المرتهن والمكسور للمرتهن بالضمان ترجمہ اور اگر لوٹا ٹوٹ گیا تو پہلی صورت میں اور وہ وہ ہے جبکہ لوٹے کی قیمت اس کے وزن کے برابر ہو تو ابوحنیفہ اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک را ہن کو رہن چھڑانے پر مجبور نہیں کیا جائیگا اس لئے کہ اس کی تو کوئی وجہ نہیں کہ کچھ قرض ساقط ہو جائے اس لئے کہ راہن تنہا جودت و ساخت سے اپنے قرض کو ادا کرنے والا ہو جائیگا ( اور یہ باطل ہے ) اور نہ اس کی کوئی وجہ ہے کہ راہن نقصان کے باوجود اس کو چھڑالے کیونکہ اس میں راہن کا ضرر ہے تو ہم نے اس کو اختیار دیا کہ اگر چاہے اس کو اس کے قرض کے عوض چھڑالے ( یعنی خسارہ برداشت کر کے مرتبہن کا پورا قرض ادا کر کے ) اور اگر چاہے تو مرتہن اس کی قیمت کا ضامن بنا دے اس کی جنس سے ہو یا خلاف جنس سے اور قیمت مرتہن کے پاس رہن رہے گی اور ٹوٹا ہوا لو ٹا ضمان ادا کرنے کی وجہ سے مرتہن کی ملک ہو گا۔ تشریح جولو ٹا مرہون تھا وہ مرتین کے پاس ہلاک ہونے کے بجائے ٹوٹ گیا مثلاً اس کی ٹونٹی ٹوٹ گئی اور وہ مختون ہو گیا تو اب کیا حکم ہے؟ -1 و فرمایا کہ اگرلوٹے کا وزن اور قیمت برابر ہو تواس میں شیخین اور امام کا اختلاف ہے۔ شیخین فرماتے ہیں کہ را ہن کو واختیار ہیں۔ خساره برداشت کرے اور مرتین کا پورا قرض دیکر اپنا لوٹا جس حال میں ہے واپس لے لے ۔ مرتہن کو مکلف کرے کہ لوٹے کا تو مالک بن گیا اور تو اس کی قیمت جو دس درہم ہے ادا کر ۔ اور قیمت کو مرہون کی جگہ پر رکھ پھر راہن جب قرض ادا کر دے تو مرہون کے قائم مقام یعنی قیمت مذکورہ کو مرتہن سے واپس لے گا پھر قیمت کا ضمان خواہ دراہم سے ادا کیا جائے یا دینار سے دونوں جائز ہیں یہ ہے اس صورت میں حضرات شیخین کا مذہب لہزار اہن پر شیخین کے نزدیک یہ جبر نہیں کیا جاسکتا کہ رہن چھڑائے کیونکہ اس کی دو ہی صورتیں ہو سکتی ہیں اور دونوں باطل ہیں جب یہ دونوں صورتیں باطل ہو ئیں تو ہم نے راہن کو یہ اختیار دیا اور دو باطل صور میں یہ تھیں۔ راہن ٹوٹا ہوا لوٹا لے لے اور مرتہن کے دس دراہم میں سے ٹوٹنے کی وجہ سے تین درہم کم کر دئیے جائیں کیونکہ لوٹے کا وزن تو پورا باقی ہے تو تین درہم کو کم کر نا خالص لوٹے کی ساخت کی وجہ سے ہوگا جس کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ را بہن نے لوٹے کی ساخت کی وجہ سے تین در هم قرض کے ادا کر دیئے اور یہ باطل ہے۔ - یارا ہن نقصان برداشت کرے اور پورا قرض دیگر مختون لوٹا واپس لے تو ظاہر ہے کہ اس میں راہن کا کھلا ہوا ضر ر ہے کہ اس نے رکھا تھا عمدہ لوٹا اور مل رہا ہے ٹوٹا ہوا۔ لہذا جب یہ دونوں صورتیں باطل ٹھہریں تو ہم نے اختیار کو منتخب کیا۔ امام محمد کا نقطہ نظر وعند محمد ان شاء افتكه ناقصا وان شاء جعله بالدين اعتبارا لحالة الانكسار بحالة الهلاك وهذا لانه لما تعذر الفكاك مجانا صار بمنزلة الهلاك وفى الهلاك الحقيقى مضمون بالدين بالاجماع فكذا فيما هو في معناه ترجمہ اور محمد کے نزدیک اگر چاہے تو اس کو نقصان کی حالت میں چھڑالے اور اگر چاہے تو اس کو قرض کا عوض ٹھہرا دے انکسار کی حالت کو ہلاکت کی حالت پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اور یہ اس لئے کہ جب مفت چھڑا نامستعد رہو گیا تو انکسار ہلاکت کے درجہ میں ہو گیا اور حقیقی ہلاکت کی صورت میں بالا جماع مرہون قرض کے بدلہ مضمون ہوتا پس ایسے ہی اس صورت میں جو ہلاکت کے درجہ میں ہو۔ تشریح یہ اما محمد کا مذہب ہے کہ راہن کو صورت مذکورہ میں دو اختیار ہیں۔ (۱) تو وہی ہے جونمبر (۱) پر شیخین نے فرمایا تھا کہ نقصان برداشت کرے اور مرتہن کا قرض دیگر ٹوٹا ہوا لوٹا واپس لے لے۔ (۲) راہن کو یہ اختیار ہے کہ ٹوٹے ہوئے لوٹے کو قرض کا بدل قرار دیدے یعنی گویا کہ راہن نے مرتین کا قرض ادا کر دیا۔ خلاصہ کلام امام محمد نے انکسار پر ہلاکت کا حکم جاری کیا ہے اور اگر لوٹا ہلاک ہو جاتا ہو تو یہی حکم ہوتا کہ مرتہن کا قرض ساقط اور انکسار بھی گویا کہ ہلاکت ہی ہے لہذا جو چیز ہلاکت کے درجہ میں آگئی ہو تو اس کے اوپر بھی ہلاکت کا حکم جاری کر دیا جائیگا اور کہا جائیگا کہ ٹوٹا ہوا لوٹا قرض کا بدل ہو گیا اور بات ختم ہو گئی۔ -1 کیونکہ اگر مکسور کو بلاک کے درجہ میں نہ لیا جائے تو تین ہی صورتیں ہو سکتی ہیں۔ جودت ختم ہونے کی وجہ سے قرض میں کچھ کمی کر دی جائے اور یہ باطل ہے۔ ( کمامر ) - راہن مرتہن سے انکسار کا مضمان لے لے یہ بھی باطل ہے کیونکہ اس میں ربوا ہے۔ نقصان کو مفت چھوڑ دے اور پورا قرض ادا کر کے ٹوٹا ہوا لوٹا لے لے تو اس میں راہن کا ضرر ہے لہذا جب کوئی صورت نہ بن سکی تو ہمیں مجبوراً کہنا پڑا کہ جب مفت فک رہن محال ہوا یعنی نقصان کا عوض لئے بغیر فک رہن ممکن نہ ہوا تو یہ نقصان بمنزلہ تلف ہو گیا اور تلاف کی صورت میں بالاتفاق ہلاکت دین کے مقابلہ میں ہوتی ہے اسی طرح نکسار کی صورت میں بھی ہونا چاہیے کیونکہ جب راہن پر یہ جبر نہیں کیا جاسکتا کہ وہ ٹوٹا ہوا لوٹا لے تو مجبوراً اس کو مرتہن رکھیگا تو یہ نقص تلف کے درجہ میں ہو گیا اور تلف میں کل قرض ساقط ہوتا ہے لہذا یہاں بھی ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ امام محمد کے استدلال کا جواب قلنا الاستيفاء عند الهلاك بالمالية وطريقه ان يكون مضمونا بالقيمة ثم تقع المقاصة وفي جعله بالدين اغلاق الرهن وهو حكم جاهلى فكان التضمين بالقيمة اولى ترجمہ ہم کہیں گے کہ ہلاکت کے وقت وصولیابی مالیت سے ہوتی ہے اور اس کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ مرہون مضمون بالقیمہ ہوتا ہے پھر مقاصہ واقع ہو جاتا ہے اور مرہون کو قرض کا عوض قرار دینے میں مرہون اقتباس کلی ہے اور یہ زمانہ جاہلیت کا حکم ہے تو قیمت کا ضامن بنانا ہی اولی ہو گا۔ تشریح یہاں سے مصنف امام محمد کے استد خلال کا جواب دے رہے ہیں ۔ کہ جب مرہون ہلاک ہو جاتا ہے تو چونکہ عین تو ختم ہوا تو قرض کی وصولیابی عین سے نہیں ہوگی بلکہ مرہون کی مالیت سے ہوتی ہے کہنے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ہلاکت مرہون کی صورت میں بھی مرہون کا عوض قیمت ہی ہوتی ہے پھر چونکہ قیمت اور قرض ایک سے ہیں اس وجہ سے پھر اجازت ملتی ہے کہ بس مرتہن اس قیمت کو
[Book of Rahn: If he redeems it with the deficiency, because there is harm in it, so we gave him a choice: if he wishes, he redeems it with what is in it (i.e., pays the full debt), and if he wishes, he makes him liable for its value, from its kind or other than its kind, and it remains a pledge with the mortgagee, and the broken piece belongs to the mortgagee by way of liability. Translation: And if the jug broke, then in the first case—and that is when the jug's value equals its weight—according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the pledgor cannot be forced to redeem the pledge because there is no reason for some of the debt to be dropped, since the pledgor would be repaying the debt solely due to quality and craftsmanship (and this is invalid), and there is no reason for the pledgor to redeem it despite the deficiency because there is harm to the pledgor. So we gave him a choice: if he wishes, he redeems it in exchange for the debt (i.e., bearing the loss and paying the full debt to the mortgagee), and if he wishes, he makes the mortgagee liable for its value, whether from its kind or other than its kind, and the value remains a pledge with the mortgagee, and the broken jug becomes the property of the mortgagee due to the liability. Explanation: What is a mortgaged jug? It broke instead of being destroyed in the possession of the mortgagee, e.g., its spout broke and it became defective. What is the ruling? -1 It is stated that if the weight and value of the jug are equal, there is a difference between the two shaykhs and Imam Muhammad. The two shaykhs say that the pledgor has a choice: he bears the loss and pays the full debt to the mortgagee and takes back his jug in its current condition, or he makes the mortgagee liable for the value (ten dirhams) and the value takes the place of the pledge; then when the pledgor pays the debt, he will take back the substitute value from the mortgagee. The liability for the value may be paid in dirhams or dinars; both are permissible. This is the madhhab of the two shaykhs. Therefore, according to the two shaykhs, the pledgor cannot be forced to redeem because there are only two possibilities and both are invalid. Since both possibilities are invalid, we gave the pledgor this choice. The two invalid possibilities were: (1) the pledgor takes the broken jug and three dirhams are reduced from the mortgagee's ten dirhams due to the breakage, because the weight of the jug remains perfect, so reducing three dirhams would be due to the craftsmanship of the jug, meaning the pledgor paid three dirhams of the debt due to craftsmanship (this is invalid). (2) The pledgor bears the loss and pays the full debt and takes back the defective jug; clearly this causes open harm to the pledgor, as he had deposited a good jug and receives a broken one. Therefore, since these two possibilities are invalid, we selected the option. Imam Muhammad's viewpoint: According to Muhammad, if he wishes, he redeems it deficiently, and if he wishes, he makes it a substitute for the debt, analogizing the state of breakage to the state of destruction. This is because when redeeming it for free became impossible, breakage became akin to destruction, and in actual destruction, the pledge is liable for the debt by consensus, so too in what is analogous to it. Translation: According to Muhammad, if he wishes, he redeems it with the deficiency, and if he wishes, he makes it a substitute for the debt, drawing an analogy between the state of breakage and the state of destruction. This is because when free redemption became problematic, breakage reached the level of destruction. And in the case of actual destruction, by consensus, the pledge is liable for the debt, so similarly in this case which is at the level of destruction. Explanation: This is Imam Muhammad's madhhab: the pledgor has two options in the mentioned case. (1) The same as what the two shaykhs said: he bears the loss and pays the full debt to the mortgagee and takes back the broken jug. (2) The pledgor has the option to make the broken jug a substitute for the debt, i.e., as if the pledgor has repaid the debt. In summary, Imam Muhammad applied the ruling of destruction to breakage. If the jug had been destroyed, the ruling would be that the mortgagee's debt drops, and breakage is akin to destruction. Therefore, whatever has reached the level of destruction, the ruling of destruction is applied, and it is said that the broken jug has become a substitute for the debt, and the matter is closed. -1 Because if the broken piece is not considered at the level of total loss, then there are only three possibilities: (1) reduce the debt due to loss of craftsmanship—this is invalid (as mentioned). (2) The pledgor takes compensation from the mortgagee for the breakage—this is also invalid because it involves riba. (3) The pledgor forgives the loss and pays the full debt and takes the broken jug—this involves harm to the pledgor. Therefore, when no valid possibility remained, we were forced to say that when free redemption of the pledge became impossible (i.e., redemption without compensation for the loss became impossible), this loss became like destruction, and in the case of destruction, by agreement, the loss is in exchange for the debt, so likewise in the case of breakage. Because when the pledgor cannot be forced to take the broken jug, he is compelled to leave it with the mortgagee, so this loss reaches the level of destruction, and in destruction the entire debt drops, so here too it drops. Answer to Imam Muhammad's reasoning: We say: Recovery at the time of destruction is through monetary value, and its method is that it is liable for value, then offset occurs. However, making it a substitute for the debt is a forfeiting of the pledge, which is a pre-Islamic ruling, so making liable for value is more appropriate. Translation: We say that at the time of destruction, recovery is through monetary value, and its method is that the pledge is liable for value, then offset occurs. And making it a substitute for the debt is a complete forfeiture of the pledge, which is a pre-Islamic ruling, so making liable for value is more appropriate. Explanation: From here, the author is responding to Imam Muhammad's reasoning. When the pledge is destroyed, since the specific item is gone, the debt is not recovered from the item but from its monetary value. The meaning is that even in the case of destruction of the pledge, the substitute for the pledge is its value. Then since the value and the debt are the same, permission arises that the mortgagee simply takes this value.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling when a mortgaged item (specifically a jug/lota) breaks partially (e.g., its spout breaks) while in the custody of the mortgagee. The issue arises when the item's weight remains intact but its craftsmanship/value decreases. The passage presents the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the shaykhayn) and then the position of Imam Muhammad, followed by a rebuttal to Muhammad's view. According to the shaykhayn, the rahin (pledgor) cannot be forced to redeem the broken item automatically. Instead, he is given a choice: either he bears the loss and redeems the item by paying the full debt, or he demands that the murtahin (mortgagee) compensate him for the value of the item (which then becomes the new pledge). This is because forcing him to either accept a reduction in debt (which would be invalid as it cancels debt without consideration) or to redeem at a loss (which harms him) are both impermissible. Imam Muhammad, by contrast, analogizes breakage to total destruction. Since free redemption became impossible, breakage reaches the level of destruction, and in destruction, by consensus, the pledge becomes a substitute for the debt (i.e., the debt drops). Therefore, Muhammad gives the rahin the option to either redeem with deficiency or to make the broken item full payment for the debt. The author (commentator of Ashraf al-Hidaya) then responds to Muhammad's reasoning, arguing that even in destruction, recovery is through value, not through forfeiture of the specific item. Making the item a substitute for the debt (ighlaq al-rahn) is a pre-Islamic practice and is disapproved. Therefore, the view of the shaykhayn—making the mortgagee liable for the value—is more appropriate. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, as the author explicitly favors it.

Key Terms
انكسار (inkisar): Partial breakage or damage to a mortgaged item that does not render it completely destroyed, e.g., a broken spout.
اغلاق الرهن (ighlaq al-rahn): The practice of the mortgagee keeping the pledged item as full satisfaction of the debt without recourse to its value, which the author calls a pre-Islamic (jahili) practice.
مكسور (maksur): The broken or damaged piece of the mortgaged item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, what options does the rahin have when a mortgaged item is partially broken (e.g., a jug's spout breaks) and its weight equals its original value?
A) He must redeem the item by paying the full debt, bearing the loss.
B) He can either redeem the item by paying the full debt or demand that the mortgagee compensate him for the item's value.
C) He can automatically deduct the loss from the debt.
D) He must forfeit the item to the mortgagee as full payment.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, partial breakage does not automatically forfeit the item; the rahin has a choice between redeeming at full debt or claiming the item's value.

Third Scenario of Broken Pawn: Value Less Than Weight
Ruling on broken pawn when value is less than weight

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a pawn breaks and its value is less than its weight, and explain the legal reasoning of the three Hanafi imams.

Core Idea
When a pawn's value is less than its weight, mortgagee guarantees value, which becomes the new pawn, by consensus.

We now examine the third scenario of a broken pawn (rahn) where the market value of the pawn is less than its weight. All three Hanafi imams – Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani – agree on the ruling, though their reasoning differs. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the underlying qiyas, and the careful conditions to avoid riba when paying the guaranteed value.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The pawn (marhun) is broken while in the mortgagee's custody without negligence, and its market value (e.g., 8 dirhams) is less than its weight (e.g., 10 dirhams). The debt remains (e.g., 10 dirhams).
This is the 'third aspect' (wajh thalith) referenced in the text.
2
State the agreed ruling
The mortgagee (murtahin) must guarantee (damān) the market value of the pawn (8 dirhams). That guaranteed amount becomes a new pawn in place of the original.
The value is paid either as good quality from a different type (e.g., gold dinars) or inferior quality from the same type (e.g., impure silver) to avoid riba.
3
Analyze the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
They extend the ruling from the first scenario (value equals weight) a fortiori (a min al-awla). In the first scenario they already held that the mortgagee guarantees the value; here, since the value is less, the guarantee is even more necessary because the pawn cannot cover the debt by weight.
Their principle: the mortgagee is liable for the market value in all cases of breakage.
4
Analyze Imam Muhammad's reasoning
Imam Muhammad analogizes breakage (inkisar) to complete destruction (halak). In his view, destruction of a pawn that is less valuable than its weight is compensated by value (damān al-qīmah), not by the debt amount. Because the pawn cannot be considered a substitute for the debt at its weight without causing loss to the pawner.
He treats breakage as equivalent to destruction for liability purposes, but since the value is lower, the liability is for value, not debt.
5
Identify the payment conditions to avoid riba
To avoid riba, the guaranteed amount must be paid in a form that prevents inequality. If paid from the same type (silver), it must be inferior quality than the original pawn. If paid from a different type (e.g., gold), it can be of good quality.
This detail is clarified by Sahib al-Hidayah and echoes caution from al-Bada'i.

وفي الوجه الثالث وهو ما اذا كانت قيمته اقل من وزنه ثمانية يضمن قيمته جيدا من خلاف جنسه او رديا من جنسه وتكون رهنا عنده ولهذا بالاتفاق اما عندهما فظاهر و کذالک عند محمد لانه يعتبر حالة الانكسار بحالة الهلاك والهلاك عنده بالقيمة ... تشریح اگر لوٹے کی قیمت آٹھ درہم ہو اور باقی تفصیلات بحالہ ہوں تو کیا حکم ہے؟ تو فرمایا کہ بالا تفاق مرتہن کو لوٹے کی قیمت یعنی آٹھ درہم کا ضامن بنایا جائے گا اور اس قیمت کو مرہون کی جگہ رکھ دیا جائیگا شیخین کے نزدیک تو یہ بات ظاہر ہے کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک پہلی صورت میں بھی قیمت کا ضمان آیا تھا لہذا یہاں بھی بدرجہ اولی آئے گا۔ البتہ اما محمد کا اتفاق کچھ پھل تأمل ہے کیونکہ انہوں نے پہلی مثال میں مرہون کو مضمون بالدین قرار دیا ہے اور یہاں مضمون بالقیمتہ کہتے نہیں کیوں؟ کیونکہ امام محمد نے انکسار کو ہلاکت پر محمول کیا ہے اور ان کے نزدیک اگر پہلی صورت میں ہلاکت ہو تو مرہون مضمون بالدین ہوتا ہے اور اگر قیمت وزن سے کم ہونے کی صورت میں ہلاکت ہو تو پھر مرہون مضمون بالقیمہ ہوتا ہے اور یہاں قیمت کم ہے اس لئے انہوں نے بھی شیخین کے قول سے اتفاق کیا ہے۔ کیونکہ امام محمد مر ہون کو دین کے بدلہ اسی وقت شمار کرتے ہیں جبکہ اس کا امکان ہو اور یہاں اس کا امکان نہیں ہے کیونکہ اگر مرہون کو وزن کے اعتبار سے دین کا بدل قرار دیں گے تو مرہون کا ضر ر لازم آئے گا کیونکہ رہن کی قیمت آٹھ دراہم اور اس کا قرض دس در اہم ہیں اور اگر قیمت کا اعتبار کیا جائے تو یہ ر ہوا ہو گا کما ہو ظاہر دلہذا ضمان قیمت کے علاوہ کوئی چارہ کار نہ نکلا ہکذافی البدائع ص ۱۶۲ ج 4 تنبیہ وجہ ثالث کو ثانی پراس لئے مقدم آیا کہ ثانی میں تفصیل کچھ زیادہ ہے۔ تنبیہ - ۲ شما دیۂ اقل سے بدل ہے اس لئے اس مفہوم کو ادا کرنے کے لئے بدائع کی عبارت ایسے بنے بان كانت ثمانية۔ تنبیہ - بدائع میں کہا ہے کہ اس صورت میں قیمت کا نعمان خلاف جنس سے ہو گا مگر صاحب ہدایہ نے یوں بیان فرمایا ہے کہ اس جنس کے ہوں یا دوسری جنس کے دونوں جائز ہیں بس اس کا خیال رہے کہ سود کا شائبہ نہ ہونے پائے لہذا اگر درہم کے بجائے قیمت میں دینار رکھے تو عمدہ دینا ر ر کھنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں کیونکہ اختلاف جنس کی وجہ سے جودت مردائت کی وجہ سے کوئی خلل نہ ہوگا اور ربوالا زم نہ آئیگا۔ البتہ جب قیمت دراہم سے ہوتو وہ چاندی کھوئی ہونی چاہئے مرہون کے مثل تا کہ ربوا کا لزوم نہ ہو۔ بہر حال چونکہ احتیاط اول میں تھی اس لئے بدائع میں صرف اسی کا ذکر کیا گیا ہے اور گنجائش اس کی بھی ہے لہذا مصنف نے دونوں کو بیان کر دیا ہے۔ خلاصہ کلام خلاف جنس سے کھرا بال رکھنے کا حکم بطریق جواز ہے ورنہ اس کے عکس میں بھی کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے اور اتحاد جنس کی صورت میں کھوئے مال کا حکم بطریق وجوب ہے تا کہ سود نہ ہو جائے شروح ہدا یہ میں اس کو واضح نہیں کیا گیا اس لئے اصول کو سامنے رکھ کر جو بات سمجھ میں آئی وہ میں نے عرض کر دی ہے واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔
And in the third aspect, and it is when its value is less than its weight, eight (dirhams), he guarantees its value, good from a different type or inferior from its type, and it becomes a pawn with him. And this is by agreement. As for with the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is apparent, and likewise with Muhammad, because he considers the state of breakage as the state of destruction, and destruction with him is by value.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage discusses the third scenario of a broken pawn (marhun) where the value of the pawn is less than its weight. For example, the vessel weighs 10 dirhams but its market value is only 8 dirhams. The ruling, by agreement of all three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani), is that the mortgagee (murtahin) becomes guarantor for the full value (8 dirhams). He must pay this amount in a form that avoids riba: either good quality from a different type (e.g., gold dinars instead of silver) or inferior quality from the same type (e.g., impure silver). This amount becomes a new pawn in place of the original. The reasoning: the two shaykhs extend their principle from the first scenario (where value equals weight) a fortiori. Imam Muhammad analogizes breakage to complete destruction (halak). In his view, when value is less than weight, destruction is compensated by value (not by debt) because the pawn cannot cover the debt by weight without causing loss to the pawner. Thus, he agrees with the shaykhs. The commentary also notes a subtlety: when paying from the same type, the silver must be inferior to avoid riba; when from a different type, quality can be good. The author (Sahib al-Hidayah) allows both, while al-Bada'i mentions only the different type for caution. The discussion confirms that the mortgagee does not automatically own the pawn; he must pay its value.

Key Terms
مرهون (marhun): The pawned item itself; in this case, the vessel (lota) that was deposited as collateral.
ضمان (daman): Liability or guarantee; the mortgagee becomes responsible for the value of the pawn due to its breakage.
انكسار (inkisar): Breakage of the pawn while in the custody of the mortgagee, not due to his negligence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the third scenario of the broken pawn, what is the value that the mortgagee must guarantee?
A) The weight of the pawn in dirhams
B) The full market value of the pawn, even if it exceeds the weight
C) The market value of the pawn (8 dirhams in the example), paid from different type or inferior same type
D) The amount of the debt (10 dirhams)

Key Takeaway
When a pawn breaks and its value is less than its weight, the mortgagee must guarantee the market value, which becomes the new pawn, by consensus of the Hanafi imams, paid in a manner that avoids riba.
